Article I. Tax Exemption for Certain Multi-Family Housing
Sec. 4-1.   Title.
   This Article shall be known and cited as the City of Fremont “Multi-Family
Housing Tax Exemption” Article. (O-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-2.   Preamble.
   It is acknowledged that it is a proper public purpose of the State of
Michigan and its political subdivisions to provide housing for its citizens of
low income and to encourage the development of such housing by providing for a
service charge in lieu of property taxes in accordance with the State Housing
Development Authority Act of 1966 (Public Act 346 of 1966, as amended, being
Michigan Compiled Laws Section 125.1401 et seq.). The City is authorized by
this Act to establish or change the service charge to be paid in lieu of taxes
by any or all classes of housing exempt from taxation under this Act at any
amount it chooses not to exceed the taxes that would be paid but for this Act.
It is further acknowledged that such housing for persons of low income is a
public necessity, and as the City will be benefited and improved by such
housing, the encouragement of the same by providing certain real estate tax
exemption for such housing is a valid public purpose; further, that the
continuation of the provisions of this Article for tax exemption and the
service charge in lieu of taxes during the period contemplated in this Article
are essential to the determination of economic feasibility of housing
developments which are constructed and financed in reliance on such tax
exemption.
   The City acknowledges that the Newaygo County Community Services (NCCS)
Center for Nonprofit Housing (CNH) in its own behalf and on behalf of a limited
dividend housing association limited partnership to be formed (the “Sponsor”)
has offered, subject to receipt of an allocation under the low income housing
tax credit (LIHTC) and a mortgage loan, to erect, own, and operate a housing
development identified as the Fremont Apartments Development on certain
property located on an approximately 4.2-acre site in the City to serve persons
of low income, and that the Sponsor has offered to pay the City on account of
this housing development an annual service charge for public services in lieu
of taxes. (O-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-3   Definitions.
   All terms not herein defined shall have the meanings given them in the State
Housing Development Authority Act of 1966, being Public Act 346 of 1966, of the
State of Michigan, as amended.
   “Act” means the State Housing Development Authority Act, being Michigan
Public Act 346 of 1966, as amended.
   “Annual Shelter Rent” means the total collections during an agreed annual
period from all occupants of a housing development representing rent or
occupancy charges, exclusive of charges for gas, electricity, heat or other
utilities furnished to the occupants.
   “Authority” means the Michigan State Housing Development Authority (MSHDA).
   “Housing Development” means a development that contains a significant
element of housing for persons of low income and such elements of other
housing, commercial, recreational, industrial, communal and educational
facilities as the Authority determines improve the quality of the development
as it relates to housing for persons of low income.
   “Mortgage Loan” means a loan to be made by the Authority to the Sponsor for
the construction and/or permanent financing of the housing development.
   “Sponsor” means person(s) or entities that have applied to the Authority for
a mortgage loan or for an allocation under the low income housing tax credit
program to finance a housing development.
   “Utilities” mean fuel, water, sanitary sewer service, and/or electrical
service that are paid by the housing development. (Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-4.   Class of Housing Development.
   It is determined that the class of housing developments to which the tax
exemption shall apply and for which a service charge shall be paid in lieu of
such taxes shall be housing developments that are financed or assisted pursuant
to the Act. It is further determined that the Fremont Apartments Development is
of this class. (Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-5.   Establishment of Annual Service Charge.
   The housing development known as the Fremont Apartments Development and the
property on which it shall be constructed (Property Identification Number 62-
13-34-400-061; common address of 1218 W. State Street) shall be exempt from all
property taxes from and after the commencement of construction. The City,
acknowledging that the Sponsor and the Authority have established the economic
feasibility of the housing development in reliance upon the enactment and
continuing effect of this Article and the qualification of the housing
development for the exemption from all property taxes and a payment in lieu of
taxes as established in this Article, and in consideration of the Sponsor's
offer, subject to receipt of a mortgage loan and an allocation under the LIHTC
program, to construct, own and operate the Housing Development, agrees to
accept payment of an annual service charge for public services in lieu of all
property taxes. The annual service charge shall be equal topercent (%) of the
difference between the annual shelter rents actually collected and utilities.
(Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-6.   Limitation on the Payment of the Annual Service Charge.
   Notwithstanding Section 4-5, the service charge to be paid each year in lieu
of taxes for the part of the housing development which is tax exempt and which
is occupied by other than low income persons or families shall be equal to the
full amount of the taxes which shall be paid on that portion of the housing
development if the housing development were not tax exempt. The term “low
income persons or families” as used herein shall be the same meaning found in
Section 15(a)(7) of the Act. (Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-7.   Contractual Effect of this Article.
   Notwithstanding the provisions of Section 15(a)(5) of the Act to the
contrary, a contract between the City and the Sponsor, with the Authority as
third party beneficiary under the contract, to provide tax exemption and accept
payments in lieu of taxes, as previously described, is effectuated by enactment
of this Article. (Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-8.   Payment of Service Charge.
   The service charge in lieu of taxes as determined under this Article shall
be payable in the same manner as general property taxes are payable to the City
except that the annual payment shall be paid on or before August 10th of each
year. (Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-9.   Duration.
   This Article shall remain in effect and shall not terminate so long as the
Authority’s mortgage loan remains outstanding and unpaid or the Authority has
any interest in the property; or the housing development remains subject to
income and rent restrictions pursuant to Section 42 of the Internal Revenue
Code of 1986, as amended, provided that construction of the housing development
commence within one year from the effective date of this Article. (Ord. 0-04-
03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-10.   Severability.
   The various sections and provisions of this Article shall be deemed to be
severable and should any section or provision of this Article be declared by
any court of competent jurisdiction to be unconstitutional or invalid, the same
shall not affect the validity of the Article as a whole or any section or
provision of this Article other than the section or provision so declared to be
unconstitutional or invalid. (Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Sec. 4-11.   Effective Date.
   This Article shall take effect ten (10) days after publication thereof.
(Ord. 0-04-03, 12-20-04)
Article II. Tax Exemption for Certain Multi-Family Housing Serving Low Income
Seniors
Sec. 4-12.   Title.
   This Article shall be known and cited as the City of Fremont "Senior Citizen
Multi-Family Housing Tax Exemption" Article. (Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-13.   Preamble.
   It is acknowledged that it is a proper public purpose of the State of
Michigan and its political subdivisions to provide housing for its senior
citizens of low income and to encourage the development of such housing by
providing for a service charge in lieu of property taxes in accordance with the
Michigan State Housing Development Authority (MSHDA) Act of 1966 (1966 PA 346,
as amended, MCLA Section 125.1401 et seq.). The City is authorized by this Act
to establish or change the service charge to be paid in lieu of ad valorem
property taxes by any or all classes of housing exempt from taxation under this
Act at any amount it chooses, not to exceed the taxes that would be paid but
for this Act. It is further acknowledged that such housing for senior persons
of low income is a public necessity, and because the City will be benefited and
improved by such housing, the encouragement of the same by providing certain
real estate tax exemption for such housing is a valid public purpose; further,
that the provisions of this Article for tax exemption and the service charge in
lieu of taxes during the period contemplated in this Article are essential to
the determination of economic feasibility of housing developments that are
constructed, renovated and/or financed in reliance on such tax exemption.
   The City acknowledges that the Newaygo County Community Services (NCCS)
Center for Nonprofit Housing (CNH) has, on its own behalf, created a new
ownership entity named the "Senior Wedgewood Limited Dividend Housing
Association Limited Partnership" also known as the "Senior Wedgewood LDHA-LP"
for short (hereinafter the "Sponsor"). The Sponsor has offered, subject to
receipt of an allocation under the federal Low Income Housing Tax Credit
(LIHTC) program and a Mortgage Loan from USDA Rural Development to renovate,
own and operate a housing development identified as the Senior Wedgewood
Apartment Development (20 units) on certain property located at 216 Meadow
Hills Lane in the City to serve senior citizens of low income. CNH shall be the
General Partner and the LIHTC investors represented by the syndicator, Great
Lakes Capital Fund for Housing Limited Partnership, shall be the Limited
Partners. The Sponsor has offered to pay the City on account of this housing
development an annual service charge for public services in lieu of property
taxes. (Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-14.   Definitions.
   All terms not herein defined shall have the meanings given them in the State
Housing Development Authority Act of 1966, being Public Act 346 of 1966, of the
State of Michigan, as amended.
   "Act" means the State Housing Development Authority Act, being Michigan
Public Act 346 of 1966, as amended.
   "Annual Shelter Rent" means the total collections during an agreed annual
period from all occupants of a housing development representing rent or
occupancy charges, exclusive of charges for utilities as defined in this
Section, which are furnished to and used by the occupants.
   "Authority" means the Michigan State Housing Development Authority (MSHDA).
   "Commitment for Low Income Housing Tax Credits (LIHTC's)" means the
commitment for the tax credits allocated by the Authority to the sponsor under
provisions of Section 42(m)(1)(A) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended.
   "Low or Moderate Income Seniors" means seniors who cannot afford to pay the
amounts at which private enterprise, without federally-aided mortgages or loans
from the Authority, is providing a substantial supply of decent, safe and
sanitary housing and who fall within income limitations set in the Act or by
the Authority in its rules.
   "Mortgage Loan" means only the initial loan to be made by the Authority to
the Sponsor for the construction, renovation and/or long-term financing of the
Housing Development.
   "Senior", "Senior Citizen" or "Elderly" mean a single person who is 55 years
of age or older or a household in which at least one member is 55 years of age
or older and all other members are 50 years of age or older.
   "Senior Housing Development" means the senior citizen rental housing
development that contains the 20 units of housing for elderly persons of low
and moderate income and such other elements of housing, commercial,
recreational, communal and educational facilities that the City may
subsequently approve and that the developer determines necessary to maintain
the quality of the development for its stated purpose.
   "Sponsor" means the "Senior Wedgewood Limited Dividend Housing Association
Limited Partnership," also known as the "Senior Wedgewood LDHALP" for short, a
Michigan-limited partnership, which has received a commitment from the
Authority for a LIHTC allocation and a Mortgage Loan from the USDA Rural
Development program.
   "Taxing Jurisdiction" means a municipality, county or district, including a
school district or any special district having the power to levy or collect ad
valorem taxes upon real or personal property or in whose behalf taxes may be
levied or collected.
   "Utilities" mean only those essential for heating/cooling fuel, water,
sanitary sewer service and/or electrical service that are paid by the Housing
Development and used by the senior occupants. The definition of utilities
hereby excludes all other utilities or services including, but not limited to,
video/audio, data, computer, Internet, telephone, television or radio services
received via any electronic, mechanical or other means (cable, satellite or
wireless and all others now or in the future.) (Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-15.   Class of Housing Development.
   It is hereby determined that the class of Housing Developments to which the
tax exemption shall apply and for which a service charge shall be paid in lieu
of such taxes shall be all units in the Senior Wedgewood Housing Development,
owned, renovated, operated and developed by the Sponsor and rented to elderly
or senior persons under provisions of the commitment for low income housing tax
credits and the initial/original Mortgage Loan awarded to the Sponsor by the
Authority.
   It is further determined that the Wedgewood Apartment Development, as
described and acknowledged in Section 4-13, is of this class. (Ord. O-07-04, 9-
17-07)
Sec. 4-16.   Establishment of an Annual Service Charge.
   The Housing Development known as the Senior Wedgewood Apartment Development
and the property on which it shall be renovated (Property Identification Number
62-13-36-455-013; common address of 216 Meadow Hills Lane) shall be exempt from
all ad valorem property taxes from and after the commencement of renovation, as
further limited, however by this Article. Said renovation shall commence within
one year of the effective date of this Article.
   The City of Fremont, acknowledging that the Sponsor and the Authority have
established the economic feasibility of the Senior Housing Development in
reliance upon the enactment and effect of this Article and the qualification of
the Senior Housing Development for the exemption from all property taxes and a
payment in lieu of taxes as established in this Article, and in consideration
of the Sponsor's offer, subject to receipt of the initial Mortgage Loan from
the USDA Rural Development program and an allocation under the LIHTC program,
to renovate, own and operate the Senior Housing Development, agrees to accept
payment of an annual service charge for public services in lieu of all property
taxes.
   The annual service charge shall be equal to ten percent (10%) of the annual
shelter rents, but in no event less than $9,000.00. Beginning in 2010, the
annual service charge shall be the greater of: (1) ten percent (10%) of the
annual shelter rents; or (2) $9,000.00 PLUS a percentage increase equal to the
net percentage increase in the U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics "Chained
Consumer Price Index for All Urban Consumers: U.S. City Average for all Items,
Expenditure Categories and Commodity and Service Groups" (December 1999=100)
(the "C-CPI-U") from the C-CPI-U as published in January 2008 and the C-CPI-
U published in January of the year in which the service charge is due. (Ord. O-
07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-17.   Limitation on the Payment of the Annual Service Charge.
   Notwithstanding Section 4-16, the service charge to be paid each year in
lieu of taxes for the part of the Housing Development that is tax exempt and
which is occupied at any time during each year by other than low income senior
citizens shall be equal to the full amount of the annual property taxes, based
on the total property tax millage rate of all taxing jurisdictions in effect at
the time such occupancy occurs, which would have been paid on that portion of
the Housing Development if the Housing Development were not tax exempt. The
benefits of any tax exemption granted under this Article shall be allocated by
the owner of the Housing Development exclusively to low income senior citizens
in the form of reduced housing charges. The term "low income senior citizens"
as used herein shall be the same meaning found in Section 15(a)(7) of the Act.
(Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-18.   Payment of the Service Charge.
   The annual service charge in lieu of taxes as determined under this Article
shall commence in the calendar year in which initial occupancy of the Senior
Housing Development occurs. The service charge in lieu of taxes shall be
payable in the same manner as general property taxes are payable to the City
except that the annual payment shall be paid on or before August 10th of each
year.
   Should the Sponsor's payment of the annual Service Charge be received by the
City after August 10th of each year it is due, then the City shall apply an
initial four (4) percent penalty to the amount due. The original service
charge, plus the four (4) percent penalty, shall accrue interest at the rate of
one (1) percent per month compounded monthly, beginning from the first day the
payment is delinquent. In addition to the penalty and the accrued interest, the
City may use any legal remedies at its disposal to secure payment of the
service charge, plus any penalty and interest. (Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-19.   Duration.
   This Article shall remain in effect and shall not terminate so long as the
original/initial USDA Rural Development Mortgage Loan remains outstanding and
unpaid or the Housing Development remains subject to income and rent
restrictions pursuant to Section 42 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended. Provided, however that renovation of the Senior Housing Development
commences within one year from the effective date of this Article. Provided
further that the term of this Article shall not exceed thirty (30) years,
regardless of whether the original/initial USDA Rural Development Mortgage Loan
remains outstanding or unpaid or the Senior Housing Development remains subject
to any income or rent restrictions. At the end of the thirty- (30) year term,
the Senior Wedgewood Apartment Development shall no longer be exempt from ad
valorem property taxes and shall be placed on the ad valorem property tax roll
by the City Assessor and City Treasurer at its assessed value at the time the
exemption terminates.
   Any significant change of the Senior Housing Development's original or
initial public or private financing, refinancing, ownership, or other similar
factors shall automatically trigger a review by the City Council of the facts,
conditions, acknowledgments, rates of return and any other aspect of the
Sponsor's and other partners' or entities' participation in the Development. If
the Council's review determines, in its reasonable yet sole determination, that
there were or would be significant changes in the intent, return on investment,
or any other facet of the Development as originally proposed by the Sponsor and
as acknowledged and agreed to in this Article, then the City Council reserves
the right to modify, continue or cancel the tax exemption for the Senior
Wedgewood Housing Development. (Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-20.   Review and Audit of Sponsor's Records.
   The Sponsor shall permit the City, its appointed representatives, advisors
or financial auditing firm(s) to periodically conduct an audit of the annual
financial records of the project to determine the accuracy of the data used and
the calculations made to determine the PILOT amounts. If an audit reveals an
underpayment by the Sponsor of more than ten (10) percent of the PILOT as
calculated and paid by the Sponsor to the City in any one year, then the
Sponsor shall be required to pay the City for the costs of the audit. (Ord. O-
07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-21.   Contractual Effect of this Article.
   Notwithstanding the provisions of Section 15(a)(5) of the Act to the
contrary, a contract between the City and the Sponsor, with the Authority as
third party beneficiary under the contract, to provide tax exemption and accept
payments in lieu of taxes, as previously described, is effectuated by enactment
of this Article. However, the City reserves its rights to pursue other legal
remedies to enforce provisions of this Article. (Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-22.   Severability.
   The various sections and provisions of this Article shall be deemed to be
severable and should any section or provision of this Article be declared by
any court of competent jurisdiction to be unconstitutional or invalid, the same
shall not affect the validity of the Article as a whole or any section or
provision of this Article other than the section or provision so declared to be
unconstitutional or invalid. (Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Sec. 4-23.   Effective Date.
   This Article shall take effect ten (10) days after publication thereof.
(Ord. O-07-04, 9-17-07)
Article III. Tax Exemption for Certain Existing Multi-Family Housing Serving
Low Income Citizens
Sec. 4-24.   Title.
   This Article shall be known and cited as the City of Fremont "Existing
Multi-Family Low Income Housing Tax Exemption" Article. (Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-
07)
Sec. 4-25.   Preamble.
   It is acknowledged that it is a proper public purpose of the State of
Michigan and its political subdivisions to provide housing for its citizens of
low income and to encourage the development of such housing by providing for a
service charge in lieu of property taxes in accordance with the Michigan State
Housing Development Authority (MSHDA) Act of 1966 (1966 PA 346, as amended,
MCLA Section 125.1401 et seq.). The City is authorized by this Act to establish
or change the service charge to be paid in lieu of ad valorem property taxes by
any or all classes of housing exempt from taxation under this Act at any amount
it chooses, not to exceed the taxes that would be paid but for this Act. It is
further acknowledged that such preservation of existing housing for persons of
low income is a public necessity, and because the City will be benefited and
improved by such housing, the encouragement of the same by providing certain
real estate tax exemption for such housing is a valid public purpose; further,
that the provisions of this Article for tax exemption and the service charge in
lieu of taxes during the period contemplated in this Article are essential to
the determination of economic feasibility of housing developments that are
constructed, renovated and/or financed in reliance on such tax exemption.
   The City acknowledges that the Newaygo County Community Services (NCCS)
Center for Nonprofit Housing (CNH) has, on its own behalf, created a new
ownership entity named the "Meadow Hills Limited Dividend Housing Association-
Limited Partnership" also known as the "Meadow Hills LDHA-LP" for short
(hereinafter the "Sponsor"). The Sponsor has offered, subject to receipt of an
allocation under the federal Low Income Housing Tax Credit (LIHTC) program and
both the assumption of an existing and receipt of a supplemental Mortgage Loan
from USDA Rural Development to renovate, own and operate a housing development
identified as the Meadow Hills North Family Apartment Development (48 units) on
certain property located at 106 Meadow Hills Lane in the City of Fremont to
serve citizens of low income. CNH shall be the General Partner and the LIHTC
investors represented by the syndicator, Great Lakes Capital Fund for Housing
Limited Partnership, shall be the Limited Partners. The Sponsor has offered to
pay the City of Fremont on account of this housing development an annual
service charge for public services in lieu of property taxes. (Ord. O-07-06,
11-19-07)
Sec. 4-26.   Definitions.
   All terms not herein defined shall have the meanings given them in the State
Housing Development Authority Act of 1966, being Public Act 346 of 1966, of the
State of Michigan, as amended.
   "Act" means the State Housing Development Authority Act, being Michigan
Public Act 346 of 1966, as amended.
   "Annual Shelter Rent" means the total collections during an agreed annual
period from all occupants of a housing development representing rent or
occupancy charges, exclusive of charges for utilities as defined in this
Section, which are furnished to and used by the occupants.
   "Authority" means the Michigan State Housing Development Authority (MSHDA).
   "Commitment for Low Income Housing Tax Credits (LIHTC's)" means the
commitment for the tax credits allocated by the Authority to the sponsor under
provisions of Section 42(m)(1)(A) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended.
   "Low or Moderate Income Families" means families who cannot afford to pay
the amounts at which private enterprise, without federally-aided mortgages or
loans from the Authority, is providing a substantial supply of decent, safe and
sanitary housing and who fall within income limitations set in the Act or by
the Authority in its rules.
   "Mortgage Loan" means the assumption of the existing mortgage loans and only
the initial supplemental loan to be made by the U.S. Department of Agriculture,
Rural Development Program to the Sponsor for the construction, renovation and/
or long-term financing of the Housing Development.
   "Multi-Family Existing Housing Development" means the rental housing
development that contains the forty-eight (48) units of housing for low and
moderate income families and such other elements of housing, commercial,
recreational, communal and educational facilities that the City may
subsequently approve and that the developer determines necessary to maintain
the quality of the development for its stated purpose.
   "Sponsor" means the "Meadow Hills Limited Dividend Housing Association-
Limited Partnership," also known as the "Meadow Hills LDHA-LP" for short, a
Michigan-limited partnership, which has received a commitment from the
Authority for a LIHTC allocation and both the assumption of existing Mortgage
Loans and the approval for an initial supplemental loan from the USDA Rural
Development program.
   "Taxing Jurisdiction" means a municipality, county or district, including a
school district or any special district having the power to levy or collect ad
valorem taxes upon real or personal property or in whose behalf taxes may be
levied or collected.
   "Utilities" mean only those essential for heating/cooling fuel, water,
sanitary sewer service and/or electrical service that are paid by the Housing
Development and used by the family occupants. The definition of "utilities"
hereby excludes all other utilities or services including, but not limited to,
video/audio, data, computer, Internet, telephone, television or radio services
received via any electronic, mechanical or other means (cable, satellite or
wireless and all others now or in the future.) (Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-27.   Class of Housing Development.
   It is determined that the class of Housing Developments to which the tax
exemption under this Article shall apply and for which a service charge shall
be paid in lieu of such property taxes shall be 48-unit multi-family housing
developments that exist in the City of Fremont at the time of adoption of this
Article that provide housing to families of low income; and which are financed
or assisted pursuant to the Act; and which receive an allocation of federal Low
Income Housing Tax Credits (LIHTC); and which will assume an existing USDA
Rural Development Loan; and which will secure a supplemental USDA Rural
Development Loan; and which will be owned, rehabilitated and managed by a local
(Newaygo County) nonprofit housing center; and which will invest an average of
at least $19,000 per unit ($912,000 total) to renovate and update the Housing
Development.
   It is hereby determined that the class of Housing Developments to which the
tax exemption shall apply and for which a service charge shall be paid in lieu
of such taxes shall be all forty-eight (48) units in the Meadow Hills North
Housing Development, owned, renovated, operated and developed by the Sponsor
and rented to eligible families under provisions of the commitment for low
income housing tax credits and the initial/original Mortgage Loan awarded to
the Sponsor by the USDA Rural Development program.
   It is further determined that the Meadow Hills North Family Apartment
Development, as described and acknowledged in Section 4-25, is of this class.
(Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-28.   Establishment of an Annual Service Charge.
   The Housing Development known as the Meadow Hills North Family Apartment
Development and the property on which it shall be renovated (Property
Identification Number 62-13-36-455-005; common address of 106 Meadow Hills
Lane) shall be exempt from all ad valorem property taxes from and after the
commencement of renovation, as further limited, however by this Article. Said
renovation shall commence within one year of the effective date of this
Article.
   The City of Fremont, acknowledging that the Sponsor and the Authority have
established the economic feasibility of the existing Low Income Family Housing
Development in reliance upon the enactment and effect of this Article and the
qualification of the Low Income Family Housing Development for the exemption
from all property taxes and a payment in lieu of taxes as established in this
Article, and in consideration of the Sponsor's offer, subject to assumption of
the initial Mortgage Loan from the USDA Rural Development program and the
receipt of a supplemental Mortgage Loan from the USDA Rural Development
program, and an allocation under the LIHTC program, to renovate, own and
operate the Low Income Family Housing Development, agrees to accept payment of
an annual service charge for public services in lieu of all property taxes.
   The annual service charge shall be equal to ten (10) percent of the annual
shelter rents, but in no event less than $18,000. Beginning in 2010, the annual
service charge shall be the greater of: (1) ten (10) percent of the annual
shelter rents; or (2) $18,000 PLUS a percentage increase equal to the net
percentage increase in the U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics "Chained Consumer
Price Index for All Urban Consumers: U.S. City Average for all Items,
Expenditure Categories and Commodity and Service Groups" (December 1999=100)
(the "C-CPI-U") from the C-CPI-U as published in January 2008 and the C-CPI-
U published in January of the year in which the service charge is due. (Ord. O-
07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-29.   Limitation on the Payment of the Annual Service Charge.
   Notwithstanding Section 4-28, the service charge to be paid each year in
lieu of taxes for the part of the Housing Development that is tax exempt and
which is occupied at any time during each year by other than low income
families or persons shall be equal to the full amount of the annual property
taxes, based on the total property tax millage rate of all taxing jurisdictions
in effect at the time such occupancy occurs, which would have been paid on that
portion of the Housing Development if the Housing Development were not tax
exempt. The benefits of any tax exemption granted under this Article shall be
allocated by the owner of the Housing Development exclusively to low income
families in the form of reduced housing charges. The term "low income families"
as used herein shall be the same meaning found in Section 15(a)(7) of the Act.
(Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-30.   Payment of the Service Charge.
   The annual service charge in lieu of taxes as determined under this Article
shall commence in the calendar year in which initial occupancy of the Low
Income Family Housing Development owned by the Sponsor occurs. The service
charge in lieu of taxes shall be payable in the same manner as general property
taxes are payable to the City except that the annual payment shall be paid on
or before August 10th of each year.
   Should the Sponsor's payment of the annual Service Charge be received by the
City after August 10th of each year it is due, then the City shall apply an
initial four (4) percent penalty to the amount due. The original service
charge, plus the four (4) percent penalty, shall accrue interest at the rate of
one (1) percent per month compounded monthly, beginning from the first day the
payment is delinquent. In addition to the penalty and the accrued interest, the
City may use any legal remedies at its disposal to secure payment of the
service charge, plus any penalty and interest. ( Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-31.   Duration.
   This Article shall remain in effect and shall not terminate so long as the
assumed USDA Rural Development Mortgage Loan or the initial supplemental USDA
Rural Development Mortgage Loan remains outstanding and unpaid or the Housing
Development remains subject to income and rent restrictions pursuant to Section
42 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended. Provided, however that
renovation of the Low Income Family Housing Development commences within one
year from the effective date of this Article. Provided further that the term of
this Article shall not exceed thirty (30) years, regardless of whether the
assumed or initial supplemental USDA Rural Development Mortgage Loans remain
outstanding or unpaid or the Low Income Family Housing Development remains
subject to any income or rent restrictions. At the end of the thirty- (30) year
term, the Meadow Hills North Low Income Family Apartment Development shall no
longer be exempt from ad valorem property taxes and shall be placed on the ad
valorem property tax roll by the City Assessor and City Treasurer at its
assessed value at the time the exemption terminates.
   Any significant change of the Low Income Family Housing Development's
original or initial public or private financing, refinancing, ownership, or
other similar factors shall automatically trigger a review by the City Council
of the facts, conditions, acknowledgments, rates of return and any other aspect
of the Sponsor's and other partners' or entities' participation in the
Development. If the Council's review determines, in its reasonable yet sole
determination, that there were or would be significant changes in the intent,
return on investment, or any other facet of the Development as originally
proposed by the Sponsor and as acknowledged and agreed to in this Article, then
the City Council reserves the right to modify, continue or cancel the tax
exemption for the Meadow Hills Low Income Family Housing Development. (Ord. O-
07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-32.   Review and Audit of Sponsor's Records.
   The Sponsor shall permit the City, its appointed representatives, advisors
or financial auditing firm(s) to periodically conduct an audit of the annual
financial records of the project to determine the accuracy of the data used and
the calculations made to determine the PILOT amounts. If an audit reveals an
underpayment by the Sponsor of more than ten (10) percent of the PILOT as
calculated and paid by the Sponsor to the City in any one year, then the
Sponsor shall be required to pay the City for the costs of the audit. (Ord. O-
07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-33.   Contractual Effect of this Article.
   Notwithstanding the provisions of Section 15(a)(5) of the Act to the
contrary, a contract between the City and the Sponsor, with the Authority as
third-party beneficiary under the contract, to provide tax exemption and accept
payments in lieu of taxes, as previously described, is effectuated by enactment
of this Article. However, the City reserves its rights to pursue other legal
remedies to enforce provisions of this Article. (Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-34.   Severability.
   The various sections and provisions of this Article shall be deemed to be
severable and should any section or provision of this Article be declared by
any court of competent jurisdiction to be unconstitutional or invalid, the same
shall not affect the validity of the Article as a whole or any section or
provision of this Article other than the section or provision so declared to be
unconstitutional or invalid. (Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-07)
Sec. 4-35.   Effective Date.
   This Article shall take effect ten (10) days after publication thereof.
(Ord. O-07-06, 11-19-07)
Article IV. Tax Exemption for Certain Existing Multi-Family Housing Serving Low
Income Citizens
Sec. 4-36. Title.
   This Article shall be known and cited as the City of Fremont “Existing
Multi-Family Low Income Housing Tax Exemption” Article. (O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-37. Preamble.
   It is acknowledged that it is a proper public purpose of the State of
Michigan and its political subdivisions to provide housing for its citizens of
low income and to encourage the development of such housing by providing for a
service charge in lieu of property taxes in accordance with the Michigan State
Housing Development Authority (MSHDA) Act of 1966 (1966 PA 346, as amended,
MCLA Section 125.1401 et. seq.) The City of Fremont is authorized by this Act
to establish or change the service charge to be paid in lieu of ad valorem
property taxes by any or all classes of housing exempt from taxation under this
Act at any amount it chooses, not to exceed the taxes that would be paid but
for this Act. It is further acknowledged that such the preservation of existing
housing for persons of low income is a public necessity, and because the City
of Fremont will be benefited and improved by such housing, the encouragement of
the same by providing certain real estate tax exemption for such housing is a
valid public purpose; further, that the provisions of this Article for tax
exemption and the service charge in lieu of taxes during the period
contemplated in this Article are essential to the determination of economic
feasibility of housing developments that are constructed, renovated and/or
financed in reliance on such tax exemption.
   The City of Fremont acknowledges that the Werth Investments, LLC has, on its
own behalf, created a new ownership entity named the JPS Fremont Limited
Dividend Housing Association Limited Partnership also known as JPS Fremont for
short (hereinafter the “Sponsor”). The Sponsor has offered, subject to receipt
of an allocation under the federal Low Income Housing Tax Credit (LIHTC)
program and the assumption of an existing Mortgage Loan from USDA Rural
Development to renovate, own and operate housing developments identified as:
   1)   Apple Ridge Family Apartments, 318 Dewitte Ave., Fremont, MI (32 units)
(62-13-34-300-042)
   2)   Greenfield Manor Apartments, 228 Dewitte Ave., Fremont, MI (26 units)
(62-13-34-300-041)
   3)   Oak Creek Village Apartments, 1101 & 1103 W. Main St., Fremont, MI (32
units) (62-13-34-400-037)
   4)   Peachtree Village Apartments, 1100, 1102 & 1104 State St., Fremont, MI
(20 units) (62-13-34-400-036)
in the City of Fremont to serve citizens of low income. Werth Investements, LLC
shall be the General Partner. The Sponsor has offered to pay the City of
Fremont on account of this housing development an annual service charge for
public services in lieu of property taxes. (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-38. Definitions.
   All terms not herein defined shall have the meanings given them in the State
Housing Development Authority Act of 1966, being Public Act 346 of 1966, of the
State of Michigan, as amended.
   (a)   “Act” means the State Housing Development Authority Act, being
Michigan Public Act 346 of 1966, as amended.
   (b)   “Annual Shelter Rent” means the total collections during an agreed
annual period from all occupants of a housing development representing rent or
occupancy charges, exclusive of charges for utilities as defined in Subsection
(j) of this Section, which are furnished to and used by the occupants.
   (c)   “Authority” means the Michigan State Housing Development Authority
(MSHDA).
   (d)   “Commitment for Low Income Housing Tax Credits (LIHTC’s)” means the
commitment for the tax credits allocated by the Authority to the sponsor under
provisions of Section 42(m)(1)(A) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended.
   (e)   “Low or Moderate Income Families” means families who cannot afford to
pay the amounts at which private enterprise, without federally-aided mortgages
or loans from the Authority, is providing a substantial supply of decent, safe
and sanitary housing and who fall within income limitations set in the Act or
by the Authority in its rules.
   (f)   “Mortgage Loan” means the assumption of the existing mortgage loans
made by the U.S. Department of Agriculture, Rural Development Program to the
Sponsor for the construction, renovation and/or long-term financing of the
Housing Development.
   (g)   “Multi-Family Existing Housing Development” means the rental housing
development that contains the 110 units of housing for low and moderate income
families and such other elements of housing, commercial, recreational, communal
and educational facilities that the City may subsequently approve and that the
developer determines necessary to maintain the quality of the development for
its stated purpose.
   (h)   “Rural Development” means the United States Department of Agriculture
– Rural Development through the Rural Rental Housing Program under Section 515
of the Federal Housing Act of 1949, as amended.
   (i)   “Sponsor” means JPS Fremont, a Michigan-limited partnership, which
will apply for a commitment from the Authority for a LIHTC allocation and the
assumption of existing Mortgage Loans from the USDA Rural Development program.
   (j)   “Taxing jurisdiction” means a municipality, county or district,
including a school district or any special district having the power to levy or
collect ad valorem taxes upon real or personal property or in whose behalf
taxes may be levied or collected.
   (k)   “Utilities” mean only those essential for heating/cooling fuel, water,
sanitary sewer service and/or electrical service that are paid by the Housing
Development and used by the family occupants. The definition of “utilities”
hereby excludes all other utilities or services including, but not limited to,
video/audio, data, computer, Internet, telephone, television or radio services
received via any electronic, mechanical or other means (cable, satellite or
wireless and all others now or in the future.) (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-39. Class of Housing Development.
   It is determined that the class of Housing Developments to which the tax
exemption under this Article shall apply and for which a service charge shall
be paid in lieu of such property taxes shall be 110-unit multi-family housing
developments that exist in the City of Fremont at the time of adoption of this
Article that provide housing to families of low income; and which are financed
or assisted pursuant to the Act; and which receive an allocation of federal Low
Income Housing Tax Credits (LIHTC); and which will assume an existing USDA
Rural Development Loan; and which will be owned, rehabilitated and managed by a
the Sponsor or its authorized agent; and which will invest an average of at
least $31,000 per unit ($3,500,000 total) to renovate and update the Housing
Development.
It is hereby determined that the class of Housing Developments to which the tax
exemption shall apply and for which a service charge shall be paid in lieu of
such taxes shall be all 110 units in the Apple Ridge Family, Greenfield Manor,
Oak Creek Village and Peachtree Village Apartments Housing Developments, owned,
renovated, operated and developed by the Sponsor and rented to eligible
families under provisions of the commitment for low income housing tax credits
and the Mortgage Loan transferred to the Sponsor by the USDA Rural Development
program.
   It is further determined that the above listed Apartment Developments, as
described and acknowledged in Section
4-37 “Preamble” of this Article, is of this class. (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-40. Establishment of an Annual Service Charge.
   The Housing Developments described in Section
4-37 “Preamble” to be renovated shall be exempt from all ad valorem property
taxes from and after the commencement of renovation, as further limited,
however by this Article. Said renovation shall commence within one year and be
completed within two years of the effective date of this Article will be
revoked and any and all ad valorem property taxes that were waived shall become
due.
   The City of Fremont, acknowledging that the Sponsor and the Authority have
established the economic feasibility of the existing Low Income Family Housing
Development in reliance upon the enactment and effect of this Article and the
qualification of the Low Income Family Housing Development for the exemption
from all property taxes and a payment in lieu of taxes as established in this
Article, and in consideration of the Sponsor’s offer, subject to assumption of
the initial Mortgage Loan from the USDA Rural Development program and an
allocation under the LIHTC program, to renovate, own and operate the Low Income
Family Housing Development, agrees to accept payment of an annual service
charge for public services in lieu of all property taxes.
   The annual service charge shall be equal to ten percent (10%) of the annual
shelter rents, but in no event less than $31,000. Beginning in 2013, the annual
service charge shall be the greater of: (1) ten percent (10%) of the annual
shelter rents; or (2) $31,000. (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-41. Limitation on the Payment of the Annual Service Charge.
   Notwithstanding Section
4-40, the service charge to be paid each year in lieu of taxes for the part of
the Housing Development that is tax exempt and which is occupied at any time
during each year by other than low income families or persons shall be equal to
the full amount of the annual property taxes, based on the total property tax
millage rate of all taxing jurisdictions in effect at the time such occupancy
occurs, which would have been paid on that portion of the Housing Development
if the Housing Development were not tax exempt. The benefits of any tax
exemption granted under this Article shall be allocated by the owner of the
Housing Development exclusively to low income families in the form of reduced
housing charges. The term “low income families” as used herein shall be the
same meaning found in Section 15(a)(7) of the Act. (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-42. Payment of the Service Charge.
   The annual service charge in lieu of taxes as determined under this Article
shall commence in the calendar year in which initial occupancy of the Low
Income Family Housing Development owned by the Sponsor occurs. The service
charge in lieu of taxes shall be payable in the same manner as general property
taxes are payable to the City of Fremont except that the annual payment shall
be paid on or before August 10th of each year.
   Should the Sponsor’s payment of the annual Service Charge be received by the
City after August 10th of each year it is due, then the City shall apply an
initial four percent (4%) penalty to the amount due. The original service
charge, plus the 4% penalty, shall accrue interest at the rate of 1% per month
compounded monthly, beginning from the first day the payment is delinquent. In
addition to the penalty and the accrued interest, the City may use any legal
remedies at its disposal to secure payment of the service charge, plus any
penalty and interest. (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-43. Duration.
   This Article shall remain in effect and shall not terminate so long as the
assumed USDA Rural Development Mortgage Loan remains outstanding and unpaid or
the Housing Development remains subject to income and rent restrictions
pursuant to Section 42 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended.
Provided, however that renovation of the Low Income Family Housing Development
commences within one year and is completed within two years from the effective
date of this Article.
Provided further that the term of this Article shall not exceed thirty (30)
years, regardless of whether the assumed USDA Rural Development Mortgage Loans
remain outstanding or unpaid or the Low Income Family Housing Development
remains subject to any income or rent restrictions. At the end of the thirty-
(30-) year, or earlier term, the aforementioned Apartment Developments shall no
longer be exempt from ad valorem property taxes and shall be placed on the ad
valorem property tax roll by the City Assessor and City Treasurer at its
assessed value at the time the exemption terminates. Any significant change of
the Low Income Family Housing Development’s original or initial public or
private financing, refinancing, ownership, or other similar factors shall
automatically trigger a review by the Fremont City Council of the facts,
conditions, acknowledgments, rates of return and any other aspect of the
Sponsor’s and other partners’ or entities’ participation in the Development. If
the Council’s review determines, in its reasonable yet sole determination, that
there were or would be significant changes in the intent, return on investment,
or any other facet of the Development as originally proposed by the Sponsor and
as acknowledged and agreed to in this Article, then the City Council reserves
the right to modify, continue or cancel the tax exemption for the
aforementioned Housing Development. (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-44. Review and Audit of Sponsor's Records.
   The Sponsor shall permit the City, its appointed representatives, advisors
or financial auditing firm(s) to periodically conduct an audit of the annual
financial records of the project to determine the accuracy of the data used and
the calculations made to determine the PILOT amounts. If an audit reveals an
underpayment by the Sponsor of more than ten percent (10%) of the PILOT as
calculated and paid by the Sponsor to the City in any one year, then the
Sponsor shall be required to pay the City for the costs of the audit. (Ord. O-
11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-45. Contractual Effect of this Article.
   Notwithstanding the provisions of Section 15(a)(5) of the Act to the
contrary, a contract between the City of Fremont and the Sponsor, with the
Authority as third-party beneficiary under the contract, to provide tax
exemption and accept payments in lieu of taxes, as previously described, is
effectuated by enactment of this Article. However, the City reserves its rights
to pursue other legal remedies to enforce provisions of this Article. (Ord. O-
11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-46. Severability.
   The various sections and provisions of this Article shall be deemed to be
severable and should any section or provision of this Article be declared by
any court of competent jurisdiction to be unconstitutional or invalid, the same
shall not affect the validity of the Article as a whole or any section or
provision of this Article other than the section or provision so declared to be
unconstitutional or invalid. (Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Sec. 4-47. Effective Date.
   This Article shall take effect ten (10) days after publication thereof.
(Ord. O-11-06, 7-18-11)
Article V. Tax Exemption for Certain Multi-Family Housing Serving Low Income
Seniors
Sec. 4-48. Title.
   This Article shall be known and cited as the City of Fremont "New Low Income
Senior Housing Tax Exemption" Article. (Ord. O-12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-49. Preamble.
   It is acknowledged that it is a proper public purpose of the State of
Michigan and its political subdivisions to provide housing for its citizens of
low income and to encourage the development of such housing by providing for a
service charge in lieu of property taxes in accordance with the Michigan State
Housing Development Authority (MSHDA) Act of 1966 (1966 PA 346, as amended,
MCLA Section 125.1401 et. seq.) The City of Fremont is authorized by this Act
to establish or change the service charge to be paid in lieu of ad valorem
property taxes by any or all classes of housing exempt from taxation under this
Act at any amount it chooses, not to exceed the taxes that would be paid but
for this Act. It is further acknowledged that such the preservation of existing
housing for persons of low income is a public necessity, and because the City
of Fremont will be benefited and improved by such housing, the encouragement of
the same by providing certain real estate tax exemption for such housing is a
valid public purpose; further, that the provisions of this Article for tax
exemption and the service charge in lieu of taxes during the period
contemplated in this Article are essential to the determination of economic
feasibility of housing developments that are constructed, renovated and/or
financed in reliance on such tax exemption.
   The City of Fremont acknowledges that Home Renewal Systems, LLC has, on its
own behalf, created a new ownership entity named The Fremont Gateway Limited
Dividend Housing Association Limited Partnership also known as Fremont Gateway
for short (hereinafter the "Sponsor"). The Sponsor has offered, subject to
receipt of an allocation under the federal Low Income Housing Tax Credit
(LIHTC) program and securing appropriate financing to renovate, own and operate
housing developments identified as portions of:
   1)   The former Fremont High School Building, 204 E. Main Street, Fremont,
MI (62-17-02-230-006) in the City of Fremont to serve senor citizens of low
income. Home Renewal Systems, LLC shall be the General Partner. The Sponsor has
offered to pay the City of Fremont on account of this housing development an
annual service charge for public services in lieu of property taxes. (Ord. O-
12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-50. Definitions.
   All terms not herein defined shall have the meanings given them in the State
Housing Development Authority Act of 1966, being Public Act 346 of 1966, of the
State of Michigan, as amended.
   (a)   "Act" means the State Housing Development Authority Act, being
Michigan Public Act 346 of 1966, as amended.
   (b)   "Annual Shelter Rent" means the total collections during an agreed
annual period from all occupants of a housing development representing rent or
occupancy charges, exclusive of charges for utilities as defined in Subsection
(j) of this Section, which are furnished to and used by the occupants.
   (c)   "Authority" means the Michigan State Housing Development Authority
(MSHDA).
   (d)   "Commitment for low income housing tax credits (LIHTC's)" means the
commitment for the tax credits allocated by the Authority to the sponsor under
provisions of Section 42(m)(1)(A) of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as
amended.
   (e)   "Housing Development" means the rental housing development that
contains 38 units of houses, of which 30 units will be for low and moderate
income seniors and such other elements of housing, recreational and communal
facilities that the City may subsequently approve and that the developer
determines necessary to maintain the quality of the development for its stated
purpose. This Housing Development will be contained within the circa 1927
portion of the former Fremont High School.
   (f)   "Low or moderate income families" means families who cannot afford to
pay the amounts at which private enterprise, without federally-aided mortgages
or loans from the Authority, is providing a substantial supply of decent, safe
and sanitary housing and who fall within income limitations set in the Act or
by the Authority in its rules.
   (g)   "Rural Development" means the United States Department of Agriculture
- Rural Development through the Rural Rental Housing Program under Section 515
of the Federal Housing Act of 1949, as amended.
   (h)   "Sponsor" means Fremont Gateway, a Michigan-limited partnership, which
will apply for a commitment from the Authority for an LIHTC allocation and
apply for all financing required for the project.
   (i)   "Taxing jurisdiction" means a municipality, county or district,
including a school district or any special district having the power to levy or
collect ad valorem taxes upon real or personal property or on whose behalf
taxes may be levied or collected.
   (j)   "Utilities" mean only those essential for heating/cooling fuel, water,
sanitary sewer service and/or electrical service that are paid by the Housing
Development and used by the family occupants. The definition of "utilities"
hereby excludes all other utilities or services including, but not limited to,
video/audio, data, computer, Internet, telephone, television or radio services
received via any electronic, mechanical or other means (cable, satellite or
wireless and all others now or in the future). (Ord. O-12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-51. Class of Housing Development.
   It is determined that the class of Housing Developments to which the tax
exemption under this Article shall apply and for which a service charge shall
be paid in lieu of such property taxes shall be a 38-unit senior housing
developments in the City of Fremont at the time of adoption of this Article
that will provide housing to seniors of low income; and which are financed or
assisted pursuant to the Act; and which receive an allocation of federal Low
Income Housing Tax Credits (LIHTC); and which will be owned, rehabilitated and
managed by the Sponsor or its authorized agent; and which will invest an
average of at least $29,000 per unit ($1,102,000 total) to renovate and
adaptively reuse the former high school into a Housing Development.
   It is further determined that the above listed Housing Development, as
described and acknowledged in Section
4-49 "Preamble" of this Article, is of this class. (Ord. O-12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-52. Establishment of an Annual Service Charge.
   The Housing Development described in Section
4-49 "Preamble" to be created shall be exempt from all ad valorem property
taxes from and after the commencement of renovation, as further limited,
however by this Article. Said renovation shall commence within two years and be
completed within three years of the effective date of this Article or this
Article will be revoked and any and all ad valorem property taxes that were
waived shall become due.
   The City of Fremont, acknowledging that the Sponsor and the Authority have
established the economic feasibility of the existing Low Income Senior Housing
Development in reliance upon the enactment and effect of this Article and the
qualification of the Low Income Senior Housing Development for the exemption
from all property taxes and a payment in lieu of taxes as established in this
Article, and in consideration of the Sponsor's offer, subject securing all
necessary financing and an allocation under the LIHTC program, to renovate, own
and operate the Senior Housing Development, agrees to accept payment of an
annual service charge for public services in lieu of all property taxes.
   The annual service charge shall be equal to ten percent (10%) of the total
annual shelter rents, but in no event less than $21,000. Beginning in 2013, the
annual service charge shall be the greater of: (1) ten percent (10%) of the
annual shelter rents; or (2) $21,000. (Ord. O-12-04, 7-16-12; Ord. O-14-02, 5-
19-14)
Sec. 4-53. Reserved.
Sec. 4-54. Payment of the Service Charge.
   The annual service charge in lieu of taxes as determined under this Article
shall commence in the calendar year in which initial occupancy of the Senior
Housing Development owned by the Sponsor occurs. The service charge in lieu of
taxes shall be payable in the same manner as general property taxes are payable
to the City of Fremont except that the annual payment shall be paid on or
before August 10th of each year.
   Should the Sponsor's payment of the annual Service Charge be received by the
City after August 10th of each year it is due, then the City shall apply an
initial four percent (4%) penalty to the amount due. The original service
charge, plus the four percent (4%) penalty, shall accrue interest at the rate
of one percent (1%) per month compounded monthly; beginning from the first day
the payment is delinquent. In addition to the penalty and the accrued interest,
the City may use any legal remedies at its disposal to secure payment of the
service charge, plus any penalty and interest. (Ord. O-12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-55. Duration.
   This Article shall remain in effect and shall not terminate for 45 years so
long as the Housing Development remains subject to income and rent restrictions
pursuant to Section 42 of the Internal Revenue Code of 1986, as amended.
Provided, however that renovation of the Senior Housing Development commences
within two years and is completed within three years from the effective date of
this Article. At the end of the forty-fifth (45) year, or earlier term, the
aforementioned Housing Development shall no longer be exempt from ad valorem
property taxes and shall be placed on the ad valorem property tax roll by the
City Assessor and City Treasurer at its assessed value at the time the
exemption terminates.
   Any significant change of the Senior Housing Development's original or
initial public or private financing, refinancing, ownership, or other similar
factors shall automatically trigger a review by the Fremont City Council of the
facts, conditions, acknowledgments, rates of return and any other aspect of the
Sponsor's and other partners' or entities' participation in the Housing
Development. If the Council's review determines, in its reasonable yet sole
determination, that there were or would be significant changes in the intent,
return on investment, or any other facet of the Housing Development as
originally proposed by the Sponsor and as acknowledged and agreed to in this
Article, then the City Council reserves the right to modify, continue or cancel
the tax exemption for the aforementioned Housing Development. (Ord. O-12-04, 7-
16-12; Ord. O-14-02, 5-19-14)
Sec. 4-56. Review and Audit of Sponsor's Records.
   The Sponsor shall permit the City, its appointed representatives, advisors
or financial auditing firm(s) to periodically conduct an audit of the annual
financial records of the project to determine the accuracy of the data used and
the calculations made to determine the PILOT amounts. If an audit reveals an
underpayment by the Sponsor of more than ten percent (10%) of the PILOT as
calculated and paid by the Sponsor to the City in any one year, then the
Sponsor shall be required to pay the City for the costs of the audit. (Ord. O-
12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-57. Contractual Effect of this Article.
   Notwithstanding the provisions of Section 15(a)(5) of the Act to the
contrary, a contract between the City of Fremont and the Sponsor, with the
Authority as third-party beneficiary under the contract, to provide tax
exemption and accept payments in lieu of taxes, as previously described, is
effectuated by enactment of this Article. However, the City reserves its rights
to pursue other legal remedies to enforce provisions of this Article. (Ord. O-
12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-58. Severability.
   The various sections and provisions of this Article shall be deemed to be
severable and should any section or provision of this Article be declared by
any court of competent jurisdiction to be unconstitutional or invalid, the same
shall not affect the validity of the Article as a whole or any section or
provision of this Article other than the section or provision so declared to be
unconstitutional or invalid. (Ord. O-12-04, 7-16-12)
Sec. 4-59. Effective Date.
   This Article shall take effect ten (10) days after publication thereof.
(Ord. O-12-04, 7-16-12)
