Article I. In General.
Sec. 9-1. to 9-10. Reserved for future legislation.
Sec. 9-11. Burning Ordinance.
   (a)   Establishment of revised ordinances.
      (1)   Short title: This revised Ordinance shall be known as the "Burning
Ordinance" (last amended on March 26, 1945.)
      (2)   Authority: The authority for this Ordinance is set forth in Chapter
II, Section
2.1 of the City Charter of the City of Fremont.
      (3)   Purpose: This Ordinance is revised to preserve and protect public
health, safety and general welfare of the residents of the City of Fremont
(hereinafter "City") by prohibiting certain burnings within the City limits.
   (b)   Definitions.
   Ashes/Soot: By-product and residue from fire
   City of Fremont Fire Department Approval: Written approval from the Fire
Chief, Assistant Chief or their designee
   Garbage: Any putrescible animal or vegetable waste resulting from handling,
preparation, cooking or consumption of food
   Refuse: Any combustible trash including, but not limited to, paper, cartons,
boxes, plastics, extrusions, furniture, and bedding, and non combustible trash
including, but not limited to, metals, tin cans and glass
   Yard Waste: Regular wastes produced from landscaping and gardening
activities including, but not limited to, leaves, grass clippings, vegetable or
other garden debris, shrubbery or brush or tree clippings or similar materials.
   (c)   Burning prohibited.
      (1)   General Prohibition: It shall be unlawful for any person or persons
to burn, or cause to burn, assist in burning, continue or permit continuance of
the burning of any material including, but not limited to, refuse, garbage,
yard waste, papers and windblown refuse within the City limits of Fremont
except as prescribed herein.
      (2)   Streets, alleys, highways, curbs and sidewalks: No material of any
kind shall be burned or attempted to be burned in any street, alley or highway,
or between any curb and the sidewalk adjacent thereto, or any public or private
street rights-of-way within the City.
      (3)   Commercial incinerators: Commercial and industrial type
incinerators used for the burning of combustible solid waste material (non-
garbage) are prohibited by State law.
      (4)   Burning uses permitted: Exceptions to Section 9-11.3 are as
follows:
         a.   Open burning: No open burning other then recreational fires
referred to in part ‘C' of this Section, shall be allowed unless a burning
permit is first issued by the City Clerk. The permit must be signed by the Fire
Chief or his/her designee. If permitted, all burning shall be carried out in
accordance with Fire Department instructions and any other applicable rules
that may be adopted by the City or the State of Michigan.
         b.   Cooking fires: Fires are permitted for the cooking and smoking of
food for personal, non commercial uses provided that such fires are confined to
a barbecue grill, barbecue pit, smokehouse or other enclosure, and provided
further that the emission of smoke and fumes do not irritate, annoy or
constitute a nuisance to other property owners in the neighborhood.
         c.   Recreational fires: Recreational fires on private property are
permitted and do not need City Clerk or Fire Chief approval when in a pit or
pile which does not exceed three (3) feet in diameter, provided the following
conditions are met:
            1.   Fires are attended by a person at least 18 years of age until
extinguished ashes are cold.
            2.   Only clean wood products or commercially-produced fuel
products are burned.
            3.   The fire does not endanger other buildings or structures.
            4.   Atmospheric conditions are favorable.
            5.   Prohibit emission of smoke or fumes, which irritate, annoy or
constitute a nuisance to others living in the neighborhood.
         d.   Bonfires: Public or private bonfires in which material would
exceed three (3) feet in diameter require a permit issued by the City Clerk and
are subject to prior approval of the City Fire Department. Such approval may be
granted at the sole discretion of the Clerk and Fire Department based upon:
            1.   The proximity of the proposed bonfires to dwellings, trees and
other structures.
            2.   Facilities available for fire management.
            3.   Atmospheric conditions.
            4.   Type of material to be burned.
            5.   Any other consideration judged by the Clerk or Fire Department
to be required to ensure safe burning.
         e.   Contractor generated fires: Fires for the heating of outdoor
building sites shall not be permitted. Outdoor fires are permitted when
necessary to pursue a business or trade requiring the use of fire, including by
the way of example, but not necessarily by way of limitation, the heating,
boiling of tar, pitch or oil or other substances when used by roofer and other
tradesmen.
         f.   Papers: It shall be unlawful to burn paper, paper products or
other materials anywhere in the City unless burned inside a building in a
stove, fireplace or furnace sufficiently constructed to prohibit the escape of
ignited particles, provided that the emission of smoke and fumes does not
irritate, annoy or constitute a nuisance to other property owners in the
neighborhood.
      (5)   Exceptions and special circumstances.
         a.   Open fires are permitted in the performance of an official duty
by public officers for fires necessary for one or more of the following reason
or purposes:
            1.   For the prevention of a fire hazard that cannot be abated by
any other means.
            2.   For the instruction of public firefighters or industrial/
commercial employees under proper supervision of a qualified instructor.
            3.   For the protection of public health, safety, or welfare.
            4.   For controlled disposal of refuse or debris as collected by or
on behalf of the City at a site owned or operated by the City.
         b.   Special circumstances: In the sole discretion of the City fire
Department when there exist circumstances which lack any other reasonable means
of disposing of items which need to be disposed and not addressed herein, then
the Fire Department may issue a permit to burn.
      (6)   Remedies and liability for cost recovery.
         a.   Costs: All cost incurred by the City for enforcement of this
Ordinance shall be the responsibility of the part in violation of this
Ordinance.
         b.   Civil remedies: The City may pursue any other remedy, or may
institute any appropriate action for proceedings in a court with competent
jurisdiction or before any administrative agency to collect costs for liability
imposed for violation of this Ordinance.
      (7)   Violations; municipal civil infractions; authorized city officials;
civil fines and sanctions.
         a.   General provisions: Any violation of any provision of this
ordinance or of any permit granted herein, or of any lawful order of the City
Clerk, Fire Chief, or other public official issued in pursuance of this
Ordinance shall be and shall constitute a Municipal Civil Infraction. A
"violation" includes any act that is prohibited or made or declared to be
unlawful or an offense by this Ordinance and any omission failure where the act
is required by this Ordinance.
         b.   The sanction for any violation of this Ordinance, which
constitutes a Municipal Civil Infraction, shall be a Civil Fine as provided
hereunder, plus any costs, damages, expenses and other sanctions as authorized
and permitted under Chapter 87 of Act No. 236 of the Michigan Public Acts of
1961, as amended, and under other applicable laws:
            1.   Any person, individual, firm, partnership, co-partnership,
corporation, company, association, club, joint venture, and any other group,
entity or association acting as a unit, and the individuals constituting such
group, entity or unit, who, as a result of violating any provision of this
Ordinance, is responsible for Municipal Civil Infraction, shall pay a civil
fine to the City Clerk's, plus costs and other sanctions as authorized and
permitted by law, for each Municipal Civil Infraction. The first infraction of
this Ordinance shall carry a civil fine of fifty dollars ($50.00).
            2.   Repeat violations shall be subject to increased Civil Funds as
set forth below. As used in this Section, "repeat violation" means a second (or
any subsequent) Municipal Civil Infraction of requirement or provisions of this
Ordinance (1) committed by a violating party within any 12-month period, and
(2) for which the violating party admits responsibility or is determined to be
responsible. The increased Civil Fine for a repeat violation under this
Ordinance shall be as follows:
               i.   The Civil Fine for any violation which is a repeat
violation shall be two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) plus costs and other
sanctions as authorized and permitted by law.
               ii.   The Civil Fine for any violation which is a second (or any
subsequent) repeat violation shall be five hundred dollars ($500.00) plus costs
and other sanctions as authorized and permitted by law.
      (8)   Compliance with federal and state law: Not withstanding anything
set forth in this Ordinance, all open burning permitted under the terms and
provisions of this Ordinance shall also be conducted and performed in
compliance with all federal and state laws, statutes, rules and regulations
applicable thereto.
      (9)   Severability: In any section, sentence, clause or phrase of this
Ordinance is for any reason held to be invalid or unconstitutional by a
decision of any court of competent jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect
the validity of the remaining portions of this Ordinance.
      (10)   Conflicting ordinances and amendments superseded.
         a.   Present ordinance: On the effective date of the adoption of this
Ordinance, Sections 9-11 and 9-12 of Article I of Chapter 9 of the Fremont City
Code are hereby repealed.
         b.   Conflicts: All other ordinances, amendments or provisions
thereof, which may be inconsistent or in conflict with this Ordinance are
hereby repealed.
      (11)   Effective date: This Ordinance shall become effective ten (10)
days following publication; said effective date being October 23, 1999. (Ord.
O-99-04, 10-4-99)
Sec. 9-12. Reserved
Sec. 9-13. False fire alarms
   No person shall cause to be made any fire alarm without reasonable cause.
(7-23-23, 8.)
Sec. 9-14 to 9-26. Reserved for future legislation.
Article III. Prohibition of Freestanding Outdoor Furnaces
Sec. 9-27. Freestanding outdoor furnaces.
   Freestanding Outdoor Furnace - shall mean, but is not limited to, any
device, apparatus or structure that:
   1.   Is designed, intended or used to provide heat and/or hot water to any
residence or structure; and
   2.   Operates by burning wood or other solid fuel such as, but not limited
to, coal, paper or agricultural products; and
   3.   Is not located within the residence or structure for which it is
providing heat and/or hot water. (Ord. No. O-04-01, 3-15-04)
Sec. 9-28. Prohibition.
   It shall be unlawful to install or operate a freestanding outdoor furnace,
or to cause or permit the installation or operation of a freestanding outdoor
furnace, within the City. (Ord. No. O-04-01, 3-15-04)
Sec. 9-29. Conflicts.
   This Section shall not be construed as an exemption or exception to any
other provision of these Codified Ordinances. In the event of a conflict
between the provisions of this Section and any other ordinance or other
provision of law, the more restrictive provision shall apply. (Ord. No. O-04-
01, 3-15-04)
Sec. 9-30. Existing Uses.
   This Section shall not apply to any freestanding outdoor furnace that was
installed, connected and operating as of the effective date of this Section.
However, this Section shall not be deemed as specific authorization for the use
of any preexisting freestanding outdoor furnace and shall not be deemed to bar,
limit, or otherwise affect the rights of any person to take private legal
action regarding damage or nuisance caused by the use of a freestanding outdoor
furnace. (Ord. No. O-04-01, 3-15-04)
Sec. 9-31. Violations; Declaration of Nuisance.
   Any freestanding outdoor furnace installed or operated in violation of this
Section is hereby declared to be nuisance per se. (Ord. No. O-04-01, 3-15-04)
Sec. 9-32. Penalty.
   Whoever violates any provision of this Section is responsible for a
Municipal civil infraction, and shall be subject to the payment of a civil fine
in the amount as provided in this ordinance and all other sanctions that apply
to civil infractions for each infraction. Each day that a violation exists or
continues shall constitute a separate and additional violation. (Ord. No. O-04-
01, 3-15-04)
Sec. 9-33. Effective Date.
   Article III of this Ordinance shall take effect ten (10) days after
publication thereof in accordance with the provisions of the City of Fremont
City Charter. (Ord. No. O-04-01, 3-15-04)
Article IV. Fire Department
Sec. 9-34. Title, Authority and Purpose.
   (a)   Short title: This Article shall be known as the "Fire Department
Ordinance" (previously established by City Ordinance adopted on November 23,
1923, as amended.)
   (b)   Authority: The authority for this Article is set forth in the
following Sections of Chapter II of the City Charter of the City of Fremont:
      (1)   Section
2.1 "General Powers";
      (2)   Section
2.2 "Specific Powers"; and
      (3)   Section
2.3 "Intergovernmental Contracts".
   (c)   Purpose: This Article is adopted to:
      (1)   Preserve and protect public health, safety and general welfare of
the residents of the City of Fremont (hereinafter "City") by establishment of
the Fremont Fire Department.
      (2)   Provide for the basic organizational structure of said Department.
      (3)   Delegate broad management authority and responsibility to the City
Manager and Fire Chief.
      (4)   Provide standards of accountability of the Chief and other
Department personnel to the City Manager and City Council.
      (5)   Establish authority to adopt Department by-laws, rules and
regulations for the conduct of personnel and operation and maintenance of the
Department and its equipment.
      (6)   Employ, appoint and prescribe the powers and duties of a Chief,
firefighters and officers.
      (7)   Repeal any parts or portions of City ordinances inconsistent
herewith. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-35. Establishing a Fire Department.
   The City Council hereby establishes the "Fremont Fire Department"
(hereinafter referred to as "Department") as further organized, structured,
governed and regulated herein. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-36. Geographic Coverage/Service Area.
   The Department shall be responsible for providing services, as defined in
Section
9-37, to the entire geographic corporate limits of the City, as they may be
adjusted from time to time through annexation or other means permitted by the
State of Michigan Constitution or Statutes.
   The City Council may, through an intergovernmental contract or agreement,
authorize the Department to provide services to all or a portion of the
geographic area of any other governmental unit or agency, or with any number of
combinations thereof.
   The Department shall restrict its delivery of emergency services to the
geographic area or areas described in this Section and authorized by the City
Council, and to other jurisdictions with which the City Council has entered
into "mutual aid agreements." Mutual aid agreements may allow for the provision
of all or a portion of Department services. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-37. Scope and Level of Services.
   Consistent with appropriations and budget authorization, the Department is
authorized to provide the following programs and services within the City
Council authorized Service Area:
   (1)   Fire Suppression;
   (2)   Fire Education;
   (3)   Fire Prevention and Code Enforcement;
   (4)   Medical First Responder (Level 1 "life threatening emergencies" only);
and
   (5)   Rescue. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-38. Basic Organizational Structure.
   The Department shall be actively supervised and managed by a Fire Chief. In
accordance with Section
7.3 of the City Charter, the position of Fire Chief is an "administrative
officer" of the City and shall be appointed or removed by the City Council
based upon the City Manager's recommendation. As directed in the same Charter
Section
7.3, the City Manager shall "supervise and coordinate the work of all
administrative officers (including the Chief) and Departments (including the
Fire Department.)"
   To ensure continuity of command and appropriate incident supervision, the
City Council authorizes the following officer positions, which creates the
following chain of command in descending order of authority:
   (1)   Chief;
   (2)   Assistant Chief;
   (3)   1st Captain;
   (4)   2nd Captain;
   (5)   Lieutenant.
   With the advice and assistance of the City Manager, the Chief shall develop
and approve job descriptions and qualifications for each of the above officer
positions and all paid-per-call firefighters. Appointment and selection of the
above officers and firefighters shall be as prescribed in Department By-Laws as
authorized in Section
9-40. The Department shall consist of such number of members as are designated,
from time to time, by the City Council, consistent with appropriations, budget
authorization, service area, and scope and level of services. (Ord. No. O-08-
03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-39. Fire Department Finances.
   The City Council shall approve an annual appropriation for the operation and
maintenance of the Department and its equipment based on the recommendations
contained in the City Manager's proposed Annual City Operating & Capital
Improvement Budget. For that above purpose, the City Council shall have the
authority to:
   (1)   Use General Funds;
   (2)   Initiate the creation of a special assessment district and levy
special assessments;
   (3)   Sell bonds;
   (4)   Establish user fees;
   (5)   Bill for services rendered; and
   (6)   Raise revenues in any other manner provided for under State law and
consistent with the City Charter for the operation and maintenance of the
Department.
   The City Council shall provide for payment of any debts incurred incidental
to the Department's continued operation and shall purchase necessary equipment
and/or construct public buildings for uses incidental to the maintenance and
operation of the Department. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-40. Department By-Laws, Rules and Regulations.
   The City Council shall establish rules and regulations for the operations of
the Department and the care and use of the equipment through adoption of
general policies. The members of the Department shall draft their own by-laws,
which shall be reviewed and modified, if necessary, by the City Manager and
recommended for ratification by the City Council before becoming effective. The
Chief shall prepare and enforce specific operating procedures consistent with
such general policies and by-laws. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-41. Chief Duties.
   The Chief shall be accountable to the City Manager and City Council for the
efficient and effective operation for the Department, and for the Department's
compliance with all state laws and administrative rules, and City ordinances
and policies. The Chief may delegate or assign the completion of individual
duties as needed, but shall continue to remain accountable for their proper and
timely completion. Duties shall include, but are not limited to, the following:
   (a)   Develop written administrative rules to increase the efficiency and
effectiveness of the Department, including pre-planning and post-incident
critiques, regulations, and assigning and scheduling of personnel.
   (b)   Develop plans for the long-range operating and capital needs of the
Department.
   (c)   Be familiar with state and federal laws that impact Department
operations, and develop written rules and regulations, and issue orders
consistent with applicable state and federal laws and administrative rules.
Department noncompliance with applicable state and federal laws and regulations
shall be promptly reported to the City Manager.
   (d)   Develop written policies and procedures to ensure compliance with the
General Industry Safety Standards of the Michigan Occupational Safety and
Health Act (MIOSHA). The Chief shall promptly inform the City Manager of any
procedure or equipment that is not in compliance with any MIOSHA General
Industry Safety Standards and shall recommend actions necessary to achieve
compliance.
   (e)   Hold regular Department informational and training meetings.
   (f)   Incur expenditures against the Department budget as appropriated by
the City Council. The Chief shall monitor the unencumbered balances remaining
in the Department budget and shall make timely recommendations to the City
Manager for budget amendments at such time as the need for such amendments
become known. The Department's expenditures shall not exceed the amounts
appropriated for each line item within the Department's budget. Capital outlay
purchases shall be made in compliance with the City's Purchasing Ordinance.
   (g)   The Chief shall also be responsible for the following:
      (1)   Supervise the extinguishment of all fires that endanger the health,
safety and welfare of the City.
      (2)   Enforce City burning ordinances.
      (3)   Ensure that all personnel are trained and qualified for the duties
that they are expected to fulfill.
      (4)   Ensure that the Department conducts fire prevention and education
programs.
      (5)   Ensure that all Department equipment, vehicles and buildings are
properly maintained and in good and safe working order.
      (6)   Ensure that all Department personnel comply with Departmental and
City rules, regulations and policies. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-42. Training.
   The Chief shall develop a regular schedule of in-house training classes,
including an attendance requirement for all Department personnel. The schedule
shall specify the type, amount and frequency of training to be provided to fire
service personnel necessary to ensure that all employees are adequately trained
to handle properly the inherent risks of fire fighting and other emergency
incidents. The Chief shall ensure that a record of each firefighter's
participation and skill mastery is maintained. Employees shall be trained
before they are permitted to perform emergency operations. The Chief shall
ensure that qualified individuals deliver in-house instruction.
   The Chief shall require that all firefighters have achieved and maintained
all certifications required by state or federal law or rule to perform fire
suppression, medical first responder, rescue or other services performed by the
Department. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-43. Safety.
   The Chief shall be familiar with the provisions of federal and state laws
and administrative rules related to employee safety and health regulations, and
shall develop written procedures to ensure compliance.
   The Chief shall establish and implement written procedures for emergency
operations in compliance with current MIOSHA regulations. The procedures shall
include all of the following:
   (1)   Compliance with a nationally recognized incident management system
that will be implemented at each emergency.
   (2)   A personnel accountability system that will be implemented at each
emergency.
   (3)   Applicability to all employees who are operating at the emergency.
   (4)   Initial training and annual refresher training in emergency operations
and the incident management system
   (5)   Procedures that are in accordance with the "two in / two out" rules as
found in the provisions of current MIOSHA standards.
   (6)   A properly trained employee shall function as the incident commander
at each emergency. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-44. Disciplinary Procedures.
   Disciplinary actions, procedures and proceedings shall be developed and
incorporated into the Department's by-laws as authorized under Section
9-40. Those actions, procedures or proceedings not addressed in the
Department's by-laws shall be governed by the City's Personnel Policies and
Procedures Manual. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-45. Compensation of Members.
   The amount and terms of compensation of the Chief, other officers and
firefighters shall be fixed from time to time by the City Council. The
Department shall keep accurate records that indicate the amount of compensable
time served by all personnel. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-46. Public Contact.
   The Fire Chief, or his/her designee, may release facts regarding fires or
other emergencies to the news media. The Chief, or designee, shall speak to the
media on behalf of the Department. All other personnel shall refer all media
inquiries requiring a statement on behalf of the Department to the Chief, or
designee.
   Department personnel shall not, in connections with Department activities or
functions, make statements or writings that constitute libel or slander; which
would impede a law enforcement investigation or compromise the presumption of
innocence until proven guilty; or which would deny any person due process.
   Members of the public may be allowed in or upon the Fire Station, other
Department facilities or vehicles only when accompanied by a member of the
Department or the City Manager or his/her designee. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-47. Emergency Response.
   When responding to emergencies, all personnel shall drive emergency vehicles
with appropriate concern for the safety of the public and defensive driving.
Use of emergency signals on vehicles shall be considered a "request" for the
right-of-way from other drivers.
   Use of emergency signal equipment shall be permitted only when the
Department has been officially dispatched to an emergency, or as part of a tour
or static demonstration.
   The Fire Chief shall establish written regulations regarding the use of
emergency signal equipment on City-owned and personal vehicles. (Ord. No. O-08-
03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-48. Department Equipment.
   Protective equipment shall be worn when engaged in firefighting in any
enclosed structure, or outdoors when warranted.
   Lost or damaged equipment shall be reported as soon as possible to a
Department officer. City property shall be disposed of only in accordance with
City rules or policies. All Department-issued equipment shall be returned to
the Chief upon terminating employment with the Department. (Ord. No. O-08-03,
3-17-08)
Sec. 9-49. Use of Fire Station and Equipment.
   Only City-owned vehicles and equipment may be kept or stored at the Fire
Station. Department equipment or vehicles shall not be borrowed for private
use. Private vehicles must be parked in designated areas only. Alcohol and
controlled substances shall not be brought into, used or consumed in the Fire
Station or in any City-owned vehicle, building or facility. (Ord. No. O-08-03,
3-17-08)
Sec. 9-50. Damage to Equipment.
   No person shall willfully damage, mar or deface in any manner any vehicle,
equipment or other apparatus of the Department or any building or structure
belonging to or connected with the Fire Department of this City. No person
shall in any manner molest, handle, meddle or interfere with any of the
apparatus in or about the Fire Station, at any emergency scene or elsewhere.
(Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-51. Powers and Duties Generally; Obedience of Persons at Emergency
Scene; Obstructing, Hindering or Resisting Performance of Duty.
   The incident commander shall have full power, control and command over all
members of the Fire Department and all other persons at emergency scenes. The
incident commander shall have the power to enforce the laws of the State, the
provisions of this Code and other ordinances of the City relative to the
conduct of persons at emergency scenes. Every person present at any emergency
scene shall obey the lawful orders of the incident commander and shall not
obstruct, hinder or resist them in the performance of their duties. (Ord. No.
O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-52. Soliciting Donations.
   All fundraising activities shall have the prior approval of the City
Manager, and all revenues solicited in the name of the Fire Department shall be
deposited with the City Treasurer. Such funds will be disbursed by the
Treasurer upon receipt of proper documentation signed by the Chief following
approval by the City Council. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-53. Destruction of Buildings to Arrest Progress of Fire.
   The Fire Chief, with the concurrence of the City Manager, may cause any
building to be pulled down or destroyed when deemed necessary in order to
arrest the progress of any fire, or to preserve the health, safety or welfare
of the public and no action shall be maintained against any person or against
the City. The costs for such actions, whether performed with the use of City-
owned equipment and personnel or by contractual private equipment or personnel,
may be assessed against the property and/or property owner. (Ord. No. O-08-03,
3-17-08)
Sec. 9-54. Savings Clause.
   Should any court of competent jurisdiction declare any portion of this
Article unenforceable, then the remainder of this Article shall remain in full
force and effect unaffected by the portion that might be so declared to be
unenforceable. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
Sec. 9-55. Effective Date.
   Upon adoption by the City Council, this Article shall become effective ten
(10) days after proper publication thereof, in accordance with the provisions
of the Fremont City Charter, said effective date being immediately on March 17,
2008. (Ord. No. O-08-03, 3-17-08)
