ARTICLE I: ALCOHOLIC BEVERAGES, CURFEW, DESTRUCTION OF PROPERTY, ETC.
Sec. 13-1. Alcoholic beverages – Purchase, possession, transportation, etc., by
person under twenty-one.
   No person under the age of twenty-one (21) years shall purchase or knowingly
possess, transport or have under his control in any motor vehicle any alcoholic
liquor unless such person is employed by a licensee under state statute and is
possessing, transporting or having such alcoholic liquor in a motor vehicle
under his control during regular working hours and in the course or his
employment.
(6-17-68, 1; 8-6-79)
   State law reference – For similar state law, M.C.L.A. § 257.624b.
   Cross reference – Intoxicating beverages in parks, 14-23.
Sec. 13-1.1. Same – Purchase, possession, transportation, etc., by person under
twenty-one; outside motor vehicle.
   No person under the age of twenty-one (21) years shall purchase alcoholic
liquor, consume alcoholic liquor in a licensed premises, or possess alcoholic
liquor, except where the person is employed by a licensee under state statute,
a common carrier designated by the Michigan Liquor Control Commission, the
Liquor Control Commission, or an agent of the Liquor Control Commission and is
transporting or having the alcoholic liquor in a motor vehicle under the
person's control during regular working hours and in the course of the person's
employment. A person less than twenty-one (21) years of age who violates this
section is liable for the civil fines as determined by resolution of the city
council and shall not be subject to the penalties specified in Section 1-16 of
the Fremont City Code:
   (a)   For the first violation a fine of not more than twenty-five dollars
($25.00).
   (b)   For the second violation a fine of not more than fifty dollars
($50.00).
   (c)   For the third or subsequent violation a fine of not more than one
hundred dollars ($100.00).
(Ord. No. O-91-06, 10-21-91)
Sec. 13-1.2. Same – Consumption of alcoholic liquor on a highway, public place,
or area generally accessible to motor vehicles, including area designated for
parking of vehicles; violation punishable as a misdemeanor.
   (a)   A person shall not consume alcoholic liquor or possess any open
container of alcoholic liquor upon a highway, street, alley, sidewalk, parking
area, parking lot or any public or private property which is open to the
general public and which is not licensed to sell alcoholic liquor for
consumption on the premises, or within the passenger compartment of a moving
vehicle upon a highway or in any place open to the general public or generally
accessible to motor vehicles, including an area designated for the parking of
vehicles in the City of Fremont. The term "parking area" shall include any area
wherein motor vehicles are parked by the public in conjunction with any private
business, enterprise, commercial establishment, office building, or apartment
building.
   (b)   A person who violates this section is guilty of a misdemeanor,
punishable by a term of imprisonment of not more than ninety (90) days and a
fine of not more than one hundred dollars ($100.00), or both.
(Ord. No. O-92-01, 6, 3-2-92)
Sec. 13-2. Same – Furnishing to minors.
   No person shall willfully give or furnish any alcoholic beverage to a person
twenty-one (21) years of age, except upon authority of and pursuant to a
prescription of a duly licensed physician. (6-17-68, 2; 8-6-79)
   State law reference – For similar state law, M.C.L.A. § 750.141a.
Sec. 13-3. Same – Misrepresentation of age.
   No person under the age of twenty-one (21) years shall falsely represent
himself to be twenty-one (21) years of age or over for the purpose of
purchasing or attempting to purchase any alcoholic beverage; no person shall
furnish any documentary evidence falsely representing himself to be twenty-one
(21) years of age to be used for the purpose of obtaining any alcoholic
beverage.
(6-17-69, 3; 8-6-79)
Sec. 13-4. Curfew – Minors under twelve.
   No minor under the age of twelve (12) years shall loiter, idle, wander,
stroll, play or congregate in or on any public street, highway, alley,
playground, beach, other public grounds or public buildings, vacant lots or
other unsupervised places in the city between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 6:00
a.m., unless the minor is accompanied by a parent or guardian or some adult
delegated by the parent or guardian to accompany the child.
(3-12-62, § 1)
   State law references – For similar state law, M.C.L.A. § 722.751; as to
powers of city to regulate curfews of minors, M.C.L.A. § 722.754.
Sec. 13-5. Same – Minors under sixteen.
   No minor under the age of sixteen (16) years shall loiter, idle, wander,
stroll, play or congregate in or on any public street, highway, alley, park,
playground, beach, other public grounds or public buildings, vacant lots or
other unsupervised places in the city between the hours of 12:00 midnight and
6:00 a.m., except where the minor is accompanied by a parent or guardian or
some adult over the age of eighteen (18) years delegated by the parent or
guardian to accompany the minor child or where the minor is upon an errand or
other legitimate business directed by his parent or guardian.
(3-12-62, § 2)
   State law reference – For similar state law, M.C.L.A. § 722.752.
Sec. 13-6. Same – Aiding, etc., violation of curfew by person over sixteen.
   Any person of the age of sixteen (16) years or over assisting, aiding,
abetting, allowing, permitting or encouraging any minor under the age of
sixteen (16) years to violate the provisions of sections 13-4 and 13-5 is
guilty of a misdemeanor.
   State law reference – For similar state law, M.C.L.A. § 722.753.
Sec. 13-7. Destruction, etc., of property – Signs, markers, barricades, etc.,
of city.
   No person shall damage, destroy, carry away, remove, deface or in any manner
whatsoever molest or interfere with, unless authorized so to do by the city
council, any of the signs, markers, lanterns, torches, flares or barricades at
any time erected, placed, kept or maintained by or under the authority of the
city or within its jurisdiction or control upon any of the streets, alleys,
sidewalks, highways, parks or other places, whether public or private, within
the corporate limits of the city.
(2-8-37, § 1)
   Cross references – As to destruction of property in parks, 14-33; as to
destruction, injury, etc., of trees and shrubs in parks, 14-37.
Sec. 13-8. Same – Tools, machinery, personal property, etc., of city.
   No person shall damage, destroy, carry away, remove, deface or in any manner
whatsoever molest or interfere with, unless authorized so to do by the city
council any tools, implement, trucks, machinery, equipment or other personal
property of any name or nature of the city or in its possession or under its
jurisdiction or control wherever situated within or without the corporate
limits of the city.
(2-8-37, § 2)
   Cross references – As to opening mains valves or hydrants of water system,
21-7; as to destruction of structures or equipment of sewage system, 21-45.
Sec. 13-9. Same – Trees, buildings, etc., of city.
   No person shall damage, destroy, carry away, remove, deface or in any manner
whatsoever molest or interfere with unless authorized so to do by the city
council any of the trees, shrubs, public buildings, or other property of any
name or nature owned by the city or in its possession or within its
jurisdiction or control or situated upon any public or private property over
which the city has jurisdiction or control.
(2-8-37, § 3)
Sec. 13-10. Disorderly persons – Acts and practices constituting.
   Definitions: For purposes of this ordinance "public place" and/or "place
open to the public" shall include but not be limited to the following:
   Any place to which the general public has access for business, entertainment
or other lawful purposes, but does not necessarily mean a place devoted solely
to the use of the public, and includes any shopping center, shopping mall,
store, shop, restaurant, tavern or bar, parking lot, or other place of
business, public park or other public place. Any person shall be deemed a
disorderly person who shall, or who shall aid and abet another to commit one
(1) or more of the following acts:
   (a)   Assembling for illegal purposes. Collect or stand in crowds or
arrange, encourage or abet the collection or persons in crowds for illegal or
mischievous purposes in any public place or place open to the public.
   (b)   Loitering. Loiter on any street or sidewalk or in any park or other
public place open to the public. The following acts shall be deemed to
constitute loitering within the meaning of this subsection:
      (1)   Congregate in such a fashion as to obstruct the free and
uninterrupted passage of the public;
      (2)   Obstruct vehicular traffic;
      (3)   Sit on the sidewalk;
      (4)   Lie on the sidewalk;
      (5)   Sit on the steps leading to any building open to the public or to
which the public is invited;
   (c)   Unnecessary crowding. Jostle or roughly crowd unnecessarily in any
public place or place open to the public.
   (d)   Public fight or disturbance. Engage in any disturbance, fight or
quarrel in any public place or place open to the public.
   (e)   Assault and battery. Commit an assault or an assault and battery on
any person.
   (f)   Fireworks. Fire, discharge, display or possess any fireworks, except
of the type and under the conditions permitted by Chapter 39 of the Penal Code
of the State of Michigan, as amended.
   (g)   Peeping Tom. Engage in peeping in the windows of any inhabited place.
   (h)   Begging. Beg in any public place or any place open to the public.
   (i)   Use of obscene language in public place or place open to the public.
Utter vile, profane or obscene language in any public place or place open to
the public.
   (j)   Indecent, immoral or obscene conduct. Engage in any indecent, immoral
or obscene conduct.
   (k)   Indecent exposure. Make any immoral exhibition or indecent exposure of
his person.
   (l)   Prostitution, gambling, and illegal or immoral business or occupation.
Engage in prostitution, gambling, the illegal sale of intoxicating liquor or
any other illegal or immoral business or occupation.
   (m)   Attend, operate, or occupy places of prostitution, gambling or other
illegal or immoral business or occupation. Knowingly attend, frequent, operate
or be an occupant or inmate of any place where prostitution, gambling, the
illegal sale of intoxicating liquor or where any other illegal or immoral
business or occupation is permitted or conducted.
   (n)   Solicitation for illegal or immoral act. Solicit or accost any person
for the purposes of inducing the commission of any illegal or immoral act.
   (o)   Transportation of person to prostitution or gambling house. Knowingly
transport any person to a place where prostitution or gambling is practiced,
encouraged or allowed for the purpose of enabling such person to engage in
gambling or in any illegal or immoral act.
   (p)   Maintenance of gaming room, table, or policy or pool tickets. Keep or
maintain a gaming room, gaming table or any policy or pool tickets used for
gaming; or knowingly suffer a gaming room, gaming table or any policy or pool
tickets to be kept, maintained, played or sold on any premises occupied or
controlled by him, provided, same is without property licensure from
appropriate governmental authorities.
   (q)   Disturbing the peace. No person shall disturb the public peace and
quiet by loud, boisterous or vulgar conduct or by making such excessive,
unnecessary, or unusually loud noise, whether on public or private property,
nor allow others under his control or direction to make such noise, which
disturbs the peace, good order, health and safety of other persons, a
neighborhood or the community in general.
   (r)   Disorderly houses. Permit or suffer any place occupied or controlled
by him to be a resort of noisy, boisterous and disorderly persons.
   (s)    Interfere with peace officer in discharge of duty. Obstruct, resist,
hinder or oppose any member of the police force or any peace officer in the
discharge of his duties as such.
      (1)   No person shall fail to obey a lawful order to disperse by a police
officer, when known to be such an official, where one (1) or more persons are
committing acts of disorderly conduct in the immediate vicinity, and individual
or public health, good order, safety or property is imminently threatened.
      (2)   No person shall knowingly give false information to any police
officer, official, employee, or representative of the city on any matter
pertaining to or affected by his/her official duties. No person shall conceal
his identity, or falsely identify him/herself in response to any inquiry by a
police officer, official, employee or representative of the city in connection
with the performance of his/her official duties.
   (t)   Prowling at night. Prowl about any alley or the private premises of
any person in the nighttime without authority or the permission of the owner of
such premises.
   (u)   Throwing of objects wrongfully. Throw or propel any snowball, missile
or object from any moving automobile, or wrongfully throw or propel any
snowball, missile or object toward any person or automobile.
   (v)   Throwing object at person or automobile. Wrongfully throw or propel
any snowball, missile or object toward any person or automobile.
   (w)   Destruction of property of another. Willfully destroy, remove, damage,
alter or in any manner deface any property not his own or any public school
building or any public building, bridge, fire hydrant, alarm box, street light,
street sign, traffic control device, railroad sign or signal, parking meter or
shade tree belonging to the city or located in the public places of the city or
mark or post handbills on or in any manner mar the walls of any public
building, fence, tree or pole within the city or destroy, take or meddle with
any property belonging to the city or remove the same from the building or
place where it may be kept, placed or stored without proper authority.
   (x)   False alarms. Summon as a joke or prank or otherwise without any good
reason therefor, by telephone or otherwise the police or the fire department or
any public or private ambulance to go to an address where the service called
for is not needed.
   (y)   Entry to watch specified activities. Go upon the premises of another
or upon the right-of-way of any railroad company or climb, stand in or upon any
tree or climb over, crawl under, break or cut through any fence for the purpose
of witnessing or looking at any football game, baseball game, or other athletic
sports or games whatsoever or any fair, show or other entertainment whatsoever
without the consent and permission of the owner or occupant of such lands,
right-of-way or the owner of any such tree or fence.
   (z)   Taking bicycle. Willfully and without authority take possession of and
ride or take away any bicycle without intent to steal.
   (aa)   Use of telephone to harass; vulgar, etc., language over telephone.
Telephone any person repeatedly or cause the same to be done for the primary
purpose of harassing such other person or his family or to use any threatening,
vulgar, indecent, obscene or immoral language over any telephone.
   (bb)   Dangerous lights, etc., on cars, etc. Use any light or flare on any
automobile or otherwise, in such manner as to cause annoyance to others or be
likely to endanger life or property or to interfere with traffic.
   (cc)   Disturbance of worship and other assemblages. Disrupt or aid in
disrupting in any manner any service or worship or any other assemblage for
lawful purposes.
(Ord. No. O-91-08, 10-21-91)
   Editor's note – Ord. No. O-91-08, adopted Oct. 21, 1991, repealed former 13-
10, relative to disorderly acts and conduct, and enacted a new 13-10 to read as
herein set out. Former 13-10 derived from Ords. of 1-20-69; 9-20-71; 1-20-75;
and 5-15-78.
   Cross reference – As to loitering, boisterous conduct, etc., in parks 14-24.
   State law references – For state law as to disorderly persons, M.C.L.A. §§
750.167, 750.168; as to crimes and offenses generally, M.C.L.A. Tit. 750.
Sec. 13-11. Distribution of handbills, circulars, etc.
   Unless a permit is first obtained from the city council, no person shall
peddle or distribute or cause to be peddled or distributed any handbills,
circulars, cards, pamphlets or other advertising matter in the city by leaving,
depositing or placing such materials or causing such materials to be left,
deposited or placed in, upon or at any private residence or premises or any
street, avenue, alley, public park or place in the city or in or upon any
vehicle while parked upon any street, avenue, alley, public park or place in
the city; provided, that nothing herein contained shall prohibit the
distribution of newspapers, periodicals or other printed matter to regular
subscribers thereof or the transmission of any such matter through the United
States mail.
(6-12-39, 1; 1-19-76, § 1)
   Cross reference – As to the posting of signs, bulletins or notices in parks,
14-33.
Sec. 13-12. Electrical interference – Operation of devices, etc., causing
interference.
   It shall be unlawful for any person knowingly or wantonly to operate or
cause to be operated any machine, device, apparatus or instrument of any kind
whatsoever within the corporate limits of the city, the operation of which
shall cause reasonably preventable electrical interference with radio or
television reception within the city; provided, however, that X-Ray pictures,
examinations or treatments and other medical tests, etc., involving such
devices may be made any time if the machines or apparatus used therefor are
properly equipped to avoid all unnecessary or reasonably preventable
interference with radio or television reception and are not negligently
operated.
(8-11-47, 1; 2-22-54, § 1)
Sec. 13-13. Same – Application of section 13-12 to areas in interstate commerce
or regulated by Congress.
   Section 13-12 shall not be held or construed to embrace or cover the
regulation of any transmitting, broadcasting or receiving instrument, apparatus
or device used or useful in interstate commerce or the operation of which
instrument, apparatus or device is licensed or authorized by or under the
provisions of any act of the Congress of the United States.
(8-11-47, § 2)
Sec. 13-14. Firearms – Discharge.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to fire or otherwise discharge any
firearm within the city, unless permission to do so is first obtained from the
chief of police. For the purposes of this section the word "firearm" shall mean
any weapon or device from which is propelled any missile, projectile, bullet,
shot, BB or other matter by means of explosives, compressed air or gas or by
means of springs, levers or other mechanical devices.
   Cross reference – As to discharge of firearms in parks, 14-13.
Sec. 13-15. Schools – Trespass generally.
   No person shall commit any trespass upon any land or buildings owned,
occupied or otherwise used by a school within the city; and any person not
having legitimate business in and around the schools located in the city shall
be deemed to be trespassing during the school hours or during school
activities.
(5-1-72, § 1)
Sec. 13-16. Same – Presence of persons within school during normal school
hours.
   No person other than a student or employee of any school located in the city
or parent or guardian of any student enrolled therein shall remain within any
school during normal school hours without securing the written permission of
the principle or person in charge of such school. The term "student" as used
herein is defined as any person of school age and properly enrolled in the
school system of the city.
(5-1-72, § 2)
Sec. 13-17. Same – Presence of persons on school grounds generally.
   No person other than a student or employee of any school located in the city
or parent or guardian of any student enrolled therein shall remain on any lands
owned, occupied or used by any school within the city without securing written
permission of the principal or person in charge of such school. The term
"student" as used herein is defined as any person of school age and enrolled in
the school system of the city.
(5-1-72, § 3)
Sec. 13-18. Sales by peddlers, etc. - Generally.
   The practices of going in or upon private residences in the city by
solicitors, peddlers, hawkers, itinerant merchants or transient vendors or
merchandise not having been requested or invited to do so by the owner or the
occupant of such private residences for the purpose of soliciting orders for
the sale of goods, wares and merchandise or disposing of or peddling or hawking
the sale is declared to be a misdemeanor.
(9-14-64, § 1)
   Charter reference – For charter provisions as to authority of city to
prohibit peddlers, Char., § 2.2(11).
   Cross reference – As to vending and peddling in parks, 14-39.
Sec. 13-19. Same – Dairy and farm products.
   Section 13-18 shall not apply to the sale or soliciting of orders for the
sale of milk, dairy products, vegetables, poultry, eggs and other farm and
garden produce so far as the sale of the commodities named herein is now
authorized by law.
(9-14-64, § 3)
Sec. 13-20. Same – Nonprofit organizations.
   Section 13-18 shall not apply to sales by nonprofit organizations.
Sec. 13-21. Regulation of the use of skateboards, roller skates, roller blades
or any similar device.
   (a)   Persons using or operating skateboards, roller skates, roller blades
or any similar devices can be a threat to their own safety as well as the
safety of the public at large and the pedestrian and vehicular density is
significant in the downtown area, on the public walkways and within the City of
Fremont so as to necessitate the regulation thereof.
   (b)   The use of any skateboard, roller skates, roller blades or any similar
device is prohibited on any sidewalk, public parking area, roadway, street,
alley, or other area open to the general public in the Central Business
District.
   (c)   The Central Business District is defined as that area bordered on the
West by Weaver Avenue, on the North by Dayton Street, on the East by Darling
Avenue and on the South by Sheridan Street. This includes Veterans Memorial
Park. The said border streets of the Central Business District shall be deemed
to include the following:
      (1)   Weaver Street – including the East sidewalk, but excluding the West
sidewalk;
      (2)   Dayton Street – including the South sidewalk, but excluding the
North sidewalk;
      (3)   Sheridan Street – including the North sidewalk, but excluding the
South sidewalk;
      (4)   Darling Street – including the West sidewalk, but excluding the
East sidewalk.
   (d)   This section does not apply to wheelchairs or other similar devices
which are being used by handicapped persons.
   (e)   No person shall use any skateboard, roller skates, roller blades or
similar device on any bench, table, planter, wall or other fixture located in
or along any public roadway, street, alley, sidewalk, parking lot or other area
open to the general public within the city limits of the City of Fremont.
   (f)   No person shall use any vehicle, motorcycle or bicycle to tow another
person on any skateboard, roller blades, roller skates or other similar device
within the city limits of the City of Fremont.
   (g)   No person shall use a skateboard, roller blades, roller skates or any
other similar device in any public place in a careless or negligent manner
which causes or reasonably could cause any injury to any person or any damage
to property owned by any other person, including, without limitation, any
public property, and further, such person shall yield the right of way to any
pedestrian and shall not approach, overtake or pass such pedestrian in a
reckless or careless manner, and shall not pass such pedestrian except in
single file if such person is roller skating or riding a skateboard or other
similar device with other such skaters or riders.
   (h)   The City Council may in its discretion, authorize the City Manager to
have signs placed on any city-owned property prohibiting the use of
skateboards, roller blades, roller skates or any other similar device on any
city-owned property which is so posted, and it shall be unlawful for any person
to use same on property so posted.
   (i)   A person that violates this section is responsible for a civil
infraction punishable by a fine of not more than $50.00 for the first offense,
$100.00 for the second offense, and $200.00 for the third offense and
thereafter. If any civil fine is imposed, the person assessed shall also
assessed and taxed as costs the expenses, direct and indirect of the
prosecution of such offense, to a maximum of $250.00 per offense, and, in
addition thereto, the cost of replacing, restoring or repairing damage to
property. Further, the offending device may be impounded for a period not to
exceed 60 days. This shall be in addition to or in lieu of the civil infraction
penalty indicated above.
Sec. 13-22. Regulation of the use of motor vehicles on recreational trailways.
   (a)   Purpose. The purpose of this section is to ensure the safe use and
quiet enjoyment of the City's recreational trails by pedestrians, bicyclists
and other lawfully permitted users.
   (b)   Definitions. For the purpose of this section, the following
definitions shall apply unless the context clearly indicates or requires a
different meaning.
      Recreational trailway means a trail, path or corridor that is (1) either
inside or outside of a street right-of-way, (2) owned or under the control of
the City, and (3) designated by the City for use by the public for recreational
purposes including but not limited to bicycling, walking, jogging and similar
non-motorized uses.
      Motor vehicle means a land conveyance impelled by mechanical power,
including but not limited to automobiles, trucks, buses, tractors, motorcycles,
mopeds, all-terrain vehicles, motor scooters, gopeds, snowmobiles and any other
vehicle propelled by a motor. This definition shall specifically exclude an
electric wheelchair or other similar mobility device being used by the
physically handicapped person for which it was intended.
   (c)   Prohibition of motor vehicles. No person shall operate, drive, park,
place, or occupy a motor vehicle, or permit the operation, driving, parking,
placing, or occupancy of any motor vehicle owned or possessed by him or her
upon a recreational trailway.
   (d)   Exception. This prohibition shall not apply to:
      (1)   Emergency vehicles acting in their official capacity, including but
not limited to fire, police, or emergency medical service vehicles; and
      (2)   Maintenance, construction, or other vehicles when used for purposes
expressly permitted and authorized by the City.
   (e)   Posting. The prohibition of motor vehicles shall be posted and
maintained near each gate or principal entrance of each recreational trailway
to which this section applies, as designated by the City.
   (f)   Trailway municipal civil infraction.
      (1)   A person who violates any provision of this section is responsible
for a civil infraction, subject to payment of a civil fine of not less than
$50.00 plus costs, and other sanctions or damages, for each infraction. In
addition, offending vehicles may be seized/impounded at the discretion of the
investigating officer.
      (2)   Repeat offenses under this section shall be subject to increased
fines not to exceed $500.00.
   (g)   Effective date. This section shall take effect ten (10) days after
publication thereof. (Ord. 0-05-01, 2-7-05)
ARTICLE II. SMOKING AND VAPING PROHIBITED
Sec. 13-23. Definitions.
   (a)   Smoking or vaping means possessing a cigarette, e-cigarette, cigar, or
pipe that contains tobacco or any other product that is lighted or burning;
lighting a cigarette, e-cigarette, cigar, or pipe that contains tobacco or any
other burning product that is contained in a pipe, cigar, cigarette and e-
cigarette.
   (b)   City building means any building or structure owned, managed,
operated, and/or leased by the City of Fremont.
(Ord. O-18-04, 4-16-18)
Sec. 13-24. Smoking prohibited locations.
   (a)   A person shall not smoke or use tobacco products in any city-owned:
park, outdoor athletic complex, linear park, trail, pathway, cemetery, beach,
or city owned parking lots when used for community events.
   (b)   No person shall smoke in any city building.
(Ord. O-18-04, 4-16-18)
Sec. 13-25. Signs.
   Signs may be posted in the locations listed in Sec.
13-24 where smoking and the use of tobacco products are prohibited, but the
absence of posted signs does not invalidate this article.
(Ord. O-18-04, 4-16-18)
Sec. 13-26. Violations and penalties.
   A person who violates or fails to comply with this article shall be subject
to any one or more of the following:
   (a)   Being asked to stop smoking or using the tobacco product.
   (b)   Being asked to leave the premises.
   (c)   Being responsible for a civil infraction punishable by a fine of not
more than fifty dollars ($50.00) for the first offense, one-hundred dollars
($100.00) for the second offense, and two- hundred dollars ($200.00) for the
third offense and thereafter.
(Ord. O-18-04, 4-16-18)

PARKS.
