   Article I. In General.
Sec. 14-1. Dedication of block number 25 as public park.
   Block number 25 of the City of Fremont, as appears by the recorded plat
thereof, is hereby dedicated as a public park to be used as such subject to the
rights of the city at any future time, to erect upon such block any public
buildings or to convey or lease the whole or any part thereof, to any
municipal, educational, philanthropic, library, scientific or other corporation
of a public character for the purpose of erecting any public buildings thereon.
(5-13-07, § 1)
Article II. Rules and Regulations.
Division 1. Generally.
Sec. 14-2. Definitions.
   For the purposes of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall have
the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section:
   Director. The Superintendent of Public Works or any person designated by the
Superintendent as in charge of any park area and its activities and to whom all
park attendants or employees of such area are responsible.
   Park. A park, reservation, playground, beach, recreation center or any other
area owned or used by the City and devoted to active or passive recreation.
   Vehicle. Any means of conveyance, whether mechanically- or motor-powered,
animal or animal-drawn, or self-propelled by the rider thereupon. The term
shall include any trailer in tow of any size, kind or description.
(7- -55, § 2; Ord. No. O-07-03, 8-20-07)
Sec. 14-3. Hours of operation.
   Except for unusual and unforeseen emergencies, parks shall be open to the
public every day of the year during designated hours. The opening and closing
hours for each individual park shall be posted therein for public information.
(7- -55, § 9)
Sec. 14-4. Closing of certain areas.
   Any section or part of any park may be declared closed to the public by the
city manager at any time and for any interval of time, either temporarily or at
regular and stated intervals, daily or otherwise, and either entirely or merely
to certain uses, as the city manager shall find reasonably necessary.
(7- -55, § 9)
Sec. 14-5. Enforcement powers and duties of city manager and park attendants
generally.
   (a)   Officials.  The city manager and park attendants shall, in connection
with their duties imposed by law, diligently enforce the provisions of this
chapter.
   (b)   Ejectment. The city manager and any park attendant shall have the
authority to eject from the park any person acting in violation of this
chapter.
   (c)   Seizure of property. The city manager and any park attendant shall
have the authority to seize and confiscate any property, thing or device in the
park or used in violation of this chapter.
(7- -55, § 10)
Sec. 14-6. Lost and found articles.
   The finding of lost articles by park attendants shall be reported to the
city manager, who shall make every reasonable effort to locate the owners. The
city manager shall make every reasonable effort to find articles reported as
lost.
(7- -55, § 9)
Sec. 14-7. Use of Fremont Lake Park for camping.
   The Fremont Lake Park may be used for camping by the public under such rules
and regulations and upon the payment of such fees as may be from time to time
established by the city manager.
Sec. 14-8. Exhibition of permit.
   No person shall fail to produce and exhibit any permit from the city manager
he claims to have upon request of any authorized person who shall desire to
inspect such permit for the purpose of enforcing compliance with any
regulation.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-9. Disturbing, etc., person occupying area, etc., under authority of a
permit.
   No person shall disturb or interfere unreasonably with any person or party
occupying any area or participating in any activity under the authority of a
permit.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-10. Advertising.
   Unless authorized by the city council, no person shall announce, advertise
or call the public attention in any way to any article or service for sale or
hire.
(7- -55, § 8)
As to distribution of handbills, circulars, etc., see 13-11 of this Code.
Sec. 14-11. Climbing trees; sitting, etc., on monuments, etc.
   No person shall climb any tree or walk, stand or sit upon monuments, vases,
fountains, railings, fences, or gun carriages or upon any other property not
designated or customarily used for such purposes.
(7- -55, § 3)
Sec. 14-12. Domestic animals generally.
   No person shall cause the entry of a dog or other domestic animal into areas
other than automobile parking concourses and walks immediately adjacent thereto
and such other areas as may be clearly marked by signs bearing the words
"domestic animals permitted in this area." Nothing herein shall be construed as
permitting dogs running at large. All dogs in those areas where such animals
are permitted shall be restrained at all times on adequate leashes not greater
than fifteen feet in length.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-13. Domestic animals running at large; discharge of firearms.
   No person shall permit any domestic animal to run at large within any park,
nor shall any person discharge therein any firearm of any kind or description.
(5-25-36, § 12)
As to discharge of firearms generally, see 13-14 of this Code.
Sec. 14-14. Dress; "properly clothed" defined.
   No person shall appear at any place in other than proper clothing. With the
exception of the restricted bathing areas, "properly clothed" shall be
construed to prohibit the wearing of trunks or clothing that does not cover the
upper portion of the body.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-15. Entering prohibited areas.
   No person shall enter an area posted as "closed to the public," nor shall
any person use or abut the use of any area in violation of posted notices.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-16. Presence in area reserved for opposite sex.
   No person shall occupy any seat or bench or enter into or loiter or remain
in any pavilion or other park structure or section thereof which may be
reserved and designated for the use of the opposite sex. An exception shall be
made for children not over five years of age.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-17. Erection of structures.
   No person shall construct or erect any building or structure of whatever
kind whether permanent or temporary in character or run or string any public
service utility into, upon or across such lands, except on special written
permit issued hereunder.
(7- -55, § 3)
Sec. 14-18. Fires; scattering of flammable materials.
   No person shall build or attempt to build a fire except in such areas and
under such regulations as may be designated by the city manager. No person
shall drop, throw or otherwise scatter lighted matches, burning cigarettes or
cigars, tobacco, paper or other inflammable material within any park or on any
highway, road or street abutting or contiguous thereto.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-19. Fireworks and explosives.
   Unless a written permit is first obtained from the city council, no person
shall bring or have in his possession or set off or otherwise cause to explode
or discharge or burn any firecracker, torpedo, rocket or other fireworks or
explosives of inflammable material or discharge them or throw them into any
such area from land or highway adjacent thereto. This prohibition includes any
substance, compound, mixture or article that in conjunction with any other
substance or compound would be dangerous from any of the foregoing standpoints.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-20. Gambling.
   No person shall gamble or participate in or abet any game of chance.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-21. Treatment of animals, birds, reptiles, etc.
   No person shall hunt, molest, harm, frighten, kill, trap, chase, tease,
shoot or throw missiles at any animal, reptile or bird; nor shall he remove or
have in his possession the young of any wild animal or the eggs or nest or
young of any reptile or bird; nor shall he collect, remove, have in his
possession, give away, sell or offer to sell, buy or offer to buy or accept as
a gift any specimen alive or dead of any of the group of tree snails. Exception
to the foregoing is made in that snakes known to be deadly poisonous, such as
rattle snakes, moccasins, coral snakes or other deadly reptiles, may be killed
on sight.
   No person shall give or offer or attempt to give to any animal or bird any
tobacco, alcohol or other known noxious substances.
(7- -55, § 3)
Sec. 14-22. Hunting generally; use, possession, etc., of weapons; trapping;
shooting into park.
   No person shall hunt, trap or pursue wild life at any time. No person shall
use, carry or possess firearms of any description or air rifles, spring-guns,
bows and arrows, slings or any other form of weapons potentially inimical to
wild life and dangerous to human safety or any instrument that can be loaded
with and fire blank cartridges or any kind of trapping device. Shooting into
park areas from beyond park boundaries is forbidden.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-23. Bringing intoxicating beverage into park; being under influence of
intoxicating liquor.
   No person shall bring alcoholic beverages into a park, nor shall any person
drink alcoholic beverages at any time in the park or be under the influence of
intoxicating liquor.
(7- -55, § 7)
As to alcoholic beverages generally, see 13-1 to 13-3 of this Code.
Sec. 14-24. Loitering; boisterous, etc., language; disorderly conduct.
   No person shall sleep on the seats, benches or other areas or engage in
loud, boisterous, threatening, abusive, insulting or indecent language or
engage in any disorderly conduct or behavior tending to a breach of the public
peace.
(7- -55, § 7)
As to disorderly persons generally, see 13-10 of this Code.
Sec. 14-25. Picnicking areas generally.
   (a)   No person shall picnic or lunch in a place other than those designated
for that purpose. Attendants shall have the authority to regulate the
activities in such areas when necessary to prevent congestion and to secure the
maximum use for the comfort and convenience of all. Visitors shall comply with
any directions given to achieve this end.
   (b)   Use of the individual fireplaces together with tables and benches
follows the rule of the first come, first served.
   (c)   No person shall use any portion of the picnic areas or of any of the
buildings or structures therein for the purpose of holding picnics to the
exclusion of other persons, nor shall any person use such area facilities for
an unreasonable length of time if the facilities are crowded.
   (d)   No person shall leave a picnic area before the fire is completely
extinguished and before all trash in the nature of boxes, papers, cans,
bottles, garbage and other refuse is placed in the disposal receptacles where
provided. If no such trash receptacles are available, then refuse and trash
shall be carried away from the park area by the picnicker to be properly
disposed of elsewhere.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-26. Pollution of water.
   No person shall throw, discharge or otherwise place or cause to be placed in
the waters of any fountain, pond, lake, stream, bay or other body of water in
or adjacent to any park or any tributary, stream, storm sewer or drain flowing
into such waters any substances, matter or thing, liquid or solid, which will
or may result in the pollution of such waters.
(7- -55, § 4)
Sec. 14-27. Public speeches, meetings, etc. – Generally.
   No person shall deliver any oration, address, speech, sermon or lecture in
any such park, nor shall any public meeting be held therein unless permission
shall have been first obtained from the city council.
(5-25-36, § 10)
Sec. 14-28. Same – Permission to use Fremont Lake Park.
   Upon application being made therefor, the city council may grant to any
reputable organization the exclusive use of the whole or any part of the park
at Fremont Lake for the purpose of holding any picnic, meeting or other lawful
celebration therein including public speeches or addresses, which grant shall
include the right to grant lawful concessions, subject to such regulations as
may from time to time be adopted by the city council.
(5-25-36, § 11)
Sec. 14-29. Disposal of refuse and garbage.
   No person shall bring in or dump, deposit or leave any bottles, broken
glass, ashes, paper, boxes, cans, dirt, rubbish, waste, garbage, refuse or
other trash. No such refuse or trash shall be placed in any waters in or
contiguous to any park or left anywhere on the grounds thereof but shall be
placed in the proper receptacles where these are provided; where receptacles
are not so provided, all such rubbish or waste shall be carried away from the
park by the person responsible for its presence and properly disposed of
elsewhere.
(7- -55, § 4)
Sec. 14-30. Maintenance of camp sites.
   All persons shall at all times keep the camp sites occupied by them in a
clean and sanitary condition.
(5-25-36, § 6)
Sec. 14-31. Removal of natural resources; excavations.
   No person shall dig or remove any beach sand whether submerged or not or any
soil, rock, stones, trees, shrubs, plants, down timber or other wood or
materials or make any excavation by tool, equipment, blasting or other means or
agency.
(7- -55, § 3)
Sec. 14-32. Removal, defacement, etc., of park property.
   No person shall willfully mark, deface, disfigure, injure, tamper with or
displace or remove, any buildings, bridges, tables, benches, fireplaces,
railings, paving or paving material, water lines or other public utilities or
parts or appurtenances thereof, signs, notices, placards whether temporary or
permanent, monuments, stakes, posts or other boundary markers or other
structures or equipment, facilities or park property or appurtenances
whatsoever, either real or personal.
(7- -55, § 3)
As to destruction of city property generally, see 13-7 to 13-9 of this Code.
Sec. 14-33. Destruction, etc., of property, etc.; posting of signs, bulletins
or notices.
   No person shall injure, deface, or molest any property or thing belonging
to, living or growing in and about any public park. No person shall pull up,
remove, damage, injure, destroy or in any manner molest or interfere with any
trees, shrubs, plants, signs, buildings or other structures of any name or
nature belonging to the city or situated in any of the public parks. No person
shall affix or inscribe any sign, poster, or inscription to, upon or against
any tree, structure, or property situated in any park or any street adjacent
thereto; except, that ordinary signs, bulletins or notices may be posted upon
such billboards as may be erected in such parks for that purpose by the city.
(5-25-36, § 9)
As to distribution of handbills, circulars, etc., see 13-11 of this Code.
Sec. 14-34. Maintenance and use of restrooms and washrooms.
   No person shall fail to cooperate in maintaining restrooms and washrooms in
a neat and sanitary condition. No person over the age of five years shall use
the restrooms and washrooms designated for the opposite sex.
(7- -55, § 3)
Sec. 14-35. Signs, placards, advertisements or inscriptions generally.
   No person shall paste, glue, tack or otherwise post any sign, placard,
advertisement or inscription whatever, nor shall any person erect or cause to
be erected any sign whatever on any public lands or highways or roads adjacent
to a park.
(7- -55, § 8)
Sec. 14-36. Solicitation of money.
   Except for community school sponsored activities, no person shall solicit
alms or contributions for any purpose, whether for public or private use.
(7- -55, § 7)
Sec. 14-37. Trees and shrubs – Injury; removal; attachment of devices; digging
or disturbing.
   No person shall damage, cut, carve, transplant or remove any tree or plant
or injure the bark or pick the flowers or seeds of any tree or plant; nor shall
any person attach any rope, wire or other contrivance to any tree or plant. A
person shall not dig in or otherwise disturb grass areas or in any other way
injure or impair the natural beauty or usefulness of any area.
(7- -55, § 3)
For charter provisions as to trees and shrubs in parks, see Char., 2.2(19)
Sec. 14-38. Same – Hitching horses, etc.
   No person shall tie or hitch a horse or other animal to any tree or plant.
(7- -55, § 3)
Sec. 14-39. Vending and peddling.
   No person shall expose or offer for sale any article or thing, nor shall he
station or place any stand, cart or vehicle for the transportation, sale or
display of any such article or thing. Exception is here made as to any
regularly licensed concessionaire acting by and under the authority and
regulation of the city manager.
(7- -55, § 8)
As to sales by peddlers, etc., see 13-18 to 13-20 of this Code.
Division 2. Swimming.
Sec. 14-40. Designated areas.
   No person shall swim, bathe or wade in any waters or waterways in or
adjacent to any park, except in such waters and at such places as are provided
therefor and in compliance with such regulations as are herein set forth or may
be hereafter adopted; nor shall any person frequent any waters or places
customarily designated for the purpose of swimming or bathing or congregate
thereat when such activity is prohibited by the city manager upon a finding
that such use of the water would be dangerous or otherwise inadvisable.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-41. Hours.
   No person shall frequent any waters or places designated for the purpose of
swimming or bathing or congregate thereat, except between such hours of the day
as shall be designated by the city manager for such purposes for each
individual area.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-42. Tents, etc., in bathing area.
   No person shall erect, maintain, use or occupy on or in any beach or bathing
area any tent, shelter or structure of any kind unless there shall be an
unobstructed view into such tent, shelter or structure from at least two sides;
nor shall any guy wire, rope or extension or exterior brace or support be
connected or fastened from any such structure to any other structure, stake,
reel or other object outside thereof.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-43. Costumes; areas where bathing suit may be worn.
   No person shall allow himself to be so covered with a bathing suit as to
indecently expose his person or call forth merited criticism. No person shall
appear in bathing costume at any place in the parks, except within the limits
of designated bathing places or areas, and all bathing costumes shall conform
to commonly accepted standards.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-44. Dressing areas.
   No person shall dress or undress on any beach or in any vehicle, toilet or
other place, except in such bathing houses or structures as may be provided for
that purpose.
(7- -55, § 6)
Division 3. Traffic.
As to motor vehicles and traffic generally, see ch. 12 of this Code.
Sec. 14-45. Establishment of hours when traffic is not permitted.
   The City Manager or his/her designee may establish the times and/or days
during which any or all vehicular traffic, as defined in Section
14-2 of this chapter, in any public park shall cease or be temporarily
curtailed.
(5-25-36, § 8; Ord. No. O-07-03, 8-20-07)
Sec. 14-46. Obedience to officers and employees; power of officers and
employees to direct traffic, etc.
   No person shall fail to obey any police, traffic or other law enforcement
officers and City Parks or Public Works Department employees. Such officers and
employees are hereby authorized and instructed to direct traffic whenever and
wherever needed in the parks and on the highways, streets or roads immediately
adjacent thereto in accordance with the provisions of these regulations and
such supplementary rules and regulations as may be issued subsequently by the
City Manager.
(7- -55, § 5; Ord. No. O-07-03, 8-20-07)
Sec. 14-47. Areas in which vehicles my be operated.
   No person shall drive or operate any vehicle, as defined in Section
14-2 of this chapter, on any area of any park, except the paved or graveled
(hard-surfaced) park roadways or parking areas or such other areas as may on
occasion be specifically designated as temporary roadway or parking areas by
the City Manager.
   Exceptions are made for the use of the following vehicles in the following
locations:
   (a)   Baby carriages, strollers or similar devices being properly used to
transport infants or small children in any area of any park.
   (b)   Powered or self-propelled wheelchairs or similar mobility devices
being properly used by those persons that have a physical characteristic
categorized as a handicap, which limits ambulation or necessitates the use of a
wheelchair for mobility, or a person who is blind, in any area of any park.
   (c)   Self-propelled (non-motorized) bicycles, tricycles, skateboards,
skates (roller, in-line, etc.), scooters, coasters or similar devices being
properly used on designated paved sections or segments of the Fremont Area Town
and Country Path, as well as within the Fremont Skate/Bike Park.
   (d)   Self-propelled (non-motorized) bicycles being properly used on un-
paved sections of trails or other non-roadway or pathway areas of Branstrom
Park, but only if being used as part of or during an actual event or race
approved in advance by the City Council. The City Council may grant approval,
but for no more than two (2) such uses each calendar year. For those events or
races conducted in or upon that portion of Branstrom Park owned by the Fremont
Public School (FPS) District, advanced approval shall be required from the FPS
Board of Education. The City Council shall place appropriate conditions on its
approval for such uses to minimize damage to the Park's ecosystem and minimize
liability exposure for the City. Use of the same or other un-paved sections of
trails or other non-roadway paths in any park for practice or training for such
events or races is prohibited.
   (e)   Utility vehicles, such as golf carts, quads, "Gators", "Mules" or
other similar motorized vehicle may be used by registered campers, or their
direct relatives, any of whom are at least nineteen (19) years of age and
possess a valid motor vehicle drivers license, only within the Fremont Lake
Park Campground, but not within the remainder of Fremont Lake Park or upon any
public roadway or the non-motorized Fremont Area Town & Country Path. Exception
is made for those persons with a recognized mobility handicap as defined in (b)
above who receive annual written authorization from the Fremont Chief of Police
as qualifying for a State of Michigan motor vehicle handicap license plate or
vehicle interior placard. Said exception shall only permit such qualified
person from using such above-identified utility vehicle to travel from the
campground across a designated bridge spanning Darling Creek, along a
designated route and crossing a public roadway at a right angle (perpendicular)
to such roadway in order to access City-operated boat docking facilities along
Fremont Lake within Fremont Lake Park. Said route and bridge designations shall
be made by the Chief of Police in consultation with and the consent of the City
Manager.
   (f)   Authorized City Public Works Department or other vehicles providing
maintenance or other services within or for City parks.
   (g)   Emergency vehicles including, but not necessarily limited to, those
such as police, fire, rescue, first responder or ambulance services.
   The use of vehicles in any City park as described in the above exceptions is
not a guaranteed right of any person. Said use shall be considered a privilege,
subject to the proper and safe use of said vehicles at all times. Said
privilege may be revoked temporarily or permanently by action of the Chief of
Police, City Manager or Superintendent of Public Works if, in their opinion,
the continued use of a said vehicle by said person would be improper, dangerous
to other persons, or effect the health, safety or welfare of the City's Parks
or the community at large. Improper or unauthorized use of vehicles by persons
within the City's Parks is subject to enforcement actions in Section
14-5 of this chapter "Enforcement Powers and Duties of City Manager and Park
Attendants Generally" and may also result in a civil infraction citation and/or
fine as authorized in Chapter 5.1 of this Code "Civil Infractions, Citations
and Penalties." A separate offense shall be deemed committed each day during or
on which a violation or noncompliance occurs or continues, unless otherwise
provided. Civil fines or penalties for such offenses shall be as periodically
designated by Resolution of the City Council, but shall in no case be less than
the following:
      1st Offense         $ 90.00
      2nd Offense         150.00
      3rd or more Offense      250.00 each offense
(7- -55, § 5; Ord. No. O-07-03, 8-20-07)
Division 4. Boating.
Sec. 14-48. Areas; operation generally.
   No person shall bring into or operate any boat, raft or other watercraft,
whether motor powered or not, upon any waters, except at places designated for
boating by the city manager. Such activity shall be in accordance with
applicable regulations as are now or may hereafter be adopted.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-49. Handling of boat.
   No person shall navigate, direct or handle any boat in such a manner as to
unjustifiably or unnecessarily annoy or frighten or endanger the occupants of
any other boat.
(7- -55, § 6)
Sec. 14-50. Use of city boat landing – Generally.
   The City boat landing at Second Lake shall be used only for the launching of
small boats not equipped with gas motors of any type; except electric trolling
motors are permitted provided same are operated at "no-wake" speed. The use of
said boat landing shall be for no other purpose except as authorized by the
City Manager.
(7-10-61, § 1; Ord. No. O-08-05, 6-2-08)
Sec. 14-51. Same – Camping; overnight anchoring; storage; fires; litter, etc.
   No person shall use the city landing for camping, for the anchoring or
tieing up of boats overnight or for the storage of fish shanties, boating
equipment or other personal property. No fires shall be built upon the
launching area and all persons using the area shall keep the premises free from
litter, rubbish and trash.
(7-10-61, § 3)
As to fire protection generally, see ch. 9 of this Code. As to refuse and
garbage generally, see ch. 16.
Secs. 14-52 to 14-63. Repealed by ordinances adopted 6-16-80.
Division 5. Restricting Smoking and the Use of Tobacco Products in City Parks
Sec. 14-64. Definitions.
   As used in this section:
   (a)   Smoking or smoke means the carrying by a person of a lighted cigar,
cigarette, pipe or other lighted smoking device.
   (b)   Tobacco product means a preparation of tobacco to be inhaled, chewed,
sucked or placed in a person's mouth. (Ord. No. O-02-04, 4-15-02)
Sec. 14-65. Prohibited Acts.
   A person shall not smoke or use tobacco products in designated non-smoking
areas in public parks, which are owned or operated by the City of Fremont. The
City Council shall designate non-smoking areas from time to time by resolution.
(Ord. No. O-02-04, 4-15-02)
Sec. 14-66. Signs.
   Signs shall be posted in the public parks delineating the areas where
smoking and the use of tobacco products in such parks is prohibited. (Ord. No.
O-02-04, 4-15-02)
Sec. 14-67. Violations and Penalties.
   (a)   A person who violates or fails to comply with this Section shall be
subject to any one or more of the following:
      (1)   Being asked to stop smoking or using the tobacco product;
      (2)   Being asked to leave the premises;
      (3)   Being responsible for a municipal civil infraction and subject to
the civil fines set forth in the Schedule of Civil fines of this code and any
other relief that may be imposed by the Court. Each act of violation and each
day upon which such violation occurs shall constitute a separate violation.
   (b)   The city may establish the times during which all traffic in any
public park shall cease. (Ord. No. O-02-04, 4-15-02)
CHAPTER 15.
BUILDING AND BUILDING REGULATIONS.
For charter provision as to the regulation of buildings, etc., see Char., § 2.2
(28).
For state law as to plumbing generally, see M.C.L.A. §§ 338.3511 - 338.3569.
As to building generally, see ch. 5 of this Code. As to electricity, see ch. 8.
As to water and sewers generally, see ch. 21. As to private sewage disposal
systems, see §§ 21-62 to 21-82.
Article I. In General
§
15-1.   State construction code; enforcing agency.
§
15-2.   City to be governed by state housing statutes.
§
15-3.   Terms generally.
§
15-4.   Specific definitions.
§
15-5.   State building code; enforcing agency.
§
15-6.   State mechanical code; enforcing agency.
§
15-7.   State plumbing code; enforcing agency.
§
15-8.   State electrical code; enforcing agency.
§
15-9.   Floodplain management provisions of the state construction code.
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 15-1. State construction code; enforcing agency.
   Pursuant to the provisions of Section 9 of Act No. 230 of the Public Acts of
1972 (MCL 125.1501, MSA 5.2949(9)), as amended, the persons or agencies
designated by the city council are hereby designated as the enforcing agency to
discharge the responsibilities of the city under Act No. 230 of the Public Acts
of 1972 (MCL 125.1501 et seq., MSA 5.2949(1) et seq.), as amended. Applications
for building and other permits required by the state construction code shall be
made to persons or agencies designated by the city council.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
   State law reference- State construction code act of 1972, MCL 125.1501 et
seq., MSA 5.2949(1) et seq.
Sec. 15-2. City to be governed by state housing statutes.
   The city is hereby brought within the state housing law, Act No. 167 of the
Public Acts of 1917 (MCL 125.401 et seq., MSA 5.2771 et seq.), as amended.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
Sec. 15-3. Terms generally.
   (a)   Scope. Unless otherwise expressly stated, the following terms, words,
and phrases shall apply to this
Chapter 15 and shall have the meanings described in this section and when used
anywhere within
Chapter 15 of this code.
   (b)   Interchangeability. Words stated in the present tense include the
future; words stated in the masculine gender include the feminine and neuter;
the singular number includes the plural and the plural, the singular.
   (c)   Terms defined in other codes. Where terms are not defined in this code
and are defined in the building code, fire code, zoning code, plumbing code,
mechanical code, electrical code or the fire code, such terms shall have the
same meaning as ascribed to them as in those codes.
   (d)   Terms not defined. When terms are not defined by this section, such
terms shall have ordinarily accepted meanings as the context implies.
   (e)   Parts. Whenever the words "dwelling unit," “dwelling”, "premises,"
"structure," "rooming house," "rooming unit" or "story" are stated in this
code, they shall be construed as though they were followed by the words "or any
part thereof."
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
Sec. 15-4. Specific definitions.
   As used in this article:
   (a)   Abandoned/disabled motor vehicle means a motor vehicle which is
dismantled, in whole or in part, and/or which is mechanically unable to operate
as the result of a mechanical defect or malfunction, a mechanical defect or
malfunction includes, but is not limited to; deflated or missing tires; a
vehicle resting on supports other than inflated tires; missing or damaged
lights, windshield, or battery. The absence of minor and nonessential parts,
such as antennas, or ornaments, hubcaps, etc., shall not cause a vehicle to be
deemed dismantled and disabled. Any vehicle which is not capable of being
licensed for operation on streets, alleys or highways shall be deemed to be
disabled. Any vehicle that does not have a current license plate displayed
shall be deemed to be abandoned.
   (b)   Absentee landlord means the owner of property that is leased, assigned
or rented to another and who lives more than forty (40) miles from the Fremont
city limits.
   (c)   Accessory structure means any structure which is used exclusively for
an accessory use.
   (d)   Approved means approved by the manager of code compliance.
   (e)   Attractive nuisance means and consists of items in a structure or on a
premises, which may prove detrimental to children, this includes, but is not
limited to: any abandoned wells, shafts, basements or excavations,
refrigerators or abandoned/disabled motor vehicles, open and vacant structures,
structurally unsound fences, buildings or structures, lumber, trash, debris,
hazardous trees, broken and/or hanging tree limbs, or hazardous vegetation.
   (f)   Basement means a portion of a structure or building which is partly or
completely below ground.
   (g)   Bathroom means a room containing a lavatory, toilet, and a bathtub or
shower.
   (h)   Bedroom means any room or space used or intended to be used for
sleeping purposes.
   (i)   Building means any structure used or intended for use or occupancy by
persons, materials, or animals.
   (j)   Building code means the building code, as adopted in
Chapter 15 of the City of Fremont Codified Ordinances and in effect at the time
of an alleged violation.
   (k)   Certificate of compliance means a certificate issued by the manager of
code compliance for any rental dwelling or unit, which indicates the holder is
in compliance with this code. A certificate of compliance will be issued after
all required inspection and registration fees are paid and after the rental
dwelling has been inspected and determined to be in complete compliance with
this code. A certificate of compliance shall expire automatically at the end of
two (2) years for rental dwellings that have three (3) or more units or rooming
houses and have received any violations of this code during the most recent
inspection of the premises. A certificate of compliance shall expire at the end
of three (3) years for rental dwellings with one (1) or two (2) units and
rental dwellings with three (3) or more units or rooming houses which have not
received any violations of this code during the most recent inspection of the
premises, except as otherwise provided in this code.
   (l)   Code compliance officer means a duly authorized representative of the
manager of code compliance.
   (m)   Driveway means space on a lot, not to exceed twelve (12) feet in
width, except where such space forms the apron to the entrance of a garage,
specifically designated and used for the movement of motor vehicles, trailers
and watercraft to or from the lot or to or from a public street.
   (n)   Dwelling means any house, building, structure, tent, shelter, trailer,
mobile home, or vehicle, or portion thereof, except railroad cars on tracks or
rights-of-ways, which is occupied in whole or in part as the home, residence or
living or sleeping place for one (1) or more persons, either permanently or
intermittently. A house trailer or other vehicle, when occupied or used as a
dwelling, shall be subject to all the provisions of this code, except that a
house trailer or other vehicle, duly licensed as a vehicle, may be occupied or
used as a dwelling for reasonable periods of time without being subject to the
provisions of this code for dwellings, where such occupation is otherwise
lawful, and when it is located in a park or place designated or licensed for
their use provided that such parking sites are equipped with adequate safety
and sanitary facilities.
   (o)   Dwelling unit means a single unit providing complete, independent
living facilities for one or more persons, including permanent provisions for
living, sleeping, eating, cooking and sanitation.
   (p)   Efficiency dwelling unit means any room having cooking facilities and
used for combined living, dining and sleeping purposes.
   (q)   Electrical code means the electrical code as adopted by this chapter
and in effect at the time of an alleged violation.
   (r)   Emergency means a situation where a condition exists which is
immediately dangerous to the life, limb, property or safety of the public or
the occupants of a dwelling and/or premises.
   (s)   Exterior property means the open space on the premises and on
adjoining property under the control of owners or operators of such premises.
   (t)   Extermination means the control and elimination of insects, rats or
other pests by eliminating their harborage places; by removing or making
inaccessible materials that serve as their food; by poison spraying,
fumigating, trapping or by any other approved and safe pest elimination
methods.
   (u)   Family means:
      (1)   An individual or two (2) or more persons related by blood, marriage
or adoption, together with not more than two (2) other persons who are living
together as a single housekeeping unit or dwelling unit with no additional
roomers; or
      (2)   Not more than four (4) persons not related by blood, marriage or
adoption in a C or multiple district, as defined in the zoning code, who are
living together as a single housekeeping unit or dwelling unit with no
additional roomers.
   (v)   Fence means any wall (except a retaining wall), screen, partition or
similar structure existing on a yard or parcel of land, which encloses land;
divides land into distinct portions; separates contiguous properties; obstructs
the passage of light or air into adjacent land or obstructs the vision of
motorists on or near public roads.
   (w)   Front yard means the space on a lot, extending the full width of the
lot and situated between the street line and the front line of the main
structure on the lot. However, where a lot is located at the intersection of
two (2) or more streets, the front yard shall, in addition, include the space
on the lot extending the full width or length of the lot and situated between
the street line and the side line of the main structure on the lot.
   (x)   Garbage means the animal or vegetable waste resulting from the
handling, preparation, cooking and consumption of food.
   (y)   Guardrail means a building component or a system of building
components located at or near the open sides of elevated walking surfaces that
minimizes the possibility of a fall from the walking surface to a lower level.
   (z)   Guest means any person hiring or allowed to occupy a room for living
or sleeping purposes.
   (aa)   Guest room means any room used or intended to be used by a guest for
sleeping purposes. Every one-hundred (100) square feet of superficial floor
area in a dormitory shall be considered to be a guest room.
   (bb)   Habitable space means space in a structure for living, sleeping,
eating or cooking. Bathrooms, toilet rooms, closets, halls, storage or utility
spaces, and similar areas are not considered habitable spaces.
   (cc)   Hazard to health or safety means any unsafe structure or premises, as
defined in Subsec. 10-39(a) of this code.
   (dd)   Health officer means the county health officer or any of his or her
authorized representatives.
   (ee)   Hedge means a dense row of low branching trees, shrubs, vines or
other plants which encloses land, divides land into distinct portions,
separates contiguous properties, obstructs the passage of light and air into
adjacent land or obstructs the vision of motorists on or near public roads.
   (ff)   Hot water means water at a temperature of one-hundred (100) degrees
Fahrenheit or greater.
   (gg)   Imminent danger means a condition that could cause serious or life-
threatening injury or death at any time.
   (hh)   Infestation means the presence, within or contiguous to, a structure
or premises of insects, rats, vermin or other pests.
   (ii)   Labeled means those devices, equipment, appliances, or materials to
which have been affixed a label, seal, symbol or other identifying mark of a
nationally recognized testing laboratory, inspection agency or other
organization concerned with product evaluation that maintains periodic
inspection of the production of the above-labeled items and by whose label the
manufacturer attests to compliance with applicable nationally recognized
standards.
   (jj)   Landlord means the owner or manager of property that is leased,
assigned or rented to another.
   (kk)   Let for occupancy or let means to permit, provide or offer possession
or occupancy of a dwelling, dwelling unit, rooming unit, building, premise or
structure by a person who is or is not the legal owner of record thereof,
pursuant to a written or unwritten lease, agreement or license, or pursuant to
a recorded or unrecorded agreement of contract for the sale of land.
   (ll)   Lodging house means any structure or portion thereof containing guest
rooms where rent is paid in money, goods or services and having an occupant
load not exceeding twenty (20) people.
   (mm)   Manager of code compliance means the manager of the office of code
compliance of the department of planning and neighborhood development,
including his or her duly authorized or designated representative, unless a
contrary intent is clearly shown.
   (nn)   Mechanical code means the mechanical code, as adopted in this chapter
and in effect at the time of an alleged violation.
   (oo)   Motor vehicle means any tracked or trackless, self propelled or
mechanically operated vehicle, whether operable or not, including but not
limited to automobiles, buses, trucks, vans, wreckers or road construction
equipment or machinery.
   (pp)   Multiple dwelling means a dwelling containing three (3) or more
dwelling units.
   (qq)   Occupancy means the purpose for which a building or portion thereof
is used or occupied.
   (rr)   Occupant means any individual living or sleeping in a structure or
having possession of a space within a structure.
   (ss)   Occupied space means the total area of all buildings or structures on
any lot or parcel of ground projected on a horizontal plane, excluding
permitted projections as allowed by this code.
   (tt)   One-family dwelling means a dwelling occupied by only one (1) family,
and so designed and arranged as to provide cooking and kitchen accommodations
for one (1) family only, also called a single-family dwelling.
   (uu)   Openable area means that part of a window, skylight or door which is
available for unobstructed ventilation and/or egress and which opens directly
to the outdoors.
   (vv)   Owner means any person, corporation, partnership, trust, limited
liability company, or D.B.A. who has ownership of a parcel of property as
evidenced by a deed, a land contract, or some other documentation that shows a
legal interest in a parcel of property.
   (ww)   Owner occupied dwelling means a dwelling which a person both owns as
a title holder or land contract purchaser and lives in as his or her home.
   (xx)   Person means an individual, corporation, partnership, limited
liability company, or any other group or legal entity acting as a unit.
   (yy)   Placard means a notice posted on a structure, building or dwelling.
   (zz)   Plumbing code means the plumbing code, as adopted by this chapter and
in effect at the time of an alleged violation.
   (aaa)   Premises means a lot, plot or parcel of land, including any building
or structure thereon.
   (bbb)   Public nuisance means:
      (1)   Any public nuisance known at common law or in equity.
      (2)   Any attractive nuisance in a building or on a premises that may be
detrimental to children. This includes, but is not limited to:
         a.   Any abandoned wells, shafts, basements or excavations;
         b.   Refrigerators or abandoned/disabled motor vehicles as defined in
sec. 10-4;
         c.   Structurally unsound fences or structures; or
         d.   Lumber, trash, debris, hazardous trees, broken and/or hanging
tree limbs or hazardous vegetation.
      (3)   Whatever is dangerous to human life or is detrimental to health.
      (4)   Overcrowding a room with occupants as defined in the building code.
      (5)   Insufficient ventilation or illumination as specified in this code.
      (6)   Inadequate or unsanitary sewage or plumbing facilities
      (7)   Uncleanliness, as determined by the county health officer or the
manager of code compliance.
      (8)   Whatever renders air, food or drink unwholesome or detrimental to
the health of human beings, as determined by the health officer.
      (9)   Hazardous or unsanitary premises.
   (ccc)   Recorded land contract, deed, mortgage, etc. means a deed, land
contract, mortgage and/or any other document of title used to establish
ownership of real property, which has been certified as recorded with the
county register of deeds in which the property is located.
   (ddd)   Recreational vehicle means any self-propelled or mechanically
operated vehicle, whether operable or not, including but not limited to
motorcycles, snowmobiles, dune buggies, go-carts, all terrain vehicles, motor
homes and campers.
   (eee)   Registered agent means the person registered with the office of code
compliance who represents the owner of a parcel of property. Person includes
any individual, corporation, partnership, trust, limited liability company, or
D.B.A.
   (fff)   Registered owner means the owner registered with the office of code
compliance for a parcel of property. Registered owner includes any individual,
corporation, partnership, trust, limited liability company, or D.B.A.
   (ggg)   Rental means any premises, dwelling, dwelling unit, or rooming unit
which is not occupied on a daily basis by the owner(s), and which is offered to
let, to hire, or to assign for a period of more than thirty (30) days to any
person(s) for any or no consideration.
      (1)   If any premises, dwelling, dwelling unit, or rooming unit is
occupied by any person(s) other than the owner(s) of record, his or her spouse,
or their minor dependents, it shall be presumed to be a rental property.
      (2)   The owner(s) of record shall be established by legal instruments
recorded with the register of deeds, including but not limited to warranty
deeds or land contracts.
   (hhh)   Rooming house means a building arranged or occupied for lodging,
with or without meals, for compensation and not occupied as a one (1)- or two
(2)-family dwelling.
   (iii)   Rooming unit means any room or group of rooms forming a single
habitable unit occupied or intended to be occupied for sleeping or living, but
not for cooking purposes.
   (jjj)   Strict liability offense means any offense for which the prosecution
is not required to prove criminal intent as a part of its case. It is enough to
prove that the defendant either did an act that was prohibited, or failed to do
an act that the defendant was legally required to do.
   (kkk)   Structure means the whole or part of something that is built or
constructed for use as a border, support, shelter, or building.
   (lll)   Substandard condition means any condition defined as substandard in
subsection 10-38(a)(1). Such condition does not make a building unsafe unless
so determined by the manager of code compliance or the county health officer.
   (mmm)   Taxpayer of record means the taxpayer listed with the City of
Fremont Assessor for a parcel of property, including any person, corporation,
partnership, trust, limited liability company, or D.B.A.
   (nnn)   Tenant means a person, corporation, partnership or group, whether or
not the legal owner of record, occupying a building or portion thereof as a
unit.
   (ooo)   Toilet room means a room containing a toilet or urinal and a
lavatory but no bathtub or shower.
   (ppp)   Trailer means any contrivance without means of self locomotion which
is designed to be towed by a motor vehicle for the purpose of transporting
property, people or animals.
   (qqq)   Trash means combustible and noncombustible waste materials, except
garbage. Trash includes the residue from burning wood, coal, coke and other
combustible materials as well as paper, rags, cartons, boxes, wood, excelsior,
rubber, leather, tree branches, yard trimmings, tin cans, metals, mineral
matter, glass, crockery and dust and other similar materials.
   (rrr)   Two (2)-family structure means a building that contains two (2)
dwelling units.
   (sss)   Unsafe means any condition defined as unsafe in Subsec. 10-39(a)(1)
through (10) of the Fremont City Code of Ordinances or by state statute.
   (ttt)   Ventilation means the natural or mechanical process of supplying
conditioned or unconditioned air to, or removing such air from, any building
space.
   (uuu)   Watercraft means any contrivance used or designed for operation and
the transportation of people or property on water, including but not limited to
boats, rafts, vessels, canoes, ships, motor vessels, motorboats, rowboats or
personal watercraft.
   (vvv)   Workmanlike means work executed and performed in a skilled and
professional manner, e.g. generally plumb, level, square, in line, undamaged
and without marring adjacent work.
   (www)   Yard means an open space on the same lot with a structure.
   (xxx)   Zoning code means the Fremont Joint Zoning Code, as amended, as
adopted in Chapter 22 of Fremont City Code of Ordinances.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
Sec. 15-5. State building code; enforcing agency.
   Pursuant to the provisions of the Michigan Building Code in accordance with
Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as amended, the building
inspector of the city is hereby designated as the enforcing agency to discharge
the responsibility of the city under Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as
amended, State of Michigan. The city assumes responsibility for the
administration and enforcement of said Act throughout its jurisdiction.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
Sec. 15-6. State mechanical code; enforcing agency.
   Pursuant to the provisions of the Michigan Mechanical Code in accordance
with Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as amended, the
mechanical inspector of the city is hereby designated as the enforcing agency
to discharge the responsibility of the city under Act 230, of the Public Acts
of 1972, as amended, State of Michigan. The city assumes responsibility for the
administration and enforcement of said Act throughout its jurisdiction.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
Sec. 15-7. State Plumbing Code; enforcing agency.
   Pursuant to the provisions of the Michigan Plumbing Code in accordance with
Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as amended, the plumbing
inspector of the city is hereby designated as the enforcing agency to discharge
the responsibility of the city under Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as
amended, State of Michigan. The city assumes responsibility for the
administration and enforcement of said Act throughout its jurisdiction.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
Sec. 15-8. State Electrical Code; enforcing agency.
   Pursuant to the provisions of the Michigan Electrical Code in accordance
with Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as amended, the
electrical inspector of the city is hereby designated as the enforcing agency
to discharge the responsibility of the city under Act 230, of the Public Acts
of 1972, as amended, State of Michigan. The city assumes responsibility for the
administration and enforcement of said Act throughout its jurisdiction.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
Sec. 15-9. Floodplain management provisions of the state construction code.
   (a)   Agency designated. Pursuant to the provisions of the state
construction code, in accordance with Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public
Acts of 1972, as amended, the Building Official of the City of Fremont is
hereby designated as the enforcing agency to discharge the responsibility of
the City of Fremont under Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as amended,
State of Michigan. The City of Fremont assumes responsibility for the
administration and enforcement of said Act throughout the corporate limits of
its jurisdiction.
   (b)   Code appendix enforced. Pursuant to the provisions of the state
construction code, in accordance with Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public
Acts of 1972, as amended, Appendix G of the Michigan Building Code shall be
enforced by the enforcing agency within the City of Fremont.
   (c)   Designation of regulated flood prone hazard areas. The Federal
Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) Flood Insurance Study (FIS) Entitled
"Newaygo County, Michigan (All Jurisdictions)" and dated 2-18-2015 and the
Flood Insurance Rate Map(s) (FIRMS) panel number(s) of 26123C; 0437D, 0439D,
0441D; and 0442D dated 2-18-2015 are adopted by reference for the purposes of
administration of the Michigan Construction Code, and declared to be a part of
Section 1612.3 of the Michigan Building Code, and to provide the content of the
"Flood Hazards" section of Table R301.2(1) of the Michigan Residential Code.
(Ord. No. O-18-01, 2-5-18)
CHAPTER 16.
REFUSE COLLECTION/RESOURCE RECOVERY.
§ 16-1.   Definitions
§ 16-2.   Deposit on Public or Private Property Generally
§ 16-3.   Sanitation of Premises; Preparation of Refuse for Collection

System

Other Waste

§ 16-10.   Replacement of Damaged/Lost Containers/Carts
§ 16-11.   Commercial and Industrial Collection
§ 16-12.   Schedule of Collections

§ 16-14.   Office Services of Contractor
§ 16-15.   Salvaging, Scavenging or Removing Materials Placed for Collection
