ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL.
Sec. 18-1. Spitting on or littering sidewalks.
   No person shall spit upon the sidewalks or leave any litter or unsightly
material thereon. (1-11-09, § 1.)
Sec. 18-2. Designation and use of underground conduit territory.
   All that part of Main Street situated between the intersections of Merchant
Avenue and Weaver Avenue is hereby declared to be and is designated as
underground and conduit territory in its use by the utility companies, and it
is declared to be unlawful to use this section of Main Street for the carrying
of telephone, electric light and all other wires in any other manner than by
means of an underground conduit, unless specifically authorized to do so by the
City Council. (12-13-15, § 1.)
For charter provisions as to use of streets and sidewalks by public utilities,
see Char. 2.2 (6), § 14.10.
For state law as to use of streets and sidewalks by public utilities generally,
see M.C.L.A. §§ 247.183 - 247.186, §§ 460.553 - 460.555.
Sec. 18-3. Encroachments or obstructions generally.
   Prohibited. Except as otherwise provided in this Code, no person shall place
or cause to be placed any real or personal property, except United States
postal boxes and motor vehicles properly parked in designated parking spaces,
upon or over any street, alley, sidewalk or public right-of-way in all
districts of the city, as hereinafter defined, without first having obtained a
permit therefor from the City Manager or his/her designee. (Ord. No. O-20-05,
9-21-20)
Sec. 18-4. Placing of building materials on street, sidewalk, etc.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or cause to be placed any
material for building purposes upon any sidewalk, street, alley or public
grounds within the city under a penalty as prescribed by section 1-6 after
being notified by the chief of police or any police officer to remove such
material; provided that the City Manager or his/her designee are authorized to
grant permission in writing to place and keep building materials in any places
mentioned as aforesaid; and provided, that such permission shall not extend to
a period beyond one (1) month from the time of granting the same, and shall not
authorize the obstruction of any sidewalk or crosswalk, and more than one-half
the driveway, opposite any lot. Any such permission may be revoked by the City
Manager or his/her designee.
   Any person to whom such permission shall be granted, as aforesaid, shall
cause all building material and rubbish arising from the same to be removed at
or before the time limited by the preceding paragraph or be subject to a
penalty as prescribed by section 1-6 for each day that such material shall
remain after the expiration of the time set out in the preceding paragraph.
(Ord. No. O-20-05, 9-21-20)
Sec. 18-5. Obstruction of gutters, ditches, etc.
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct, with sand, gravel, dirt,
rubbish, filth or other substances, any sluice, gutter, ditch or watercourse in
the city in front of or adjoining any lot or premises owned or occupied by such
person. In case the owner or occupant of any such lot or premises, who shall
have caused such obstruction, shall refuse or neglect to remove such
obstruction within twenty-four (24) hours after being notified to do so by the
City Manager and his/her designee, it shall be the duty of the City Manager to
remove such sand, gravel, dirt, filth or other obstruction, and the expense and
cost of such removal shall be assessed against the property where such sluice,
gutter, ditch or watercourse may be situated, and such expense and cost plus a
reasonable administration fee shall be collected as a special assessment
thereon. (Ord. No. O-20-05, 9-21-20)
 
Sec. 18-6. Trees and shrubs – Trimming branches overhanging street or sidewalk.
   The owner of any lot or parcel of land fronting on any street in the city
shall trim or cause to be trimmed the branches from all trees in the street in
front of such land and from the trees on such land overhanging the street, so
as to leave a clear height of ten (10) feet above the surface of the sidewalk
and fourteen (14) feet above the surface of the street unobstructed by branches
of such trees. If any owner of such land shall refuse or fail to comply with
the requirements of this section, it shall be the duty of the City Manager to
cause such trees to be trimmed so as to comply with the provisions hereof, at
the expense of the owner of such land, and such expense, together with costs of
suit, shall be collected before a court having jurisdiction. (Ord. O-10-03, 5-
3-10)
Sec. 18-7. Trees and shrubs – Permits to plant or remove in street right-of-
ways.
   (1)   Definitions. For the purposes of this section, the following words and
phrases shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this section:
   Park trees: Trees, shrubs, bushes and all other woody vegetation in public
parks and all other areas owned by the City.
   Private tree: All trees within the city other than park trees and street
trees.
   Street tree: Trees, shrubs, bushes and all other woody vegetation on land
lying on the street right-of-way on either side of all streets, avenues or ways
within the city.
   (2)   Duties generally of the City Manager and City Council. It shall be the
responsibility of the City Manager to develop and administer a plan for the
care, preservation, pruning, planting, replanting, removal or disposition of
street trees and park trees. Such plan will be reviewed and approved, from time
to time, by the City Council. The City Manager shall consider, investigate and
make findings, reports and recommendations upon any special matter or question
within the scope of this work.
   (3)   Official street tree species. The following list constitutes the
official street tree species for the city. No species other than those included
on this list may be planted as street trees without prior written approval of
the City Manager.
Small Trees                 Medium Trees            Large Trees   
Flowering Cherry, tree form Ginkgo Biloba           London Plane
varieties*
Flowering Crab, tree form   Red Oak                 Norway Maple**
varieties*
Bradford Pear               Ivory Silk Tree Lilac   Improved Elm+
                           Pin Oak                 Sugar Maple
                           Little Leaf Linden      Red Maple
                           Thornless Honey Locust* Zelkova - Green Vase
*   All varieties acceptable.
**   Not to be planted within 300 feet of any naturalized area. Only
“Emerald Queen,” “Emerald Lustre” and “Crimson King” cultivars are
allowed.
+   “Improved” meaning cultivars improved to be resistant to Dutch Elm
Disease.
 
   (4)   Street tree spacing. The spacing of street trees will be in accordance
with the three (3) species size classes listed in section 18-7 (3), and no
trees may be planted closer together than the following: Small trees, thirty
(30) feet; medium trees, forty (40) feet; and large trees, fifty (50) feet;
except in special plantings designed and approved for unusual effect.
   (5)   Distance of street trees from street corners. No street tree shall be
planted closer than thirty-five (35) feet from any street corner, measured from
the point of nearest intersecting curbs or curblines.
   (6)   Distance from curbs and sidewalks; planting of street trees on private
property. The distances trees may be planted from the curbs or curblines and
sidewalks will be in accordance with the trees species size classes listed in
section 18-7(3), and trees must be centered between curbs or curblines and
streets.
   (7)   Utilities. No street trees other than those species listed as small
trees in section 18-7(3) may be planted under or within ten (10) lateral feet
of any overhead utility wire or over or within five (5) lateral feet of any
underground water line, sewer line, transmission line or other utility.
   Any subsurface installation or work (water line, sewer line, transmission
line or other utility) within a ten- (10-) foot distance of a street tree or
park tree will be by “jack and bore” method, except and unless written approval
for open trenching is issued, in which case a charge for pruning, fertilization
or other preventative maintenance service will be applicable. This requirement
shall not apply to the repair or replacement of that portion of a private
utility lateral or service which is on private property.
   (8)   Care and maintenance of public trees; private planting in streets,
etc., prohibited. The City shall have the right to plant, replant, prune,
maintain and remove trees, plants and shrubs within
the lines of all streets, alleys, avenues, lanes, squares and public grounds,
as may be necessary to ensure public safety or to preserve or enhance the
symmetry and beauty of such public grounds.
   Trees may be removed which are not dead or infected with any disease when
such trees are of an undesirable species. The City Manager is hereby authorized
to direct the removal of any tree growing within any street, park or public
place, when such tree interferes with fire hydrants, sewer and water mains,
visibility of street intersections, traffic-control devices or construction
within street rights-of-way.
   No tree, plant or shrub shall be planted, replanted or removed within the
line of any street, alley, lane, square or public grounds by any private party,
except by written permission of the City.
   (9)   Topping. It shall be unlawful as a normal practice for any private
person to top any street tree, park tree or other tree on public property.
“Topping” is defined as the severe cutting back of limbs to such a degree as to
remove the normal canopy and disfigure the tree. Trees severely damaged by
storms or other causes, or certain trees under utility wires or other
obstructions where other pruning practices are impractical may be exempted from
this section at the determination of the City Manager.
   (10)   Removal of stumps. All stumps of street and park trees shall be
removed below the surface of the ground to a depth of six (6) inches.
   (11)   Sidewalk damage. Existing street trees that have caused an upheaval
or severe cracking of public sidewalks may be removed at such time that
sidewalk replacement is ordered by the City. The necessity for such removal
shall be based upon the overall vigor of the tree and the extent of conflict
with the sidewalk structure, as determined by the City.
   (12)   Interference with City personnel. It shall be unlawful for any person
to prevent, delay or interfere with the City, or any of its agents, while
engaging in and about the planting, replanting, cultivating, mulching, pruning,
spraying or removing of any street tree, park tree or tree on private grounds,
as authorized in this section.
   (13)   Private trees. Private trees are not regulated by the terms of this
section, except for the provisions of this subsection.
   The City shall have the right to cause the removal or proper treatment of
trees on private property, which harbor insects or disease and which constitute
a potential threat to other trees within the City. The City will notify in
writing the owners of such trees. Removal or treatment shall be done by such
owners, at their own expense, within a reasonable period of time as prescribed
by the City, but in no case more than sixty (60) days after the date of service
or notice. In the event of failure of owners to comply with such provisions,
the City shall have the authority to remove or treat such trees and charge the
cost of removal or of treatment to such owners.
   No tree shall be planted upon private property within (10) feet of any fire
hydrant or within three (3) feet of the right-of-way line of any street, alley,
lane, square or public ground.
   Every owner of any tree overhanging any street or right-of-way within the
city shall prune the branches so that such branches shall not obstruct the view
of any intersection and so that there shall be a clear space of fourteen (14)
feet above the surface of the street and ten (10) feet above the sidewalk. Such
owners shall remove all dead, diseased or dangerous trees, or broken or decayed
limbs which constitute a menace to the safety of the public using streets and
sidewalks. The City shall have the right to prune any tree or shrub on private
property when it interferes with the visibility of any traffic-control device
or sign.
   (14)   Arbor Day. The City Council shall annually celebrate Arbor Day. The
Council may provide trees and shrubs for its citizens at reduced cost depending
upon the demand for such trees and shrubs. (Ord. of 1-15-90; Ord. O-10-03, 5-3-
10; Ord. No. O-20-05, 9-21-20.)
Editor’s note – An ordinance of Jan. 15, 1990, repealed 18-7 and enacted a new
18-7 in lieu thereof with subsections designated 18.7-118.7-15. At the
discretion of the editor, and in order to maintain Code format, said
subsections have been redesignated as (1)-(15) or 18-7 hereon.
Sec. 18-8. Erection of street name placards.
   The City Manager shall place at the intersection of all streets and avenues
in a conspicuous manner a suitable placard, containing the name of the street
or avenue. (8-11-13, § 8.)
Sec. 18-9. Removal, destruction, mutilation or defacement of street or avenue
signs.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to take down, destroy, mutilate or
deface in any manner any street or avenue sign. (8-11-13, § 9.)
Sec. 18-10. Violations and penalties; civil remedies.
   Violation of this Article shall constitute a civil infraction, per Chapter
5.1 Civil Infractions of the City Code. The City may also seek such civil
relief as is available to it in law or equity. (Ord. No. O-20-05, 9-21-20)
ARTICLE II. SIDEWALKS, CROSSWALKS, DRIVEWAY APPROACHES AND CURBS*
   * Charter reference – Construction and repair of sidewalks, 2.2(16.) without
first having obtained and having in force a permit as hereinafter provided. (8-
26-57, 2.)
Sec. 18-11. Same – Specifications and compliance therewith.
   No person shall construct or repair any sidewalk, crosswalk, driveway
approach or curb except in accordance with the line, grade, slope and
specifications established by the City Engineer. The City Engineer shall set
proper grade and line stakes for such walks whenever such sidewalk, crosswalk,
driveway approach or curb shall have been permitted or ordered. Specifications
for all sidewalks shall be on file in the office of the City Clerk as
established by the City Engineer. (11-18-85.)
Sec. 18-12. Same – Specifications and compliance therewith.
   No person shall construct or repair any sidewalk, crosswalk, driveway
approach or curb except in accordance with the line, grade, slope and
specifications established by the City Engineer. The City Engineer shall set
proper grade and line stakes for such walks whenever such sidewalk, crosswalk,
driveway approach or curb shall have been permitted or ordered. Specifications
for all sidewalks shall be on file in the office of the City Clerk as
established by the City Engineer. (11-18-85.)
Sec. 18-13. Same – Expenses.
   All sidewalks in the city shall be built, at the expense of the owner or
owners of the lots or premises adjoining or abutting upon such sidewalks;
provided, that in the discretion of the City Council a part of the expense of
constructing any new sidewalk may be born by the City and paid from the general
fund. The proportion is to be so paid by the City and conditions, under which
payment is to be made, shall be determined by resolution of the City Council.
(11-18-85.)
Sec. 18-14. Repairs – Expenses.
   The City Council shall determine the necessity for repair of all sidewalks
in the city and the costs of such repairs shall be born by the City. (11-18-
85.)
ARTICLE III. EXCAVATIONS.
Sec. 18-18. Permits – Required.
   Unless acting under a contract with the City, it shall by unlawful for any
person other than a duly authorized City official or employee in the course of
his employment to make or cause or permit to be made any excavation or opening
in or under the surface or pavement of any street, alley, sidewalk or other
public place within the limits of the city
Sec. 18-19. Same – Application.
   Any person, desiring to procure a specific permit as herein provided shall
file with the City Manager, at least twenty-four hours before the time proposed
to begin such work, a written application on a blank form prepared and provided
by the City. Such application shall state the name and address of the
applicant, the name of the street, alley, sidewalk or public place in or under
which it is desired to make the excavation or opening, the kind of pavement or
sidewalk thereon, the purpose, size and location, as near as can be determined
of the proposed excavation or opening and the name, address, lot and
subdivision of the person whose benefit the work is to be done. Such
application shall also describe the time within which the work in such
application shall be completed. When required by the City Manager, the
application shall be accompanied by a plat or pencil tracing or sketch showing
the location, character and dimensions of the proposed excavation or opening
for the installation of new work or the location and character of the
alterations involving the location of pipes, poles, conduits, wires or other
conductors. (8-26-57, § 3.)
Sec. 18-20. Same – Issuance; fee.
   The city, upon the filing of the application , may, in its discretion, issue
a permit which issuance shall constitute an agreement by the applicant with the
City that applicant shall restore that portion of the premises not included
within a traveled roadway to its original condition and further, that the
applicant shall pay all costs of restoration of the portion of the premises
within the traveled roadway in the manner hereinafter set forth. (8-26-57, §
4.)
Sec. 18-21. Erection of barricades, etc.; removal or interference with
barricades, etc.
   Any person making or causing to be made an excavation or opening in any
street, alley, sidewalk or other public place or within five feet of the line
of any street or public place shall, at all times that the same remains open or
danger exists therefrom, keep such excavation or opening fenced or barricaded
and properly lighted at night so as to warn all persons of such excavation or
opening and all obstructions. No unauthorized person shall remove, extinguish
or in any other way interfere with the barricades, flares, lanterns or other
danger signals placed for the protection of excavations or obstructions. (8-26-
57, § 5.)
Sec. 18-22. Conformity of work to permit; interference with pedestrian and
vehicular traffic, etc.
   In no case shall a person remove a greater area of surface and at no other
location than that specified in the application for permit; provided, that at
the time of actually doing the work if it shall be necessary to remove a
greater area of surface than originally applied for, the applicant shall first
notify and procure the consent of the City Manager to do so upon the express
condition that he will, before noon of the following business day, file a
supplementary application for the making of any additional excavation.
   All work shall be performed in such a way as to cause a minimum of
inconvenience and restriction to both pedestrian and vehicular traffic. No dirt
or other material shall be placed on sidewalks. All work shall be prosecuted so
as not to interfere with any access to any fire houses, fire hydrants and
United States mail boxes. (8-26-57, § 6.)
Sec. 18-23. Restoration.
   All excavations shall be restored to their original condition. All that
portion of the excavation not within the traveled portion of the roadway,
sidewalk or pavement shall be restored by the applicant in a manner
satisfactory to the City Manager. Failure of applicant to restore such portion
of such excavation to its original condition in a manner satisfactory to the
City Manager shall constitute a violation of this article and shall subject
applicant to the penalties for violation hereinafter set forth.
   All excavations made within the traveled portion of a roadway, sidewalk or
pavement may be restored to their original condition. All backfill and surface
replacement shall be performed under the supervision of the City Manager. The
applicant shall be required to pay all the expenses incurred by the City for
furnishing such material, doing such work and taking such means as in the sole
discretion of the City Manager shall be required to properly restore and secure
against settlement of the street and sidewalk, pavement, curb and gutter
necessary to be replaced in consequence of such excavation, opening or
disturbance.
   Failure of the applicant to pay all costs incurred in the restoration of the
site to its original condition when due shall be considered a violation of this
article and shall subject applicant to the penalty for violation hereinafter
set forth. Payment for the restoration of the excavation to its original
condition shall be made within thirty days after billing date by the City. The
sum or sums of money collected for restoration work shall be paid into the City
treasury.
   All excavations in the traveled portion of any roadway, sidewalk or pavement
shall be replaced by the applicant and shall conform to the specifications as
may be adopted from time to time by the City Council and listed on the permit
for such excavation. (8-26-57, § 7.)
Sec. 18-24. Notice of intent to excavate to corporations with equipment in
street; protection of pipes, poles, conduits, etc.
   The person to whom a permit is granted shall give notice in writing to any
corporation whose pipes, poles, mains or conduits are laid in the street about
to be disturbed by such excavations at least twenty-four hours before
commencing such excavation and shall at his own expense sustain, secure and
protect such pipes, poles, mains or conduits from injury and replace and pack
the earth with the same sod that has been removed, loosened or disturbed under
or around so that they shall be well and substantially supported. If any person
shall fail to sustain, secure or protect such pipes, poles, mains or conduits
from injury or to replace and pack the earth under and around them, the
provisions of this section will require that the same may be done by the
corporation to whom the same may belong and the cost thereof and any damage
sustained by such corporation thereby shall be paid by such person, and in
default thereof, such corporation may maintain an action against him therefor.
(8-26-57, § 8.)
Sec. 18-25. Indemnification of City.
   The person to whom such permit is granted shall do no injury in any street,
avenue, alley, lane, sidewalk, park or other public place or to any shade
trees, shrubs, lawns, concrete paving or sidewalk or other like improvements or
in any manner disturb or interfere with any sewer, water main, pipe or conduit
or any other public or private appliances now or hereafter constructed by any
authorized persons and shall fully indemnify and save harmless the City from
any and all claims or damages for which the City might be made or become liable
to pay by reason of construction, maintaining or repairing or operation of such
poles, conduits, wires, mains, pipes or any other apparatus connected therewith
or otherwise arising from the use or possession of any of the rights and
privileges granted or from any neglect on the part of such person, or of his
employees to comply with the provisions of this article or ordinances of the
City and especially shall indemnify the City and assume all liability and
damages which may arise, come or occur to the City from any injury to persons
or property by reason of the doing of any work herein mentioned or the neglect
of any person or his employees to comply with the provisions of this article or
other ordinances relative to the use of streets or other public places,
especially as to the putting up of lights or barriers at or around excavations;
and the acceptance by any person of any permit under the provisions of this
article shall be an agreement by it to pay the City any sum of money for which
the City may become liable from or by reason of such injury. Such person shall
be given written notice of any and all forms of claims, suits and demands filed
with the City within thirty days after receiving such claims, etc., and shall
be given an opportunity to defend such claims, etc. (8-26-57, § 9.)
   * Charter reference – Construction and repair of sidewalks, 2.2(16.) without
first having obtained and having in force a permit as hereinafter provided. (8-
26-57, 2.)
   Editor’s note – Ordinance No. O-20-05, adopted Sept. 21, 2020, enacted a new
18-10 in Article I and redesignated the sections of Article II from 18-10–18-13
to 18-11–18-14.
ARTICLE IV. BUILDING NUMBERS
For charter provisions as to building numbers, see Char., 2.2 (22)
Sec. 18-26. System generally.
   The houses and buildings of the streets and avenues of the city shall be
numbered by the "Philadelphia" or "block system." (8-11-13, § 1.)
Sec. 18-27. Streets to be used as basis; numbering system designations.
   The streets and avenues to be used as the basis for such numbering shall be
Main Street and Division Avenue extended and beginning at the base; the blocks
shall be numbered by the decimal system in units of one hundred and designated
as north, south, east or west. (8-11-13, § 2.)
Sec. 18-28. Assignment of numbers generally.
   One number shall be assigned for each twenty-two feet as nearly as may be.
The houses or buildings in each block shall be numbered commencing with the
number of the block and thereafter by adding to the number of the block the
number of the house or building. Even numbers shall be used on the easterly and
southerly sides and odd numbers on the westerly and northerly sides of streets
proceeding from the base. (8-11-13, § 3.)
Sec. 18-29. Streets and avenues not intersecting base.
   In streets and avenues which do not intersect with the base the block shall
be numbered to correspond with the blocks in the base parallel thereto. (8-11-
13, § 4.)
Sec. 18-30. Numbering where conformity with system cannot be obtained.
   If in any case the numbers cannot be designated according to the system as
herein outlined, the City Clerk shall report the same to the City Manager,
together with his recommendations, and the City Manager shall thereupon provide
for the official numbering thereof, and such provision shall be properly noted
on the map or plat. (8-11-13, § 6.)
Sec. 18-31. Designation of official number by clerk; display; size of figures.
   The City Clerk shall designate the official numbers for all houses or
buildings within the city. Such numbers shall be of sufficient size and
displayed in such a manner that they are easily read from the street. (8-11-13,
7.)
Sec. 18-32. Display of nonofficial number; removal, destruction, etc., of house
number.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to display any number other than the
official number upon any house or building or to take down, destroy, mutilate
or deface in any manner any house or building number. (8-11-13, 9.)
ARTICLE V. PRIVATE STREETS
Sec. 18-33. Purpose.
   It is the intent of this Ordinance to permit the development of private
streets as an alternative to public streets provided said private streets are
properly designed, constructed and maintained so as to accommodate the movement
of vehicular traffic, including emergency vehicles, in a safe and efficient
manner and to ensure that connection of private streets with public streets is
accomplished according to the requirements of the agency having jurisdiction
over said public streets.
   Private streets are permitted in all zoning districts subject to the design,
construction and maintenance standards of this Ordinance. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-34. Definitions.
a.   Dwelling Units. When used in this article, the term Dwelling Units shall
mean all single family residences. For example: a building containing two
separate living areas serving two separate single families shall be deemed to
be two Dwelling Units under the terms of this article. (7-7-03)
b.   Private Street. When used in this article, the term Private Street shall
mean all means of access to any residence if said means of access is serving
two or more dwelling units regardless of length or width. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-35. Level of Design and Construction
   The minimum design and construction level of private streets as outlined in
Sections 18-40, 18-41 and 18-42 of this Article shall be based on the number of
lots and/or parcels to be served. Generally, as the number of said lots and/or
parcels increases resulting in greater demands on the street, the design and
construction requirements also increase. If the number of lots and/or parcels
to be served by an existing private street increases, said street shall be
upgraded throughout its entirety to comply with the requirements of this
Article. The upgrade shall be based on the number of new parcels to be created,
plus all existing parcels to be served by the private street. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-36. Private Street Construction Permit Application and Approval
   The owner shall submit an application for a private street permit, together
with the application review fee as determined from time to time by the City
Council, to the City Clerk. The application package shall include: (7-7-03)
a.   A written description of the proposed development to be served;
b.   Detailed site plans and construction plans; and
c.   A detailed Maintenance Agreement (hereinafter "Agreement") describing how
the costs of operation and maintenance will be addressed. In the event said
costs are to be apportioned and paid for by benefiting property owners, the
Agreement shall include a detailed description of the procedures for
administering the same.
   The proposed private street shall meet the requirements for Site Plan Review
by the City Planning Commission (hereinafter "Commission") as found in this
Article, provided, however, private streets proposed for projects subject to
final review and approval by the City Council (hereinafter "Council") shall be
subject to review and approval by the Council after receipt of a recommendation
from the Commission. In reviewing the application, the Commission and the
Council shall consider the impact of the proposed development on adjacent
properties, whether the health, safety and general welfare of persons or
property using or affected by the private street will be adequately protected,
and whether the private street will adversely affect the long-term development
policies of the City of Fremont (hereinafter "City".) An architect, engineer or
other person will be consulted if deemed necessary. If the Commission, or the
Council in the case of those projects subject to review and approval by the
Council, recommends approval of the application, the Zoning Administrator shall
issue a private street construction permit to the owner. No construction shall
begin on the private street or on adjacent properties that depend on the
private street for access until the private street construction permit has been
issued. The owner shall allow the City to enter the property for purposes of
reviewing construction progress for compliance with the approved site plan and
construction drawings. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-37. Site Plans and Construction Plans
   A site plan and construction plan showing the proposed location, adjacent
properties, proposed street grades, drainage and proposed improvements shall be
prepared by a registered engineer or registered land surveyor and shall be
submitted to the Zoning Administrator as part of the private street
construction permit application and approval. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-38. Final Private Street Permit
   Upon completion of construction, the applicant shall have its street design
surveyor or engineer inspect the private street improvements to verify
compliance with the approved site plan and construction plan. The owner shall
correct any deficiencies identified during either an interim or final review
inspection. Upon final review and approval of the completed private street
improvements, the professional engineer or professional surveyor shall provide
the City Clerk with written certification that the street has been constructed
according to the approved designed plans. The certification shall be signed by
the engineer or surveyor and shall contain the seal of same. After receipt of
the construction certification, the City Clerk shall issue a final private
street permit to the owner. Zoning permits for construction on properties
served by the private street shall not be issued until the City issues the
final private street permit. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-39. Street Names
   All streets serving more than two dwellings shall be given a name approved
by the City and the Newaygo County Road Commission. Approved street signs shall
be placed at each street intersection. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-40. Maintenance and Repair
   Maintenance, repair and liability for private streets shall be the
responsibility of benefiting property owners with access to the private street
and not the responsibility or liability of the City, city staff or consultants
used by the City in the review and approval of private streets. The developer
shall establish, by appropriate deed provisions, an association that shall be
responsible for street maintenance and repair and that shall have the authority
to apportion and collect the cost of maintenance and repair from benefiting
property owners. A Private Street Maintenance Agreement (hereinafter
"Agreement") shall be recorded at the Newaygo County Office of the Register of
Deeds. The recording shall be a separate recording from the deed, but the deed
shall also have attached to it a copy of the Agreement or otherwise give notice
of the Agreement. All property owners subject to payment for maintenance of the
private street shall receive notice of the above Agreement. Benefiting
properties must be identified in the Agreement and any change in benefiting
properties must be reflected in a revised agreement. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-41. Design Standards for Streets Serving Two (2) Dwelling Units
   Private streets serving only two (2) dwelling units shall meet the following
design standards: (7-7-03)
a.   All private streets shall have a minimum forty-foot (40') wide right-of-
way easement granted to the adjacent property owner(s).
b.   Be constructed in a good and workmanlike manner upon and parallel to the
centerline of the right-of-way easement granted to the adjacent property
owners.
c.   Be constructed so as to sufficiently control stormwater runoff and permit
effective stormwater drainage, such as by means of ditches constructed parallel
to and on either side of the drive, by sloping the sides of the drive from the
center thereof, or by other effective methods.
d.   Have a firmly compacted base with the following cross-sections as
specified by the City depending on the choice of any of the two permitted types
of driving surfaces:
   1.   Asphalt:   Six inches (6") of sand
      Six inches (6") of gravel
      Two inches (2") of asphalt placed as two (2) layers
   2.   Concrete:   Six inches (6") of sand
      Six inches (6") of concrete
e.   Have that portion of a private street located within any public street
right-of-way surfaced with either asphalt or concrete as previously specified.
f.   Have a finished driving surface width of not less than fourteen feet
(14').
g.   Be constructed over adequate culverts where necessary.
h.   Shall not be expanded to service more than two (2) dwelling units without
meeting the requirements of this Article for private streets serving more than
two (2) dwelling units.
Sec. 18-42. Design Standards for Streets Serving Three (3) to Five (5) Dwelling
Units
   Private streets serving three (3) to five (5) dwelling units shall meet the
following design standards: (7-7-03)
a.   Have a minimum sixty-six foot (66') wide right-of-way easement granted to
the adjacent property owner(s).
b.   Be constructed in a good and workmanlike manner upon and parallel to the
centerline of the right-of-way easement granted to the adjacent property owner
(s).
c.   Be constructed so as to sufficiently control stormwater runoff and permit
effective stormwater drainage such as by means of ditches constructed parallel
to and on either side of the street, by sloping the sides of the street from
the center thereof or by other effective methods.
d.   The driving surface shall be either asphalt or concrete, with firmly
compacted base with the following cross-sections as specified by the City
depending on the type of driving surface:
   1.   Asphalt:   Six inches (6") of sand
      Six inches (6") of gravel
      Three inches (3") of asphalt placed as two (2) layers
   2.   Concrete:   Six inches (6") of sand
      Six inches (6") of concrete
e.   Have a finished driving surface width of not less than sixteen feet (16').
f.   Be constructed over adequate culverts where necessary.
g.   All culs-de-sac must terminate with turnarounds, have a right-of-way
radius of fifty-five feet (55') and a finished driving surface turning radius
of forty-five feet (45').
h.   Shall not be expanded to service more than three (3) to five (5) dwelling
units without meeting the requirements of this Article for private streets
serving more than three (3) to five (5) dwelling units.
Sec. 18-43. Design Standards for Streets Serving More than Five (5) Dwelling
Units
   Private streets serving more than five (5) dwelling units shall meet the
following design standards: (7-7-03)
a.   Have a minimum sixty-six foot (66') wide right-of-way easement granted to
the adjacent property owner(s).
b.   Be constructed in a good and workmanlike manner upon and parallel to the
centerline of the right-of-way easement granted to the adjacent property owner
(s).
c.   Culverts shall be placed at all natural drainage courses or other
waterways. Culvert sizes and grades shall be determined using the appropriate
storm runoff calculations formula. Materials for culverts shall also conform to
the City's specifications. Where the placement of underground storm sewers is
determined necessary by the City Engineer, the developer shall receive approval
of the City Engineer of all designs, materials and methods of installation.
d.   The developer shall receive the approval of the City Engineer of the
layout of private streets in respect to their location, intersections, culs-de-
sac, vertical street alignment, street grades, street signs, horizontal curves,
curb openings at intersecting streets and other aspects as determined by the
City Engineer.
e.   The driving surface shall be either asphalt or concrete, with a firmly
compacted base with the following cross-sections as specified by the City
depending on the type of driving surface:
   1.   Asphalt:   Twelve inches (12") of sand
      Six inches (6") of gravel
      Three inches (3") of asphalt placed as two (2) layers
   2.   Concrete:   Twelve inches (12") of sand
      Six inches (6") of concrete
f.   Have concrete curb and gutter with a minimum width of eighteen inches
(18") as specified by the City with a finished driving width of thirty-two feet
(32') from face of curb to face of curb.
g.   All culs-de-sac must terminate with turnarounds having a right-of-way
radius of at least fifty-five feet (55') and a turning radius of forty-five
feet (45').
h.   Have a minimum five-foot (5') wide concrete sidewalk on at least one side
of the street, placement and design of which are subject to prior City
approval.
Sec. 18-44. Maximum Street Length
   In no case shall the length of a private street exceed eight hundred feet
(800') unless secondary, intersecting, streets connect to the private street at
intervals of no less than eight hundred feet (800'). Secondary streets may be
public or private and shall be of comparable or better condition than the
private street under application. Secondary streets shall provide an alternate
means of access to the local public street system. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-45. Easement Provisions
   Throughout its length, the right-of-way for private streets shall contain
easement provisions for the aboveground and underground placement of (essential
service) utility and energy lines and mains. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-46. Street Location Adjustment
   The Commission, with the concurrence of the City Engineer, may permit
adjustments in the required placement of the improved portion of a street
within a street easement if said placement would result in the protection of
mature trees, water bodies or other natural features and would not pose a
threat to the health, safety or welfare of adjoining property owner(s). (7-7-
03)
Sec. 18-47. Commercial Industrial Private Streets
   All private streets developed and/or used for commercial and/or industrial
land purposes shall comply with all public street requirements pursuant to the
City of Fremont Code. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-48. Applicability
   This ordinance will not be applied retroactively and will take effect as
indicated below. (7-7-03)
Sec. 18-49. Effective Date
   This Ordinance shall take effect ten (10) days after publication thereof,
said effective date being July 23, 2003. (7-7-03)
CHAPTER 19.
SUBDIVISION OF LAND
For Charter provisions as to platting of subdivisions, see Char. 2.2(20). As to
Planning Commission, see Char. 7.8.
For state law as to subdivision of land generally, see Michigan Statutes
Annotated (MSA), §§ 560.101 et seq. As to city planning, see 2-26 to 2-28 of
this Code. As to zoning, see Chap. 22.
