   ARTICLE I: GENERAL
Sec. 19-1. Definitions
For the purpose of this Chapter, words and phrases shall be defined as set
forth by M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq., and as follows:
Commission. The Fremont Planning Commission (hereinafter "Commission".)
Complete utility subdivision. A subdivision in which arrangements have been
made for both water service and sewage disposal by public utility systems and
for the other improvements required by this Chapter.
Governing Body. The Fremont City Council (hereinafter "Council".)
Local or minor street. A public street primarily serving abutting neighborhood
properties.
Major street. A street designated as a major street on the adopted Master Plan
of the City.
Major subdivision. The creation of a new lot or lots by platting; the creation
of more than four new lots of ten acres or less within a ten-year period from
one parcel of property by transfer or metes and bounds description; or the
creation of a new street whether by the owner or required by the Council.
Minor subdivision. The combination of existing parcels into fewer lots; the
alteration of a lot line not changing the number of lots; or the creation of
one or more new parcels of property on an existing street by transfer or metes
and bounds description. A minor subdivision shall not include new or resulting
lots of more than ten acres or lots defined as a major subdivision.
Partial utility subdivision. A subdivision in which arrangements have been made
for either water service or sewage disposal by a public utility system, but not
both, and for the other improvements required by this Chapter.
Potential utility subdivision. A subdivision in which required public water or
sewage disposal by public utility systems cannot be provided by the City at the
time of platting, but where the other improvements required by this Chapter are
provided.
Private service subdivision. A subdivision located in an area in which neither
public water nor sewage disposal by a public utility system is furnished or
contemplated.
Public utility system. A water or sewer system owned and operated by the City
or a community utility system approved by the City. (5/3/71, § 2.1)
Sec. 19-2. Purpose of Chapter
   It is the intent of this Chapter to:
·   Regulate the subdivision of land
·   Further the orderly layout and development of the City
·   Provide for and regulate the economical extension of utility services,
streets and other necessary land improvements
·   Require that land be suitable and suitably improved for building sites
·   Provide for adequate drainage
·   Prevent the premature development of land
·   Provide for proper ingress and egress to lots
·   Promote proper surveying, monuments and legal descriptions
·   Provide for safe and convenient traffic circulation and traffic movement
·   Insure against the creation of unsafe or undesirable conditions
·   Conserve the value of property
·   Regulate the density of development where utility services are not provided
for the protection of the public health
·   Conserve natural features
·   Carry out the purpose and intent of the City Master Plan and Chapter 22
·   Carry out the purpose and intent of M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq.
·   Establish rules and procedures for the process of subdivision under said
act
·   Provide for the adoption of improvement standards
·   Provide penalties for the violations of this Chapter, and
·   Provide for the variation of these rules and requirements. (5/3/71, § 1.3)
Sec. 19-3. Interpretation and Application of Chapter Generally
In their interpretation and application the provisions of this Chapter shall be
held to be minimum requirements adopted for the promotion of public health,
safety, convenience and general
welfare. It shall be administered to insure orderly growth and development and
to conserve and adequately provide for streets, utilities and other services
and other services in the city and its surrounding urbanizing area. (5-13-71, §
1.2)
For state law as to authority of city to impose stricter requirements than
imposed by state law, see M.C.L.A. § 560.259.
Sec. 19-4. Administration Generally
The Commission, City Manager and the Council shall administer this Chapter. The
rules, regulations and standards imposed by this Chapter shall be considered to
be the minimum requirements for the protection of the public health, safety and
welfare of the citizens of the City, and in interpreting and applying them
primary consideration shall be given to these factors. (5/3/71, § 10.1)
Sec. 19-5. Applicability of Chapter to Parcels of Land over Ten Acres in Area
This Chapter shall not apply to land divisions resulting in parcels of land
which are over ten (10) acres in area unless a new street is required to
provide public access as set forth in Chapter 22. (5/3/71, § 1.4)
Sec. 19-6. Density of development; Service Areas Map; Service Areas Defined
The density of all future subdivision development shall be directly related to
service areas shown on the service areas map as primary, secondary, industrial,
industrial reserve, lake and private service area. Such map is incorporated
into and made a part of this Chapter.
Primary service areas are those wherein the City provides or intends to provide
both public sewer and public water services.
Secondary service areas are those which are now provided with or wherein the
City intends to make available or provide either public sewer or public water
service at some time in the more distant future.
Industrial service areas are those wherein the City intends to make available
or provide public sewer and public water services only to uses conforming to
manufacturing zone requirements.
Industrial reserve service areas are those wherein the City anticipates the
long-range need for industrial sewer and water service but in which such
service is not now economically possible.
Lake service areas are those wherein the City anticipates the need for sewer
service to avoid lake water pollution problems but where no plans are
formulated to make such service possible.
Private service areas are those wherein the City has no intent or desire to
make available or provide either sewer or water services within the reasonably
near future. (5/3/71, § 1.5)
Sec. 19-7. Compliance Generally
After June 2, 1971 no new lot of ten (10) acres or less in area shall be
created within the City unless the provisions of Article IV of this Chapter are
complied with. The City Assessor shall report all metes and bounds or other
description transfers not complying with Article IV of this Chapter to the City
Manager for appropriate remedy or action. All new lots so created shall meet or
exceed the requirements of the zoning regulations. (5/3/71, § 1.6)
Sec. 19-8. Penalty; Each Lot Sold Deemed a Separate Offense
If any person transfers or sells any portion of an existing parcel of land
without complying with the regulations of this Chapter or if any person
violates any provision of this Chapter, such person shall be subject to a fine
as determined by resolution of the city council or to imprisonment for not more
than thirty (30) days, and each parcel, plot or lot so disposed of shall be
deemed a separate violation. (5/3/71, § 10.3)
ARTICLE II: REGULATIONS APPLICABLE TO ALL SUBDIVISIONS
Sec. 19-9. Conformity to Master Plan and Zoning Map
All subdivisions shall conform to the provisions and conditions of the Master
Plan and zoning map for future development of the City and surrounding area.
(5/3/71, § 8.1)
Sec. 19-10. Streets
All streets shall conform in direction and alignment with the Master Plan and
shall connect with existing streets without jogs or sharp angles.
a.   Curves. Curving minor streets shall have a minimum inside right-of-way
(hereinafter "ROW") radius of one hundred feet (100'). Such minimum shall be
two hundred feet (200') on collector streets and three hundred feet (300') for
major streets.
b.   Rights-of-way. Local street ROW shall be sixty-six feet (66') in width.
Major street ROW shall be at least one hundred feet (100') in width or fifty
feet (50') from the centerline. Where permitted or required, alley or utility
ROW shall be at least twenty feet (20') in width.
c.   Stub or outlet streets. Stub streets or outlets to adjacent undeveloped
property shall be fully improved by the subdivider, including drainage and
utilities as required by Section 19-43 or 19-45 as applicable.
d.   Dead-end streets. Dead-end streets shall not exceed eight hundred feet
(800') in length unless a paved outlet street is provided to adjacent property,
which will eventually make a dead-end street so conform. There shall be a turn-
around roadway with a minimum outside curb radius of forty-five feet (45') and
a street property line diameter of at least one hundred ten (110') feet at the
closed end unless the Commission approves the use of a "T"- or "Y"-shaped
turning area.
e.   Reserve strips. Reserve strips along major streets or bodies of water may
be required by the Commission to be dedicated to the City to prohibit access
upon the major street or body of water from an approved lot.
f.   Street names. All street names shall be subject to the approval of the
Council.
g.   Offsets. Offsetting at an intersection is prohibited unless the
centerlines thereof are offset at least one hundred twenty-five feet (125').
(5/3/71, § 8.2)
For state law as to authority of city to set requirements for streets, see
M.C.L.A. § 560.182. As to state law requirements for streets, see M.C.L.A. §
560.181.
Sec. 19-11. Lots
Every lot shall face upon a dedicated street accepted by the City and shall
have at least forty feet (40') of lot width at the ROW line.
a.   Lot depth. No lot shall be less than one hundred twenty-five feet (125')
in depth at any point.
b.   Shape. No lot shall be of such a shape as to require a variance of zoning
regulations.
c.   Double frontage. No lot shall be bounded on opposite sides by streets
except that on a major street the Commission may require that abutting lots
face upon a minor street and that a reserve strip be provided to prohibit
access upon such major street.
d.   Major street frontage. No lot may be platted upon a major street unless it
has a frontage of at least one hundred ten feet (110') along the major street
ROW.
e.   Suitability. Where there is a question as to the suitability of a lot or
lots for an intended use due to factors such as soil formations, flood
conditions, floodplains, high water table or similar circumstances, the
Commission shall after adequate investigation withhold approval of such lots.
Such lots shall be combined with other lots in such manner as to prohibit
future resubdivision. (5/3/71, § 8.3)
For state laws as to lots, see M.C.L.A. § 560.186.
Sec. 19-12. Block Lengths; Outlet Intervals; Pedestrian Crosswalks
No block shall exceed one thousand feet (1,000') in length. Outlets or streets
to adjoining property may be required at lesser intervals if deemed necessary
by the Commission and twenty foot (20') pedestrian crosswalk easements with a
four foot (4') sidewalk may be required. (5/3/71, § 8.4)
Sec. 19-13. Drainage; Public Utility Easements
Where a subdivision is traversed by a watercourse, drain or street, there shall
be provided a storm water easement or drainage ROW conforming substantially
with the lines of the watercourse at flooding period, with such further width
for construction and maintenance as deemed adequate by the Commission, in no
case less than twenty feet (20') in width.
The Commission may require twenty-foot (20') easements along the lot lines of a
block for utility facilities, drainage, walkways, access to public land or
similar needs of the community. Easements may be required to be dedicated to
the City. (5/3/71, § 8.5)
For state law as to drainage, see M.C.L.A. § 560.192.
As to public utility easements, see M.C.L.A. § 560.190.
Sec. 19-14. Proposed Parks, Playgrounds, Schools or Other Public Uses
Where a proposed park, playground, school or other public use shown in the
Master Plan is located in whole or in part in a subdivision, the Commission
shall bring such use to the attention of the platter and the Council and
discuss the question of acquiring such areas by dedication, reservation or
payment. (5/3/71, § 8.6)
Sec. 19-15. Monuments
Monuments shall be placed and be of such material, size and length as set forth
in M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq. (5/3/71, § 8.7)
Sec. 19-16. Services and Improvements in Business and Industrial Subdivisions
Where land is subdivided to be used for business or industrial purposes
permitted by the zoning regulations, the services and improvements to be
required pursuant to the provisions of Section 19-43, shall be fixed by the
Commission with due consideration of use and density as they relate to the
types of business or industrial activities to be carried on in the subdivided
area. (5/3/71, § 8.8)
For state law as to construction of improvements, see M.C.L.A. § 560.188.
Sec. 19-17. Approval Generally; Re-Filing after Disapproval
The Council shall take action of approval or disapproval with recommendations
for changes within ninety (90) days of filing. Where action of disapproval is
taken, no re-filing is required if the applicant resubmits revised maps to the
Commission within sixty (60) days of such action. Such resubmittal shall be
deemed a new filing date. (5/3/71, § 8.9)
Sec. 19-18. Performance Guarantees
The Council may require formal agreements or the posting of a bond or other
surety sufficient to guarantee the proper installation and performance of
required improvements or materials or to meet other provisions or intents of
this Chapter. (5/3/71, § 8-10)
For state law as to performance guarantees, see M.C.L.A. § 560.182 and §
560.188.
Sec. 19-19. Applicability of State Law
The requirements, procedures, regulations and powers set forth in M.C.L.A. §§
560.101 et seq., shall apply unless modified by greater requirements,
procedures, regulations and powers of this Chapter. (5/3/71, § 8.11)
Sec. 19-20. Establishment of Inspection Fees, Requirements, etc.
The Council may establish inspection fees, inspection requirements,
specification standards and administrative procedures necessary for the
enforcement of this Chapter and such shall be deemed to be requirements of this
Chapter. (5/3/71, § 8.12)
For similar state law, see M.C.L.A. § 560.246.
ARTICLE III: UTILITY EXTENSIONS
Sec. 19-21. Requests for Service - Generally
Where utility services have been extended to a street, requests for utility
services to existing buildings or to existing platted lots shall be submitted
to the City Manager. If the Manager finds that the property or building meets
the requirements of this Chapter and of the zoning regulations he may authorize
such service; provided, that satisfactory financing arrangements are arrived
at.
Requests to extend City utility services to nonconforming uses, to new areas or
to new streets shall be made to the City Manager or as otherwise provided by
the Charter. No request for such public services shall be approved for a
property which does not conform to the provisions of this Chapter, the zoning
regulations or the adopted Master Plan except by a three-fourths vote of the
entire Council. (5/3/71, § 3.1)
Sec. 19-22. Same - Referral to Commission
Where a request for public utilities is made for a new subdivision within the
City, for a new subdivision or a new use outside of the City or for a
nonconforming use, it shall be forwarded to the Commission for study and
report. In making its report, the Commission shall apply the standards of the
zoning regulations and of this Chapter insofar as they are applicable and shall
make recommendations relating to annexation, service agreements or other
pertinent matters. (5/3/71, § 3.2)
Sec. 19-23. Installation Costs and Service Charges
Where any public improvements or other service is recommended and where the
City agrees to provide such service, such service shall be provided only when
satisfactory arrangements have been made for financing the cost of installation
and for the payment of satisfactory service charges for the use thereof. The
charge to properties outside the City shall be in accordance with the policies
established from time to time by the Council. (5/3/71, § 3.3)
ARTICLE IV: PROCEDURES
Sec. 19-24. Sketch Plats - Minor Subdivisions
Before any owner of land or his agent shall effect a minor subdivision, three
copies of a sketch plat of the proposed subdivision shall be submitted to the
Commission for approval. Such sketch plat shall be drawn to scale in ink and
shall show the original parcel of land in full, the lot to be created, any
building located on or within fifty feet (50') of such new lot, and any other
pertinent information required for such considerations. Dimensions to the
nearest foot shall be shown on all lot lines and existing buildings, and
distances between buildings and lot lines shall be shown to the nearest plat.
The Commission shall review the proposed minor subdivisions, and if it complies
with the provisions of this Chapter and of the zoning regulations, it shall
approve the subdivision and the Chair shall affix his signature, the date and a
notation of approval to the three (3) copies of the sketch plat. The Commission
shall forward one (1) approved copy to the Assessor and return one (1) signed
copy to the owner or his agent. No more than four (4) additional new lots shall
be created by a minor subdivision from any parcel of land existing as of
January 1, 1968 within a ten-year period following the creation of the first
lot without complying with the requirements for a major subdivision. The
Commission may designate any minor subdivision as a major subdivision if it
deems a new street is necessary or that the intent of this Chapter requires
such designation. Where a proposed lot faces upon a major or secondary street,
the sketch plat shall show and provide for any additional street ROW required
by Section 19-10 or shall be classified as a major subdivision in order to
create such additional ROW. (5/3/71, § 4.1)
Sec. 19-25. Same - Major Subdivisions
A sketch plat of any major subdivision must be submitted to the Commission
prior to the preparation of submission of a preliminary plat. The sketch plat
shall contain the information required by Article V of this Chapter and shall
be designed to enable the Commission to discuss principles and problems
involved before the expense of completing engineering drawings is incurred by
the developer. The following procedure shall be followed:
a.   Six (6) prints of the sketch plat shall be submitted to the City Manager
at least one (1) week prior to the next meeting of the Commission.
b.   The Manager shall forward one (1) copy of the sketch plat to the planning
consultant, Engineer and Assessor for review prior to such meeting. All
findings shall be reported to the Commission at such meeting.
c.   The developer, subdivider or his engineer must be present to present the
sketch plat to the Commission.
d.   The Commission shall review the sketch plat and reports, and advise the
applicant of any required changes, additional requirements or any further
action that the applicant may need to take.
e.   The Commission shall be advised and shall so advise the applicant if the
plat comes under the approval jurisdiction of the Health Department, County
Drain Commission, County Road Commission, State Highway Department or the Water
Resources Commission so that the applicant may make necessary submittals and
investigations prior to submission of a preliminary plat. (5/3/71, § 4.2)
Sec. 19-26. Same - Approval
Approval of the sketch plat shall not be binding upon the Commission but will
enable the applicant to proceed on a reasonable and sound basis. Where review
by another agency is required, the sketch plat approval shall automatically be
contingent upon such recommendations and requirements from such agencies. The
Commission may require the resubmission of a sketch plat incorporating advised
changes and may also require the submittal of additional data or information
prior to sketch plat approval. Sketch plat approval does not carry the
authority to proceed with construction or to sell or transfer property. (5/3/
71, § 4.3)
Sec. 19-27. Preliminary Plats - Submission to Clerk; Filing Fees; Forwarding of
Copies; Review; Presence of Subdivider at Commission Meetings
A preliminary plat of any proposed major subdivision must be submitted and
approved prior to the preparation of a final plat. The preliminary plat shall
contain all information required by Article V of this Chapter where applicable.
The following procedures shall be followed:
a.   Six (6) copies of the preliminary plat and two (2) copies of all proposed
utility and improvement plans together with two (2) copies of all required
information and data shall be submitted to the City Clerk at least two (2)
weeks prior to the regular meeting of the Commission.
b.   The applicant shall pay the City Clerk a filing fee as determined by
resolution of the city council for each proposed lot within the plat, whichever
is greater, including any parcel left from the original property. The
Commission may later direct the Clerk to remit to the applicant one-half (½) of
such fee where there are no requirements for any new streets, utilities or
other improvements other than monuments.
c.   The City Clerk shall forward copies of the preliminary plat to the City
Manager, the planning consultant, the City Engineer, the City Assessor and the
Chair of the Commission within three (3) days of the receipt. A copy of utility
and improvements plan and other required data shall accompany the submittals to
the City Manager and Engineer.
d.   The plat and data shall be reviewed by the City Manager, City Engineer,
planning consultant and the City Assessor and a report thereon shall be made to
the Commission.
e.   The subdivider or his representative must be present to all meetings of
the Commission at which the plat is to be reviewed for approval. (5/3/71, §
4.4)
For state law as to submission to clerk, see M.C.L.A. § 560.113.
As to fees, see M.C.L.A. § 560.246.
Sec. 19-28. Same - Preliminary Approval; Tentative Approval; Tentative
Guarantees; Final Submissions
There are four stages of approval for a preliminary plat: Preliminary approval
by the Commission; tentative approval by the Council; tentative approval by
responsible county and state agencies; and final approval by the Council.
a.   With the applicant or his representative in attendance, the Commission
shall consider the preliminary plat and the recommendations of the Engineer,
Assessor, Planner and Manager and shall require any such changes or
modifications to be made to the plat as are necessary to comply with the
provisions of this Chapter and shall return the plat to the subdivider for
compliance. If the preliminary plat as originally submitter or as changed or
modified as required by the Commission meets the requirements of this Chapter,
the Commission shall give it preliminary approval.
b.   The preliminary plat shall then be referred to the Council for tentative
approval. The applicant shall submit final plans of sewer, water, storm drains,
streets, street profiles and other required improvements for approval by the
City Engineer. Upon approval of such plans, the Council may grant tentative
approval of the plat. Upon tentative approval, the City Clerk shall affix his
signature to the plat with the notation that it has received tentative
approval. The plat shall then be returned to the subdivider for compliance with
the final approval requirements.
c.   Tentative approval by the Council shall give the applicant the following
rights for a one-year period from the date of approval:
   1.   That the general terms and conditions under which the tentative
approval was granted will not be changed by the City.
   2.   That the applicant may submit on or before the expiration date the
whole or parts of the tentatively approved preliminary plat for final approval
of the preliminary plat.
d.   The applicant shall forward the following copies of the tentatively
approved preliminary plat and improvement plans to the following agencies for
final approval of the preliminary plat:
   1.   County Road Commission - three (3) copies if the proposed subdivision
includes or abuts roads under the Road Commission's jurisdiction.
   2.   County Drain Commission - three (3) copies.
   3.   State Highway Department - three (3) copies for land within a quarter
(¼) mile of a state highway.
   4.   State Conservation Department - two (2) copies for land upon a lake or
stream.
   5.   State Water Resources Commission - (2) copies for land in a floodplain.
   6.   County Health Department - two (2) copies in the absence of either
public water or public sewer.
   7.   County Plat Board - two (2) copies.
   8.   Gas, electric, telephone and cable television companies - two (2)
copies each.
(5/3/71, § 4.5; Ord. No.0-95-06, 9/5/95)
For state law as to tentative approval, see M.C.L.A. § 560.113.
Sec. 19.29.   Same - Final Approval; Improvements Generally; Improvement
Inspections; Sureties, Performance Bonds, Guarantees, etc.
a.   Upon receipt of approval from the above-involved agencies, the Council may
grant final approval of the preliminary plat. If changes have been recommended
by any agency, the Commission shall review such plat with the applicant in
attendance. The applicant shall change the plat to conform to such requirements
or any variation thereto deemed proper by the Commission prior to final
approval by the Council. Where such changes result in changes to the final
plans for improvements, amended plans shall be prepared and submitted to the
City Manager for approval by the Council.
Final approval of the preliminary plat by the Council shall give the applicant
the following rights for a two-year period from the date of approval:
   1.   That the City will not change the general terms and conditions under
which the final approval was granted.
   2.   That the applicant may submit on or before the expiration date the
whole or parts of the preliminary plat as a final plat in accordance with
M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq.
b.   Following final approval of the preliminary plat and final improvement
plans, the subdivider may proceed in making arrangements with the City for the
installation of streets, utilities and other improvements required under
Article VII of this Chapter and by the plans approved by the Council. The
subdivider's share of the cost of such improvements shall be borne in one of
the following ways:
   1.   By installation thereof in accordance with the City specifications and
inspection procedures.
   2.   By payment thereof at the time such improvements are to be installed by
the City.
   3.   By payment at a later date either in a lump sum, in installments or by
assessments, as may be agreed upon, in which case payment shall be assured
either by the posting by the subdivider of a surety bond in favor of the City
and acceptable by it sufficient in amount to cover the subdivider's share of
the cost of such improvements or by suitable contract between the subdivider
and the City.
c.   No improvements shall be installed, covered up or connected to existing
systems prior to the site inspection and approval of all locations and
installations by the City or by appropriate county, state or utility company
inspectors.
d.   Prior to the installation of any improvements, street or utilities, the
subdivider shall submit and have approved all required sureties, performance
bonds, maintenance guarantees or other agreements required by this Chapter or
by the regulations of the City. The Council shall determine appropriate
inspection fees to partially defray the costs of site inspections, which fees
shall be paid to the City Clerk prior to any such installation. (5/3/71, § 4.6)
For state law as to final approval and the rights conferred on applicant, see
M.C.L.A. § 560.120.
Sec. 19-30. Final Plats - Submission; Review; Approval; Forwarding of Copies;
Recording Generally
Within two (2) years from the date of final approval of the preliminary plat,
the subdivider may prepare a final plat containing all the certifications and
statements required by M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq., and by Article V of this
Chapter.
a.   The subdivider shall:
   1.   Submit five (5) true copies of the final plat to the County Drain
Commission if its approval was required on the preliminary plat.
   2.   Submit the same true copies to the County Road Commission.
   3.   Submit the same true copies to the City Clerk, but only after approval
of the above agencies has been designated upon the final plat.
   4.   Submittal to the City Clerk shall be at least two (2) weeks prior to
the Council meeting at which approval of the final plat is sought.
   5.   Pay to the City Clerk the recording fee required by state law together
with a municipal fee as determined by resolution of the city council.
   6.   Submit a surety bond for all materials and workmanship for improvements
not yet completed or installed.
   7.   Submit Mylar copies of all as-built plans for all improvements and
construction completed.
   8.   Pay all City inspection fees.
   9.   Submit all agreements, performance bonds, surety bonds, deed
restrictions, checklists or other guarantees required by Article V of this
Chapter or by a reviewing agency under M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq., or any rule
thereunder.
b.   The City Clerk shall forward all copies and submissions to the City
Manager for review for compliance with all requirements of the City
specifications, of this Chapter, M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq., and of the
approved preliminary plat.
c.   If all submissions are found to be acceptable, the City Manager shall
submit such submissions to the Council at its next regular meeting for
approval. The Council shall reject or approve such final plat and submissions
and, if approved, shall instruct the City Clerk to certify such approval
together with the date thereof. When required, the Clerk shall also certify
upon the final plat the approval and date of Health Department approval on the
approved preliminary plat.
d.   The City Clerk shall thereupon promptly forward all copies of the final
plat to the Clerk of the County Plat Board together with the twenty-dollar
($20) recording fee.
e.   When the final plat is returned by the State Treasury Department with a
certification of approval, the final plat shall be recorded as a plat of
record. (5/3/71, § 4.7)
For state law as to submission of final plat, see M.C.L.A. § 560.166. As to
approval of final plat by City, see M.C.L.A. § 560.182. As to recording, see
M.C.L.A. § 560.172.
Sec. 19-31. Same - Status of Property Prior to Recordation; Sales Prior to
Recordation
Until recorded as a plat of record, a property is unsubdivided. No more that
one building may be constructed thereon; except that where streets and other
improvements have been installed in accordance with the final approved
preliminary plat, such streets shall be deemed to have subdivided the plat into
blocks and one building may be constructed upon each block so formed. Sale of
any land, unless by an entire block, shall be in violation of this Chapter
until approval of the final plat. (5/3/71, § 4.8)
For state law as to sales prior to recording of plat, see M.C.L.A. § 560.252, §
560.264, § 560.267.
Sec. 19-32. Waiver of Improvement Time Limits
With adequate agreements and surety bonds posted, the Council may waive
required improvements other than required storm drains, gas lines, sanitary
sewers, water lines and road base until over one-third (1/3) of the lots along
a section of unimproved street are sold. (5/3/71, § 4.9)
Sec. 19-33. Alteration of Approved Lots
No lot or lots approved prior to May 3, 1971 or approved in accordance with
this Chapter shall hereafter be altered or otherwise be changed by the
relocation, addition or removal of a lot line, except in the following
circumstances:
a.   Where multiple alterations or changes would decrease the total number of
lots affected.
b.   Where multiple alterations or changes would increase the lot area of all
lots affected.
c.   Where one (1) lot line only is relocated between two (2) lots. Where such
relocation is permitted, no other lot line of such two (2) lots may be altered
or relocated in any way thereafter.
d.   Any such above change or alteration shall be deemed a minor subdivision
and shall follow the procedures and requirements for a minor subdivision as set
forth by this Chapter. (5/3/71, § 4.10)
For state law as to alteration of plats, see M.C.L.A. § 560.221 to 560.229 . As
to further partition or division, see M.C.L.A. § 560.263.
Sec. 19-34. Unnumbered Outlots
An unnumbered outlot within a major subdivision plat is prohibited. No
subdivision plat shall be so arranged as to create a separate lot or lots of
less than three (3) acres that are not part of the plat and are separated by
the plat from any unplatted portions of the property. (5/3/71, § 4.11)
For state law as to outlots, see M.C.L.A. § 560.186.
ARTICLE V: PLAT DETAILS
Sec. 19-35. Major Subdivision Sketch Plat
The required sketch plat shall be designed in compliance with the provisions of
Articles II, VI and VII of this Chapter, be drawn at a scale of not more than
one hundred feet to the inch (1"=100') and shall show or be accompanied by the
following information:
a.   The outlines of the entire property owned or represented by the applicant.
b.   The name of the owner, the subdivider and the person preparing the plat
and a tentative plat name.
c.   The names of all adjacent property owners.
d.   The locations of all existing lots, streets, utilities, drains, streams or
bodies of water on or abutting or within two hundred feet (200') of the
property to be subdivided.
e.   The tentative location of new streets and lots for the entire property
owned or represented by the applicant.
f.   The tentative arrangement of proposed lots shall include a measured lot
width at a point sixty feet (60') from the front lot line.
g.   The tentative designation of floodplains, waterway or drainage
alterations, high water table areas or other information unique to the land
involved.
h.   A statement regarding any intent to utilize private wells or private
sanitary sewage disposal facilities upon the lots of the subdivision. (5/3/71,
§ 5.1)
Sec. 19-36. Preliminary Plat
The preliminary plat shall be designed to accordance with: the provisions of
Articles II, VI and VII of this Chapter; the conditions stipulated under sketch
plat approval; the requirements of M.C.L.A. § 560.101; and the requirements of
the Health Department, Water Resources Commission, Conservation Department,
Highway Department or the County Road Commission
where applicable. The preliminary plat shall be drawn at a scale of not more
than one hundred feet to the inch (1"=100') and shall show or be accompanied by
the following information:
a.   The name of the plat, the name and address of the proprietor, the name and
address of the surveyor and a description of the property to be subdivided.
b.   A key map at approximately one thousand feet to the inch (1"=1,000')
showing the relationship of the property to surrounding streets and to the
surrounding community.
c.   All land owned or represented by the applicant including a delineation of
that portion for which preliminary plat approval is desired. The plat shall
indicate by appropriate symbols all existing lots and street ROW within two
hundred feet (200') of the portion being submitted as a preliminary plat. For
good cause, the Commission may require an enlargement or diminution of the area
submitted for preliminary plat approval.
d.   Five-foot (5') contour elevations adjusted to U.S.G.S. datum provided that
two-foot (2') contour elevations shall be shown on land of less than two
percent (2%) slope, on land where the groundwater elevation is within six feet
(6') of grade or on land within six feet (6') in elevation of a stream, lake or
other body of water, whether existing or proposed.
e.   Street ROW locations and widths including stub or outlet streets to
adjacent properties and connections to existing streets and street names.
f.   Lot lines, lot line dimensions, lot and block numbers and lot areas to the
nearest fifty square feet (50 ft.2).
g.   The location and dimensions of ROW, easements or reserve strips.
h.   A plan or plans showing the locations, connections to existing facilities
and sizes of street pavements, sidewalks, water lines, sanitary sewer lines,
gas lines, electrical conduits, telephone lines, cable television lines, fire
hydrants, street lights, curbs and gutters, stormsewer lines, culverts,
bridges, exiting trees to be maintained and proposed shade trees.
i.   The location, depth and results of soil boring tests or percolation test
holes on every third lot within the preliminary plat where either public water
or public sanitary sewers are not available for use.
j.   Floodplain profiles or cross sections where the land abuts, includes or is
adjacent to a stream, drain or other body of water with elevations shown at
U.S.G.S. datum.
k.   Five (5) copies of any proposed or required deed restrictions or covenants
for review and comparison to City regulations.
l.   A subdivision site report or reports, where appropriate, from the Health
Department, the Conservation Department, the Water Resources Commission, the
County Drain Commission, the Highway department or the County Road Commission.
m.   Proposed street grade profiles and sewer grades.
n.   Proposed monument locations. (5/3/71, § 5.2; Ord. No. 0-95-06, 9/5/95)
Sec. 19-37. Final Plat
The final plat shall be prepared as required by M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq. It
shall be accompanied by or show the following additional information:
a.   As-built plans of all installed improvements or final plans for all
required improvements not installed or completed.
b.   Certified deed restrictions or covenants to be placed on the property.
c.   Deeds to all properties, easement or reserve strips to be placed in public
hands or dedicated therefor.
d.   Tax certificates from the County Treasurer.
e.   A two-year performance bond for all improvements installed by the
subdivider and installation agreements on sidewalks, trees, streets, topsoil,
electric conduits, gas lines, street lights, street signs and fire hydrants.
f.   An approved improvement financing agreement where required.
g.   Certification signatures of approval by the Drain Commission and the
County Road Commission. (5/3/71, § 5.3)
   ARTICLE VI: LOT SITES
Sec. 19-38. Classification of Subdivisions; Increase in Lot Area as Public
Services Decrease; Applicability of Zoning Regulations
For the purpose of this Chapter, subdivisions shall be classified as complete
utility, partial utility, potential utility or private service subdivisions. To
ensure the economical and sound extension of utility services, to avoid
premature concentrations of population and for reasons of health and
sanitation, the minimum required area to each lot shall increase as the
availability of public services decreases. In areas beyond the City corporate
limits, the zoning districts and regulations therefor shown on the zoning map
shall apply except where greater restrictions are imposed by township or county
regulations. This Chapter may impose greater lot sizes but may not decrease the
minimums of the zoning regulations. Minor subdivisions in all zones need only
conform to or exceed the minimum set in Chapter 22. (5/3/71, § 6.1)
Sec. 19-39. Complete Utility Subdivisions
A complete utility subdivision shall be located only in a primary or industrial
service area. Fifty percent (50%) of all lots in a major subdivision shall
exceed the minimum lot width and lot area designated by the zoning regulations
by at least six percent (6%). Another twenty-five percent (25%) of all lots
shall exceed the minimum lot width and area by at least twelve percent (12%).
Corner lots shall be at least twelve percent (12%) wider and twelve percent
(12%) larger than the minimum zoning requirements. The following table is
presented for convenience:
Complete Utility Subdivisions: Lot Areas and Lot Widths *
Zoning   25% of Lots        50% of Lots             25% of Lots
District Width  Area (ft.2) Width (ft.) Area (ft.2) Width (ft.) Area (ft.2)
         (ft.)
R-S      113    17,000      120         18,000      127         19,000
R-80     80     10,400      85          11,025      90          11,650
R-65     65     8,400       69          8,900       73          9,400
R-A      60     7,800       63.6        8,290       67.2        8,780
R-M      47     6,000       50          6,360       53          6,720
 
R-L: Minimum lot widths and areas shall be as provided in Section 22-86. (5/3/
71, § 6.1)
* - For state law as to lot widths and area, see M.C.L.A. § 560.186.
Sec. 19-40. Partial or Potential Utility Subdivision in Primary Service Areas
   A partial or potential utility subdivision in a primary service area is
prohibited.
(5/3/71, § 6.1)
Sec. 19-41. Private Service Subdivisions
The minimum width of lots at the building line shall be one hundred fifty feet
(150') and the minimum lot area shall be thirty-six thousand square feet
(36,000 ft.2). (5/3/71, § 6.1)
Sec. 19-42. Partial or Potential Utility Subdivision in Secondary Service Areas
A potential utility subdivision located in a secondary service area is
prohibited where a public water system or a public water system and a public
sanitary sewer system are reasonably available or where the City arranges to
make them reasonably available. In a potential utility subdivision in the
secondary service area, the minimum lot width shall be one hundred thirty feet
(130') and the minimum lot area shall be nineteen thousand five hundred square
feet (19,500 ft.2) (5/3/71, § 6.1)
ARTICLE VII: REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS IN MAJOR SUBDIVISIONS *
For state law as to authority of city to require installations of improvements,
see M.C.L.A. § 560.188.
As to improvements relative to streets, etc., M.C.L.A. § 560.182.
Sec. 19-43. Complete Utility Subdivisions
Prior to the granting of final plat approval for a complete utility
subdivision, the subdivider shall have installed or have agreements for the
installation of the following improvements in accordance with the City
construction specifications for subdivider improvements:
a.   Pavement and curbs. A graded and paved street of not less than thirty-four
feet (34') in width between curb faces with concrete curbs and gutters. A
street designated as a collector street by the Commission shall have a width of
thirty-five feet (35') between curb faces. Where a subdivision abuts a major
street, one curb and gutter and customary drainage shall be provided thereon at
a location designated by the City Manager in conformance with major street
width plans of the City.
b.   Water. A public water supply of a size specified by the City available at
the property line of each lot within the subdivision and connected to an
existing public system together with the installation of fire hydrants and stop
boxes in locations approved by the City.
c.   Sewers and drainage. Public sanitary sewers connected to an existing
public system available and staked at the property line of each lot within the
subdivision; culverts, catchbasins and stormsewers of a size specified by the
City properly connected to an existing system as approved by the City. This
shall include basement footing drains where deemed necessary.
d.   Electric, telephone and cable television conduits. Underground electric,
telephone and cable television conduits shall be installed together in the same
trench where possible and have connection terminals available at each lot.
Locations for area service terminals shall be included in the plat of the
public street ROW.
e.   Gas service. Gas distribution lines shall be installed in a manner to
permit gas service to each lot without tunneling, cutting or otherwise
disturbing street paving or the paving base. Where gas service is not
available, a dummy gas line shall be placed across the street ROW in each block
prior to installing street paving or the paving base.
f.   Sidewalks. Five-foot (5') sidewalks shall be installed on both sides of
any street.
g.   Shade trees. Two (2) shade trees shall be provided in front of each lot
between the curb and the sidewalk. Said trees shall be a type and size
designated by the City Manager and will be at least three feet (3') from any
curb or sidewalk.
h.   Topsoil. No topsoil shall be removed from the site or used as spoil.
Topsoil moved during the course of construction shall be redistributed and
stabilized by seeding or planting as specified by the City.
i.   Monuments. Monuments shall conform to M.C.L.A. §§ 560.101 et seq.
j.   Street name signs. Signs shall be placed at all intersections within or
abutting the subdivision. The type and location shall be specified by the City
Manager. (5/3/71, § 7.1; Ord. No. 0-95-06, 9/5/95)
Sec. 19-44. Partial or Potential Utility Subdivisions
The same improvements called for in Section 19-43 shall be required; except
that:
a.   If a public utility water system is not available, individual wells may be
used provided well locations are submitted to and approved by the Health
Department.
b.   If the services of a public utility sanitary sewer system are not
available, private disposal systems may be used; provided, that their locations
are approved by the Health Department; and further provided, that prior to
final plat approval a percolation test of each lot at such location is made and
found to be satisfactory in all respects. (5/3/71, § 7.2)
Sec. 19-45. Variation of Sidewalk Requirements Where all Lots are Over One
Hundred Feet Wide
If the average width of all lots in a subdivision exceeds one hundred feet
(100'), one five-foot (5') sidewalk on one side of the street may be permitted
instead of two (2) sidewalks. (5/3/71, § 7.3)
Sec. 19-46. Additional Costs of Improvement Increased to Meet Needs of Other
Areas
Where the City requires that any given improvement be increased in size or
length to meet the needs of other areas, arrangements shall be made prior to
installation or prior to approval of a final plat for the City or the
surrounding area to pay additional costs thereof. (5/3/71, § 7.3)
ARTICLE VIII: VARIANCES *
* For state law as to waiver of restrictions, M.C.L.A. § 560.254.
Sec. 19-47. Grounds Generally; Items to be Considered by Council
If the subdivider can clearly demonstrate that literal enforcement of this
Chapter is impractical or will impose undue hardship in the use of his land
because of peculiar conditions pertaining to
such land, the Council may permit such variances as, in its sound discretion,
it believes to be reasonable and within the general purpose and policy of this
Chapter.
In making the findings required in Section 19-48, the Council shall consider
the recommendation of the Commission, the location and condition of the
proposed subdivision, the nature of the proposed variance as compared with the
existing use of land in the vicinity, the number of persons to reside or work
in the proposed subdivision and the probable effect of the proposed subdivision
and variances on traffic conditions in the vicinity. (5/3/71, § 9.1)
Sec. 19-48. Necessary Conditions
No variance shall be granted unless the Council finds that all of the following
conditions exist:
a.   There are special circumstances or conditions affecting the land such that
the strict application of the provisions of this Chapter would deprive the
applicant of the reasonable use of his property.
b.   The variance is necessary for the preservation and enjoyment of a
substantial property right of the applicant.
c.   The granting of the variance will not be contrary to state regulations,
detrimental to the public welfare or injurious to other property in the area in
which said land is situated. (5/3/71, § 9.1)
Sec. 19-49. Petition; Commission Recommendation; Approval of Variance
Disapproved by Commission
A petition for any such variance shall be submitted in writing by the
subdivider at the time the sketch plat or the preliminary plat is filed for the
consideration of the Commission. The petition shall state fully the grounds for
the application and all of the facts relied upon by the petitioner. The
Commission shall make a recommendation to the Council upon any requested
variance. The Council may not grant a variance where such has been disapproved
by the Commission except by a full two-thirds vote. (5/3/71, § 9.2)
   ARTICLE IX: SITE CONDOMINIUM PROJECTS
Sec. 19-50. Definitions
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this Article, shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this Section, except where the context clearly
indicates a different meaning:
Building Envelope means the area of a condominium unit within which the
principal building or structure may be constructed, together with any accessory
structures, as described in the master deed for the site condominium project.
In a single-family residential site condominium project, the building envelope
refers to the area of each condominium within which the dwelling and any
accessory structures may be built.
Condominium Act means Act No. 59 of the Public Acts of Michigan of 1978 (MCL,
559.101 et seq., MSA, 26.50(101) et seq.)
Condominium Project means a condominium project developed under the Condominium
Act.
Condominium Structure means the principal building or structure intended for or
constructed upon a lot or building site, together with any attached accessory
structures; e.g. in a residential development, the condominium structure would
refer to the house and any attached garage.
Condominium Unit means a condominium unit established in compliance with the
Condominium Act, which consists of an area of vacant land and a volume of
vacant air space, designed and intended for separate ownership and use as
described in the site condominium project master deed, and within which a
building or other improvements may be constructed by the condominium unit
owner.
Exempt Change means a change to a site condominium project (other than a major
or minor change) that is exempt from review and approval as required for major
or minor changes under this Article. Exempt changes shall be limited to the
following:
a.   A change in the name of the project, in the name of street within the
project, or in the name of the developer of the project;
b.   A change in the voting rights of co-owners or mortgages; or
c.   Any other change in the site condominium project which, as determined by
the Planning Commission (hereinafter "Commission"), does not constitute a major
or minor change or will not otherwise change the site configuration, design,
layout, topography or any other aspect of a project that is subject to
regulation under this Chapter.
Limited Common Element means an area appurtenant to a site condominium unit and
reserved in the master deed for the site condominium project for the exclusive
use of the owner of the site condominium unit.
Lot means the same as building site and is that portion of a condominium
project designed and intended for separate ownership and/or exclusive use, as
described in the master deed. "Lot" may be further defined as:
a.   A condominium unit consisting of the area under a building envelope and
the contiguous area around the building envelope which, by itself, meets the
minimum area and yard requirements for lots as required by this Article; or
b.   The contiguous limited common element under and surrounding a condominium
unit that is or shall be assigned to the owner of the condominium unit for the
owner's exclusive use, and which, together with the condominium unit, meets the
minimum area and yard requirements for lots as required by this Article.
Major Change means a change in the site configuration, design, layout or
topography of a site condominium project (or any portion thereof), including
any change that could result in:
a.   An increase of twenty percent (20%) or more in the number of site
condominium units from the original approved Site Condominium Project Plan; and
b.   Any other change in the site configuration, design, layout, topography or
other aspect of the project subject to regulation under this Chapter,
including, without limitation, a change in the location of streets and
utilities, or in the size, location, area, horizontal boundaries or vertical
boundaries of a site condominium unit, and which is determined by the
Commission to constitute a major change to the site condominium project.
Master Deed means the legal document prepared and recorded pursuant to the
Condominium Act to which is attached as exhibits and incorporated by reference
the approved bylaws for the project and the approved condominium subdivision
plan for the project.
Minor Change means a change in the site configuration, design, layout or
topography of a site condominium project (or any portion thereof), including
any change that will result in:
a.   An increase of less than twenty percent (20%) in the number of site
condominium units from the original approved Site Condominium Project Plan or a
decrease in the number of site condominium units from the original approved
Site Condominium Project Plan; and
b.   Any other minor variation in the site configuration, design, layout,
topography or other aspect of the project to regulation under this Chapter, and
which, as determined by the Commission, does not constitute a major change.
Setback, Front, Side and Rear Yard means the distance measured from the
respective front, side and rear of the condominium structure/building envelope
to the equivalent of the front, side and rear lot line, respectively.
Site Condominium Project means a plan or project consisting of not less than
two site condominium units established in compliance with the Condominium Act.
Site Condominium Project Plan means the plans, drawings and information
prepared for a site condominium project as required by Section 66 of the
Condominium Act (MCL 559.165, MSA, 26.50(166)) and as required by this Article
for review of the project by the Commission and the City Council (hereinafter
"Council".) (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-51. Purpose and Scope
a.   The purpose of this Article is to provide procedures for the orderly use
and development of property that results in the creation of two or more lots,
each of which is ten acres or less in size and is not otherwise regulated by
this Code and the Subdivision Control Act of 1967, Act No. 288 of the Public
Acts of Michigan of 1967 (MCL 560.101 et seq., MSA, 26.430(101) et seq.) This
Article identifies minimum standards for the development of property as site
condominiums in the City of Fremont (hereinafter "City"), and sets forth
procedures to be followed by the City in applying these rules, regulations and
standards.
b.   In addition, the purpose of this Article is to:
   1.   Provide for orderly growth and harmonious development of the City
consistent with orderly growth policies;
   2.   Secure adequate traffic circulation through coordinated street systems
with proper relation to major thoroughfares, adjoining subdivisions and public
facilities;
   3.   Achieve adequate provisions for water, drainage and sanitary
facilities, and other health requirements;
   4.   Encourage the provision of recreational areas and facilities, school
sites and other public facilities;
   5.   Ensure against the creation of unsafe or undesirable conditions;
   6.   Regulate the density of development in relation to the availability of,
or lack of, utility services;
   7.   Conserve natural features;
   8.   Carry out the purpose and intent of the City's Comprehensive
Development and Growth Management Plan and this Chapter; and
   9.   Provide procedures for the achievement of these purposes.
c.   Site condominium projects are condominium developments in which each
condominium unit consists of an area of vacant land and a volume of vacant air
space within which a building or other improvements may be constructed by the
condominium unit owner. Each site condominium unit may also have an appurtenant
limited common element reserved for the exclusive use of the owner of the
condominium unit.
d.   Either the condominium unit by itself, or the condominium unit taken
together with any contiguous, appurtenant limited common element, shall be
considered to constitute a building site which is the functional equivalent of
a lot for purposes of determining compliance with the requirement of this
Chapter and other applicable laws, ordinances and regulations. Site condominium
projects may also include general common elements consisting of common open
space, recreational areas, streets and other areas available for use by all
owners of condominium units within the project. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-52. Administration
To ensure that site condominium projects comply with this Chapter, this Article
requires preliminary review of site condominium projects plans by the
Commission followed by final review and approval by the Council, as provided by
the Condominium Act. Site condominium projects may be approved as provided by
this Article in any zoning district for the uses permitted in the zoning
district in which the project is located. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-53. General Requirements
Site condominium projects shall comply with the following general requirements:
a.   Each condominium lot shall front on and have direct access to a public or
private street. Public and private streets shall comply with the design and
construction standards of Chapter 18 of the Fremont City Code "Streets and
Sidewalks" provided, however, the Council may modify the design and
construction requirements of said Chapter as determined necessary for the
public health, safety and welfare.
b.   After construction of the condominium unit, the balance of the condominium
unit site shall become a limited common element.
c.   The term "condominium unit site" shall be equivalent to the term "lot"
(zoning lot) for purposes of determining compliance of a site condominium
subdivision with the provisions of this Article pertaining to minimum lot size,
minimum lot width, maximum lot coverage, maximum lot width to depth ratio and
other area requirements.
d.   The use or uses of a condominium project shall be as regulated by the
underlying zoning district.
e.   The condominium subdivision plan shall include all necessary easements
granted to the City for the purposes of constructing, operating, inspecting,
maintaining, repairing, altering, replacing and/or removing pipelines, mains,
conduits and other installations of a similar character for the purpose of
providing public utilities, including conveyance of sewage, water and
stormwater run-off across, through and under the property subject to said
easement, and excavating and refilling ditches and trenches necessary for the
location of said structures. The condominium plan shall also include all
easements necessary for the placement of other essential public services
including, but not limited to, natural gas, electric, telephone, cable and
other such services.
f.   All utilities, lines, mains, wires, cables, conduit and related
transmission and supply facilities shall be placed underground.
g.   Approval of a site condominium project by the City does not relieve the
applicant from compliance with applicable county, state and federal regulations
governing said project. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-54. Scheduling of Fees
The scheduling of fees for the review of projects under this Article shall be
as required by Council resolution. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-55. Review of Preliminary Plans by the Planning Commission
a.   Required. Prior to final review and approval of a site condominium project
plan by the Council, the Commission in accordance with the procedures,
standards and requirements provided by this Article shall review a preliminary
site condominium project plan.
b.   Application Submittal Requirements. An application for preliminary site
plan review along with six sets of the plan shall be submitted to the City
Clerk at least two weeks prior to the next scheduled Commission meeting along
with a fee as set forth by the Council. The application shall at a minimum,
contain the following information:
   1.   The applicant's name, address and phone number;
   2.   Proof that the applicant is the owner of the property or has a legal or
financial interest in the property such as a purchase agreement;
   3.   The name, address and phone number of the owner of record if different
than the applicant;
   4.   The address of the property;
   5.   Legal description or permanent parcel number of the property;
   6.   Project description;
   7.   Size of the parcel in acres; and
   8.   Signature of the applicant and owner of the property.
c.   Technical Review. The City Clerk shall transmit the application and
project plans to the City Manager for technical review. Copies may also be sent
to the City Planner, City Zoning Enforcement Officer, Engineer, Fire Chief and
Police Chief as deemed necessary. The site plan shall be reviewed for
compliance with the requirements of this Article and a report prepared for the
Commission.
d.   Requirements for Preliminary Plans. The preliminary plan shall contain and
include the following requirements and standards:
   1.   A condominium project shall include the documents and information
required by Section 66 of the Condominium Act (MCL, § 559.166; MSA, § 26.50
(166)), including the signature and seal of the architect, land surveyor or
engineer that prepares the plan.
   2.   A statement describing the proposed method of providing potable water
supply, waste disposal facilities and public and private utilities, and a
statement from the district health department indicating the suitability of the
land for the operation of septic tanks, if proposed.
   3.   All private streets in a site condominium shall comply with the
standards for private streets as set out in Chapter 18 of the City Code.
   4.   The location of any and all general and limited common elements, as
well as the use and occupancy restrictions and maintenance provisions for all
general and limited common elements that will be included in the master deed.
   5.   A stormwater drainage and management plan, including all lines, swales,
drains, basins and other facilities and easements granted to the City for
installation, repair and maintenance of all drainage facilities.
   6.   In its review of a site condominium project plan, the Commission may
consult with the City Manager, City Planner or other appropriate persons
regarding the adequacy of the proposed common elements and maintenance
provisions, use and occupancy restrictions, utility systems and streets,
project layout and design or other aspects of the proposed project.
   7.   The Commission shall require that portions of the plan as relevant to
the reviewing authority in question be submitted to the District Health
Department, County Road Commission, County Drain Commission, State Department
of Natural Resources, State Department of Public Health and other appropriate
state and county review and enforcement agencies having direct approval of
permitting authority over any aspect of the proposed site condominium project.
   8.   The building site for each site condominium unit shall comply with all
applicable provisions of this Article for the zoning district in which it will
be located, including minimum lot area, minimum lot width, required front, side
and rear yards, minimum floor area and maximum building height. For example,
the area and width of the building site shall be used to determine compliance
with the minimum lot area and lot width requirements. Compliance with required
front, side or rear yards shall be determined by measuring the distance from
the equivalent front, side or rear yard boundaries of the building site closest
to the respective front, side or rear yard boundary of the building envelope.
Building setback lines showing dimensions from all streets and lot lines shall
be illustrated on the project plan.
   9.   If a site condominium project is proposed to have public streets, the
streets shall be paved and developed to the minimum design, construction,
inspection, approval and maintenance requirements for platted public streets as
required by the City.
   10.   If the location of the existing lines is within two hundred feet
(200') of the property proposed for the site condominium, the site condominium
project shall be connected to the City water and sanitary sewer facilities. If
public water and sanitary sewer facilities are not available, each condominium
unit shall be served by either a private central system (designed for
connection to a public system when and if a public system is made available),
or shall have a well, septic tank and drainfield located within the condominium
unit's building site. Water and sanitary sewer facilities shall be installed
according to the standards of the district health department and the City.
   11.   The name of abutting developments, if any.
   12.   A map of the entire area scheduled for development if the proposed
project is a portion of a larger holding intended for subsequent development.
   13.   The land use and existing zoning of the proposed project shall be
included. Zoning and land use on adjacent parcels should also be illustrated.
   14.   A table listing the proposed lots by number and the respective lot
area for each lot.
   15.   Additional information that will assist the applicant in proceeding in
a reasonable and sound manner toward final approval of the project.
e.   Planning Commission Review.
   1.   After reviewing the preliminary site condominium project plan, the
Commission shall prepare a written statement of recommendations regarding the
proposed site condominium project, including any suggested or required changes
in the plan. The Commission shall provide a copy of its written recommendations
to the applicant and to the Council.
   2.   If the preliminary project plan does not meet all requirements
contained in this Section, the Commission shall notify the applicant by letter
indicating any additional information or changes required. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/
02)
Sec. 19-56. Review and Approval of Final Plans by Council
a.   After receiving the Commission's recommendations on the preliminary plan,
the applicant shall submit to the City Clerk six copies of a final site
condominium development plan that complies with the requirements for a
preliminary site condominium project plan. The applicant shall also submit
copies of reviews by those agencies with jurisdiction over the project as noted
in Section 19-54(d)(7). The City Clerk shall forward the copies of the final
plan and other information to the Council.
b.   The final site condominium project plan submitted by the applicant shall
incorporate all of the recommendations, if any, made by the Commission based on
its prior review of the preliminary plan. If any of the Commission's
recommendations are not incorporated in the final plan, the applicant shall
clearly specify in writing which have not been incorporated. Except for changes
made to the plan as necessary to incorporate the recommendations of the
Commission, the final plan shall otherwise be identical to the preliminary plan
reviewed by the Commission. Changes made to the plan other than those necessary
to incorporate the recommendations of the Commission shall be reviewed by the
Commission as provided by this Article prior to approval of the plan by the
Council.
c.   After receiving the Commission's recommendations on the preliminary plan
and a final site condominium development plan from the applicant, the Council
shall review and may approve, deny or approve with conditions the plan in
accordance with the standards and requirements of Article IV of Chapter 19 for
plat approval and other applicable procedures, standards and requirements
provided by this Article.
d.   The Council may grant tentative approval of the project and shall set
forth in writing the requirements that must be met for approval.
e.   The Council shall not review, approve or reject a final project plan until
it has received a report and recommendation from the Commission on the
preliminary project plan.
f.   As a condition of approval of a final site condominium project plan the
Council may:
1.   Require that a cash deposit, certified check, irrevocable bank letter of
credit or surety bond acceptable to the Council covering the estimated cost of
improvements associated with the site condominium project for which approval is
sought be deposited with the City Clerk/City Treasurer as provided by Section
19-18 of this Chapter.
2.   Impose additional reasonable conditions of approval necessary to ensure
that public services and facilities affected by a proposed land use or activity
will be capable of accommodating increased service and facility load caused by
the land use or activity, to protect the natural environment and conserve
natural resources and energy, to ensure compatibility with adjacent uses of
land, and to promote the use of land in a socially and economically desirable
manner.
g.   Approval of a final site condominium project plan shall not constitute
approval of expandable or convertible portions of a site condominium project
unless the expandable or convertible areas were specifically reviewed and
approved by the Council in compliance with the procedures, standards and
requirements of this Article. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-57. Construction in Compliance with Approved Final Site Condominium
Project Plan
a.   No buildings or structures shall be constructed nor shall any other site
improvements or changes be made on the property in connection with a proposed
site condominium project except in compliance with a final site condominium
project plan as approved by the Council, including any conditions of approval.
b.   Required permits may be issued by the building inspector, and the
developer may proceed with the project provided:
1.   The Council has approved a final site condominium project plan and the
City Clerk and City Manager have signed the approved plan;
2.   All conditions to commencement of construction imposed by the Council have
been met; and
3.   All applicable inspections, approvals or permits from appropriate county
and state review and enforcement agencies have been obtained for the project.
(Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-58. Review and Approval of Changes to Approved Site Condominium Project
Plan
Any change proposed in connection with a project for which the Council has
previously approved a final site condominium project plan, shall be subject to
review as provided by this Section:
a.   Any change that constitutes a major change shall be reviewed by the
Commission and reviewed and approved by the Council as provided by this Article
for the original review and approval of preliminary and final plans.
b.   Any change that constitutes a minor change shall be reviewed and approved
by the Commission alone without the need for Council review.
c.   Any change that constitutes an exempt change shall not be subject to
review by the City under this Article, but a copy of changes proposed (and of
the changes made if different than proposed) shall be filed with the City
Clerk. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-59. Incorporation of Approved Provisions in the Master Deed
All provisions of a final site condominium project plan that are approved by
the Council as provided by this Article shall be incorporated by reference in
the master deed for the site condominium project. Further, all major changes to
a project shall be incorporated by reference in the master deed. A copy of the
master deed as recorded with the county register of deeds shall be provided to
the City Clerk within ten days after recording the plan with the county. (Ord.
O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-60. Approval Effective for One Year
No approvals of a final site condominium project plan by the Council shall be
effective for a period of more than one year unless construction of the project
commences within that one-year period and is diligently pursued to completion
in accordance with the terms and conditions of the approval. The Council in its
discretion may extend this one-year period for additional periods of time as
determined appropriate by the Council if the applicant applies for the
extension within the effective period of the approval. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Sec. 19-61. Variances
A variance from the provisions of this Article may be granted if the applicant
demonstrates that literal enforcement of any of the provisions of this Article
is impractical or will impose undue hardship in the use of the land because of
special or peculiar conditions pertaining to the land. Upon application, the
Council, after recommendation by the Commission, may permit a variance or
variances that are reasonable and within the general policies and purposes of
this Article. The Commission and Council may attach conditions to the variance.
The City Zoning Board of Appeals as required by this Chapter shall review
variances from regulations not contained in but required by this Article, such
as lot width or lot size. (Ord. O-02-09, 12/2/02)
Secs. 19-62 - 19-69 Reserved for future use
CHAPTER 20.
RESERVED.

   Cross-references – Plumbing, §15-1 et seq.; street excavations, generally, §

Article I: Municipal Water System
For state law as to waterworks generally, see M.C.L.A. §§ 486.301 et seq.
As to City waterworks generally, see M.C.L.A. §§ 106.1 et seq.
Division 1: Generally
Sec. 21-1. "System" Defined.
   Whenever the words "the system" or "system" are used in this Article they
shall mean the complete water supply system of the City, including, but not by
way of limitation:
   a.   All existing watermains, wells, pumps, fire hydrants and all other
works, instrumentalities and properties used or useful in connection with the
obtaining of a water supply or the distribution of water; and
   b.   Any additions, extensions and improvements to such system. (5-9-55, §
4)
Sec. 21-2. Administration of System.
   The operation, repair, maintenance and management of the system shall be
under the immediate supervision and control of the City Manager, subject to the
overall control and rights reserved by law and the City Charter to the City
Council (hereinafter "Council".) (5-9-55, § 8)
For Charter provision as to administration of public utilities, see Char. §
14.2.
Sec. 21-3. Adoption of Rules and Regulations by Resolution.
   The Council may, by resolution from time to time, adopt such rules and
regulations relative to water service and to such water supply system not in
conflict with this Article or the Charter of the City. (5-9-55, § 18)
For Charter provision as to adoption of rules and regulations by resolution,
see Char, 8.2.
Sec. 21-4. Fiscal Year.
   Such water supply system shall be operated on the basis of a fiscal year
beginning on July 1 and ending on June 30 of each year. (5-9-55, 9)
For Charter provision as to fiscal year of City, see Char. § 9.1.
Sec. 21-5. Applications for Service; Connections to System Generally.
   No premises shall be furnished water service, except premises being
furnished such service on May 9, 1955 until after proper application therefor,
signed by the owners of the premises for which such service is requested on
blank forms to be furnished by the City Clerk (hereinafter "Clerk"), shall have
been filed with the Clerk and approved by him.
   No person, except an authorized employee of the City or a licensed plumber
under the supervision of an authorized employee of the City, shall make any tap
or connection with any watermain or lateral connecting therewith constituting a
part of such water supply system; provided, that all new water services from
the shut-off box to the inside of the building on premises being connected with
such service shall be of copper tubing of the standard type and quantity used
for such services in the City. (5-9-55, § 12; 2-13-56, § 1)
Sec. 21-5.1. Cross-Connections to Water System; Adoption of Code and
Elimination of Cross-Connections.
   The City adopts by reference the water supply cross connection rules of the
State Department of Public Health a copy of which is on file in the office of
the City Clerk.
   It shall be the duty of the City to cause inspections to be made of all
properties served by the public water supply where cross-connections with the
public water supply are deemed possible. The frequency of inspections and re-
inspections based on potential health hazards involved shall be as established
by the City and as approved by the State Department of Public Health.
   The representative of the City shall have the right to enter at any
reasonable time and property served by a connection to the public water supply
system of the City for the purposes of inspecting the piping system or systems
thereof for cross-connections. On request the owner, lessees or occupants of
any property so served shall furnish to the inspection agency any pertinent
information regarding the piping system or systems on such property. The
refusal of such information or refusal of access, when requested shall be
deemed evidence of the presence of cross-connections.
   The City is hereby authorized and directed to discontinue water service
after reasonable notice to any property wherein any connection in violation of
this Section exits, and to take such other precautionary measures deemed
necessary to eliminate any danger of contamination of the public water supply
system. Water service to such property shall not be restored until the cross
connection has been eliminated in compliance with the provisions of this
Section.
   The potable water supply made available on the properties served by the
public water supply shall be protected from possible contamination as specified
by this Section and by the state and City's Plumbing Code. Any water outlet
which could be used for potable or domestic purposes and which is not supplied
by the potable system must be labeled in a conspicuous manner as:
   WATER UNSAFE FOR DRINKING
   Nothing in this Section shall supercede the state Plumbing Code adopted
pursuant to Sec. 15-1 of the City Code, but is supplementary thereto.
   Any person or customer found guilty of violating any of the provisions of
this Section or any written order of the City, in pursuance thereof shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (4-7-75)
Sec. 21-6. Addition of Fluoride.
   Upon receiving the approval of the Michigan Department of Public Health and
until further direction of the City, the Water Department of the City is hereby
authorized and directed to provide the means and to proceed with the addition
of approximately 0.9 and not more than 1.2 parts of fluoride to every million
parts of water being distributed in the water supply system of the City. (11-6-
67, § 1)
   For state law as to addition of fluoride to water, see M.C.L.A. §§
333.12721.
Sec. 21-7. Opening Main, Valve or Hydrant; Interfering with System Pipes,
Apparatus, Machinery, etc.
   No person, except authorized agents or employees of the City and firemen in
the legitimate discharge of their duties, shall open or close any main, valve
or hydrant or in any manner molest or interfere with any building, machinery,
pipes, apparatus or fixtures constituting a part of the water supply system,
except those situated upon private property and not within the control or
jurisdiction of the City. (5-9-55, § 13)
As to destruction, etc., of City property, see § 13-7 to § 13-9 of this Code.
