Sec. 21-8. Entry for Inspection of Premises Connected with System.
   Any authorized agent or employee of the City is hereby authorized to enter
and inspect, in proper hours, all premises connected with the water supply
system and in particular to inspect valves, pipes, fixtures and meters. (5-9-
55, § 14)
Sec. 21-9. Installation, Replacement and Repair of Meters.
   All premises to which water service is furnished by the water supply system,
shall have installed thereon in a location designated by an authorized employee
of the city a water meter, or meters where there is more than water service
connection, of the type prescribed by the City Council, and furnished by the
city. No water service shall be furnished to such premises until such water
meter, or meters, shall have been properly installed. No change in the
installation or in the location of any meter shall be made without the approval
of an authorized employee of the city.
   Whenever the City Clerk shall determine that any water meter one inch or
greater in capacity has become obsolete or incapable of properly metering the
water used, the owner of the premises upon which the same is situated shall pay
the cost of any necessary repairs or of installation of a new meter of the kind
and type prescribed by the City Council. The city shall replace meters three-
fourths inch in capacity or less when the City Clerk deems the same obsolete or
otherwise inadequate.
   All meters damaged by the property owner or allowed to freeze shall be
repaired by the city at the expense of the property owner, at city's cost plus
fifteen percent for overhead and administration. All charges for repairs of
water meters and for new meters shall be due immediately after the expiration
of ten days after notice thereof has been given by the City Clerk; and in the
event payment thereof is not thereupon made, the amount of such charges for
repairs or cost of a new meter shall be added to the next quarterly water bill
chargeable against the premises of such owner and shall be due and payable and
be collected in the same manner as the service charges specified in such bill
and shall likewise become a lien upon such premises until paid and shall be
enforced in the same manner as liens for water service charges and rates. The
charges for installation and/or repair of meters shall be made from time to
time by resolution adopted by the City Council. (Ord. No. O-99-03, 9-20-99)
Sec. 21-9.1. Tampering with Meters or Breaking Seals
   Anyone, not an authorized employee of the City, in any manner tampering with
a water meter or breaking a water meter seal, shall be guilty of a misdemeanor.
Sec. 21-10. Service Connections Generally – Installation on Streets to be Paved
or Improved.
   Before any streets or alleys are paved or otherwise improved, the Clerk
shall notify each owner of premises abutting upon the proposed improvement, if
his whereabouts be known to the Clerk, to install a copper water service from
the watermain to the property line of such premises, in the event such copper
water service has not been previously installed and is not in good condition.
At the expiration of ten (10) days after such notice, if such owner shall have
failed or neglected to install such copper water service and likewise in the
event the whereabouts of such owner is unknown to the Clerk, the City may cause
such service to be installed at the expense of such property owner. In that
event, such cost shall become an indebtedness owing from such owner to the City
recoverable by the City in an action of assumpsit. (5-9-55, § 16)
Sec. 21-11. Same – Maintenance; Cutting Pavement or Improved Surface to
Install; Repairs.
   All water service connections between any watermain in the water supply
system and the premises served thereby shall be kept in good condition and
repair and free of leaks at the sole cost and expense of the owner of the
premises, and all such repairs shall be under the supervision of an authorized
employee of the City. Any such repairing of water services may be done by the
City at the expense of the owner of such premises, if such owner shall fail to
cause such repairs to be made when necessary, and the entire cost thereof shall
be a lien upon such premises and may be assessed against such premises in the
same manner as above specified with reference to new copper water services. (5-
9-55, § 16)
Sec. 21-12. Same – Connection to Hydrant; Meters for Large Projects; Persons to
be Charged; Termination Notice to Clerk.
   For service as allowed by Sec. 21-15(a) an authorized employee of the City
shall install the required size connection and control valve on the hydrant and
the user must connect to such control valve and connection for his supply. Such
connection and control valve must be removed at the end of each day's operation
by the user. Any loss or damage to the connection, valve or operating wrench
will be charged to the person making the application for the use of the
hydrant.
   In the case of large construction projects the Clerk may, at his discretion,
require an appropriate meter to be installed, and the regular rates for water
service will be charged.
   Charges for water used during construction will be made against the owner of
the premises upon which such construction is being undertaken unless other
arrangements are made with the Clerk and approved by him.
   The Clerk shall be immediately notified when the requirements for water
service are terminated. (5-9-55, § 17)
Sec. 21-13. Construction of Sewer, Drains, etc., Near City Well or Water
Supply.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to lay or construct any sewer or drain
or other facilities for the conduct or disposition of any sewage or other waste
within a radius of two hundred feet (200') of any City well or source of supply
of the water distribution system of the City; provided, that where it shall be
determined by the City Engineer that an impervious earth structure exists
between the source of water supply and the surface of the earth in the area
surrounding the source of water supply extending beyond the radius of one
hundred feet (100') from such source, a permit may be granted by the Council to
construct a sanitary sewer according to specifications prescribed by the City
Engineer and stated in such permit at least one hundred feet (100') away from
such City well or source of water supply; and provided that nothing herein
contained shall prohibit the construction of any drain exclusively for the
purpose of conducting or disposing of surface water directed away from any such
City well or source of water supply. (5-13-46, § 1)
Sec. 21-14. Depositing Refuse or Garbage near City Well or Water Supply.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to dump or deposit any garbage or other
refuse or waste upon any premises within a radius of two hundred feet of any
City well or source of water supply connected with the water distribution
system of the City. (5-13-46, § 2)
   Division 2: Rates, Charges and Bills
For Charter provisions as to utility rates, see Char., § 14.3.
As to collection of charges, see Char., § 14.4.
For state law as to establishment of water rates, see M.C.L.A. § 106.6.
As to collection of charges, see M.C.L.A. §§ 123.161 to 123.167.
Sec. 21-15. Establishment of Fees and Charges Generally.
a.   The Council shall, by resolutions passed from time to time, establish the
amount of the fees and charges to be paid by owners and occupants of premises
using the municipal water system and by the City for its fire hydrants. Tapping
fees for water taps, service pipes and installations of service lines between a
watermain and curb shutoff boxes shall be as are established from time to time
by resolution of the Council. Fees for water obtained from fire hydrants of the
system for construction work shall also be established by resolution of the
Council from time to time.
b.   In no case shall the fees and charges established by the Council pursuant
to the provisions of Subsection a. of this Section fall below those rates
established for such services by Ordinance Number 201 of the City dated May 9,
1955.
c.   A copy of any resolution establishing fees and charges pursuant to the
provisions of this Section shall be kept on file in the Office of the City
Clerk where they shall be available for public inspection.
Sec. 21-16. Remedies for Collection of Delinquent Charges.
   The rates and charges for water service furnished to any premises shall at
once become a lien thereon, and any such charges delinquent for six (6) months
or more shall be certified annually by the Clerk to the City Assessor, who
shall enter such delinquent charges upon the next general City tax roll against
the premises to which such service shall have been rendered. Such rates and
charges shall be collected and such liens shall be enforced in the same manner
as provided for the collection of taxes assessed upon such roll and the
enforcement of the lien therefor. The Clerk shall, within the period of thirty
(30) days prior to June 1 of each year, prepare a certificate containing: the
legal descriptions of each of the premises against which any such rates and
charges for water service have been delinquent for a period of six (6) months
or more prior to May 1 or such year; the name and address of the owner or
occupant to whom such water bills have been rendered, or against whom such
charges have been made; and the amount of such delinquent rates and charges and
shall deliver such certificate to the City Assessor on or before June 15 of
each year. It shall thereupon become the duty of such City Assessor to assess
against the several premises therein described the amounts certified to be
delinquent for such rates and charges against such premises, respectively, upon
the general City tax roll for that year.
   In all cases when a tenant is responsible for the payment of any such rates
and charges and the Council is so notified in writing and such notice in
writing includes a true copy of the lease of the affected premises, if there be
one, then no such rate or charge shall become a lien against such premises from
and after the date of such notice. In the event of filing of such notice of
tenancy, the City shall render no further water service to such premises until
a cash deposit in the sum of thirty dollars ($30) shall have been made with the
Clerk as security for the payment of such charges. Such deposit shall be
refunded by the Clerk to the person depositing the same or his assigns in the
event of the discontinuance of such water service or the termination of the
lease of such tenant; provided, that all rates and charges accrued against the
premises affected up to the date of such refund shall have been paid in full.
   In addition to any other lawful enforcement methods, the payment of charges
for water service to any premises may be enforced at any time after such
charges shall become delinquent by discontinuing the water service to such
premises until all of such charges have been paid in full plus an additional
charge of ten dollars ($10) for the reinstatement of such water service. (5-9-
55, § 11)
Sec. 21-17. Free Service.
   No free service shall be furnished by the system to any person or to any
public agency or instrumentality. (5-9-55, § 19)
For Charter provision as to free service, see Char., § 14.3
Sec. 21-18. Reading of Meters.
   Water meters shall, when possible, be read quarterly by an employee of the
City as soon as practicable after the close of each of the quarters above
specified and reports of such readings shall be promptly filed with the Clerk.
(5-9-55, § 10)
Sec. 21-19. Issue and Payment of Bills.
   Water bills showing the amount due for the preceding quarter according to
the meter readings shall, as soon as practicable after each quarterly meter
reading, be prepared by the Clerk, and by him delivered personally to or mailed
to the last known post office address of the owner or occupant of the premises
to which such water service is being furnished; such water bills shall be due
and payable within thirty (30) days after the date of such bill, and if not
paid within thirty (30) days, a penalty of ten percent (10%) of the amount of
each bill so remaining unpaid shall be added to the total amount due thereon.
The failure of such owner or occupant to receive any water bill shall not
relieve such owner or occupant from liability for the payment of such bill and
the penalty thereon, which liability may be enforced in the manner hereinafter
specified. (5-9-55, § 10)
Sec. 21-20. Fees for reinstatement of service after termination.
   There shall be a service fee of ten dollars ($10) for each time water
service is reinstated after such service has been terminated.
Article II: Municipal Sewage Disposal System
For state law as to sewage systems generally, see M.C.L.A. § 325.201.
As to authority of city to construct and maintain sewage system, see M.C.L.A. §
455.217.
Division 1: Generally
Sec. 21-21. Definitions.
   For the purposes of this Article, the following words and phrases shall have
the meanings respectively ascribed to them by this Section, unless the context
clearly indicates otherwise:
   B.O.D. - biochemical oxygen demand. The quantity of oxygen utilized in the
biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in
five (5) days at twenty degrees centigrade (20°C) expressed in parts per
million (ppm) by weight.
   Building drain. The part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage
system that receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drain pipes
inside the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer,
beginning five feet outside the inner face of the building wall.
   Building sewer. The extension from the building drain to the public sewer or
other place of disposal.
   Combination sewer/combined sewer. A sewer receiving both surface runoff and
sewage.
   Garbage. Solid wastes from the preparation, cooking and dispensing of food
and from the handling, storage, processing and sale of produce.
   Industrial wastes. The liquid wastes, solids or semisolids from industrial
processes as distinct from sanitary sewage.
   Natural outlet. Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other
body of water, either surface or groundwater.
   pH. The logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams
per liter of solution.
   Properly shredded garbage. The wastes from the cooking, preparation and
dispensing of food that have been cut or shredded to such a degree that all
particles will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing
in public sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (½") in any
dimension.
   Public sewer. A sewer in which all owners of abutting property have equal
rights and which is controlled by public authority.
   Sanitary sewer. A sewer that carries sewage and to which storm, surface and
groundwaters are not intentionally admitted.
   Sewage. Any combination of water carried wastes from residences, business,
buildings, institutions and industrial establishments together with such
ground, surface and storm waters as may be present.
   Sewage treatment plant. Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
treating sewage.
   Sewage works. All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing
of sewage.
   Sewer. Any pipe, tile, tube or conduit for carrying sewage.
   Storm sewer or storm drain. A sewer that carries storm and surface waters
and drainage but which excludes sewage and polluted industrial wastes.
   Suspended solids. Solids that either float on the surface of or are
suspended in water, sewage or other liquids and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
   SWRC. The State Water Resources Commission or any of their affiliates, the
State Health Department, State Conservation Commission or the State Highway
Department.
   The system or systems. The complete sewage disposal system of the City
including the sewage treatment plant and all appurtenances and all sanitary
sewers of the City now in existence or hereafter acquired.
   Watercourse. A channel in which a flow of water occurs either continuously
or intermittently.
(6-12-61, § 101 to 122; 2-10-58, § 3)
Sec. 21-22. Fiscal Year.
   The system shall be operated on the basis of an operating year commencing on
the first day of July and ending on the last day of the following June. (2-10-
58, § 12)
For Charter provision as to fiscal year of City, see Char., § 9.1.
Sec. 21-23. Conflict of Article with State or County Requirements.
   No statement contained in this Article shall be construed to interfere with
any additional requirements that may be imposed by the County Board of Health
or by the SWRC. (6-12-61, § 304)
Sec. 21-24. Administration of System.
   The operation, repair and management of the system shall be under the
supervision and control of the City Manager subject to overall supervision and
control of the Council. The Council may make such rules, orders and regulations
as they deem necessary to assure the efficient management and operation of the
system. (2-10-58, § 7)
For Charter provision as to administration of system, see Char., § 14.2.
For state law as to administration of system, see M.C.L.A. § 123.737.
Sec. 21-25. Deposit of Sewage Wastes Generally; Improperly Treated Sewage
Flowing from Outlet of Unknown Origin.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or deposit or permit to be
deposited in any unsanitary manner upon any public or private property within
the City any sewage wastes. Such waste shall be disposed of into a public
operated sewage system when available or when not available into a private
sewage system as hereinafter provided. Whenever the building inspector shall
determine that improperly treated sewage is flowing from the outlet of any
public or private drain of unknown course and origin, he may issue public
notices requiring persons owning premises from which such sewage originates to
connect such sewage flow to a publicly operated sewerage system, if available,
or in the absence thereof to comply with the provisions of Article III. Public
notice shall consist of the posting of at least five (5) conspicuous notices in
the probable area served by such drain. After not less than sixty (60) days
following posting of the notices the building inspector may plug or cause to be
plugged the outlet of such drain until such time as the source(s) of the sewage
have been located. Owners of properties known to be discharging improperly
treated sewage in such drain posted by the building inspector, shall be given
written notice of corrections required within the time allowed by the posted
notices. Failure to comply shall be considered a violation of this Section. (2-
11-63, § 2.2)
Sec. 21-26. Deposit of Excrement on Public or Private Property.
   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or deposit or permit to be
deposited in an unsanitary manner upon any public or private property within
the City or in any area under the jurisdiction of the City any human or animal
excrement. (6-12-61, § 201)
Sec. 21-27. Discharges into Natural Watercourse or other Areas Within
Jurisdiction of City.
   It shall be unlawful to discharge into any natural watercourse within the
City or on any area under the jurisdiction of the City any sanitary sewage,
industrial waste or other polluted waters, except where suitable treatment has
been provided in accordance with standards established by the SWRC. (6-12-61, §
202)
Sec. 21-28. Installation and Connection of Toilet Facilities in Houses, etc.,
Within Two Hundred Feet of Sewer.
   The owners of all houses, buildings or properties used for human occupancy,
employment, recreation or other purposes situated within the City and abutting
on any street, alley or right-of-way in which there is now located or may in
the future be located a public sanitary or combined sewer of the City is hereby
required at his own expense to install suitable toilet facilities therein and
to connect such facilities directly to the public sewer in accordance with the
provisions of this Article, within ninety (90) days after date of official
notice to do so has been issued by the City health officer or City Manager;
provided, that such public sewer is within two hundred feet (200') of the
nearest building to be served. (6-12-61, § 204)
Sec. 21-29. Connection to Public Sewer upon its Becoming Available.
   Where a public sewer passes within two hundred feet (200') of a property
served by a private sewage disposal system, as provided in Sec. 21-28, a direct
connection shall be made to the public sewer in compliance with this Article.
Any septic tank, privy, privy vault, cesspool or similar private sewage
disposal facility shall be abandoned and filled with suitable material. (6-12-
61, § 302)
Sec. 21-30. Permits for Connection, etc. – Required.
   No authorized person shall uncover, make any connections with or opening
into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or any appurtenance thereof
without first obtaining a written permit from the City Manager or his duly
authorized representatives. (6-12-61, § 401)
Sec. 21-31. Same – Forms; Fees.
   All connections with the sanitary or combined sewers of the City shall be
made only on written authorization and permits issued by the City on such forms
and on payments of such fees as shall be established from time to time by the
City. (6-12-61, § 402)
Sec. 21-32. Installation, Maintenance and Connection of Building Sewers;
Location of Sanitary Sewer Service Leads.
   All costs and expenses incident to the installation, maintenance and
connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the owner of the property.
The owner shall indemnify the City from all loss or damage that may directly or
indirectly be occasioned by the installation and maintenance of the building
sewer. The City will give locations and depths of sanitary sewer service leads
according to the records on file in the City Hall. The City will assume no
responsibility for the accuracy of the dimensions given by the City. (6-12-61,
§ 403; Ord. of 1-19-87)
Sec. 21-33. Installation of Water or Sewage Meters.
   All premises connected to the system shall have a water meter or a sewage
meter as determined by the City Manager. Such meter shall be furnished and
installed in a suitable location by the property owner. (6-28-71, § 1)
Sec. 21-34. Reserved.
Sec. 21-35. Discharge of Water into Sanitary Sewer.
   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any stormwater, surface
water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, cooling water or
unpolluted industrial process waters into any sanitary sewer. (6-12-61, § 501)
Sec. 21-36. Discharge of Unpolluted Drainage and Industrial Cooling or Process
Waters into Combined or Storm Sewers.
   Stormwater and all other unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to such
sewers as are specifically designated as combined sewers or storm sewers or to
a natural outlet approved by the City or the SWRC. Industrial cooling water or
unpolluted process waters may be discharged upon approval of the City into a
storm sewer, combined sewer or natural outlet. (6-12-61, § 502)
Sec. 21-37. Materials Not to be Discharged into Public Sewers.
   Except as hereinafter provided, no person shall discharge or cause to be
discharged any of the following described waters or wastes into any public
sewer:
   a.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred fifty
degrees (150º) Fahrenheit.
   b.   Any water or waste that may contain more than one hundred (100) ppm by
weight of fat, oil or grease.
   c.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas.
   d.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded.
   e.   Any ashes, cinders, sand mud, straw, shavings, metal, glass, rags,
feathers, tar, plastic, wood, wood pulp, paunch manure or any other solid or
viscous substance capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers or other
interference with the proper operation of the sewage works.
   f.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5 or higher than 9.0 or
having any other corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazards to the
structures, equipment and personnel of the sewage works.
   g.   Any waters or wastes containing a toxic or poisonous substance in
sufficient quantity to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process,
constitute a hazard to humans, animals, fish or aquatic life or create any
hazard in the receiving waters of the sewage treatment plant.
   h.   Any waters or wastes containing suspended solids of such character and
quantity that unusual attention or expense is required to handle such materials
at the sewage disposal plant.
   i.   Any noxious or malodorous gas or substance capable of creating a public
nuisance.
   j.   Any live animals or fish.
(6-12-61, § 503; Ord. No. O-91-09, 12-16-91)
Sec. 21-38. Grease, Oil and Sand Interceptors – Required; Construction.
   Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of
the City Manager or the SWRC, they are necessary for the proper handling of
liquid wastes containing grease in excessive amounts, inflammable wastes or
other harmful ingredients; except, that such interceptors shall not be required
for private living quarters or dwelling units.
   All interceptors shall be a type and capacity approved by the City Manager
or SWRC and shall be located as to be readily accessible for cleaning and
inspection. Grease and oil interceptors shall be constructed of impervious
materials capable of withstanding abrupt and extreme changes in temperature.
They shall be substantially constructed, watertight and equipped with easily
removable covers which when bolted in place shall be airtight and watertight.
(6-12-61, § 504)
Sec. 21-39. Same – Maintenance.
   Where installed, all grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be maintained
by the owner at his expense in continuously efficient operation. (6-12-61, §
505)
Sec. 21-40. Discharges Subject to Approval; Preliminary Treatment Generally.
   The admission into the public sewers of any waters or wastes having the
following characteristics shall be subject to the review and approval of the
Council or the SWRC:
   a.   Five-day BOD greater than three hundred (300) ppm by weight;
   b.   Containing more than three hundred fifty (350) ppm by weight of
suspended solids;
   c.   Containing any quantity of substances having the characteristics
described in Sec. 21-37; or
   d.   Having a daily average flow greater than two percent (2%) of the
average daily sewage flow of the City.
   Where necessary in the opinion of the Council or the SWRC, the owner shall
provide, at his expense, such preliminary treatment as may be necessary to:
   a.   Reduce the BOD to three hundred (300) ppm and the suspended solids to
three hundred fifty (350) ppm by weight;
   b.   Reduce objectionable characteristics or constituents to within the
maximum limits provided for in Sec. 21-37; or
   c.   Control the quantities and rates of discharge of such waters or wastes.
   Plans, specifications and any other pertinent information relating to
proposed preliminary treatment facilities shall be submitted for approval of
the Council and the SWRC. No construction of such facilities shall be commenced
until such approvals are obtained in writing. (6-12-61, § 506)
Sec. 21-41. Maintenance of Preliminary Treatment Facilities.
   Where preliminary treatment facilities are provided for any waters or
wastes, the owner at his expense shall maintain them in satisfactory and
effective operation. (6-12-61, § 507)
Sec. 21-42. Installation and Maintenance of Control Manholes.
   When required by the Council or the SWRC, the owner of any property served
by a building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable control
manhole in the building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and
measurement of wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessibly and
safely located and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by
the Council. The manhole shall be installed by the owner at his expense and
shall be maintained by him so as to be safe and accessible at all times. (6-12-
61, § 508)
Sec. 21-43. Standards for Analyses of Water and Wastes; Taking of Samples.
   All measurements, tests and analyses of the characteristics of waters and
wastes to which reference is made in Sections 21-37 and 21-40 shall be
determined in accordance with "Standard Methods for the Examination of Water
and Sewage" and shall be determined at the control manhole provided for in Sec.
21-42 or upon suitable samples taken at such control manhole. In the event that
no special manhole has been required, the control manhole shall be considered
to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to the point at which
the building sewer is connected. (6-12-61, § 509)
Sec. 21-44. Special Agreements for Discharge of Industrial Wastes.
   No statement contained in this Article shall be construed as preventing any
special agreement or arrangement between the City and any industrial concern
relative to industrial wastes. (6-12-61, § 510)
Sec. 21-45. Destruction, etc., of Structures, Appurtenances or Equipment of
System.
   No unauthorized person shall maliciously, willfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with, climb upon or enter any
structure, appurtenance or equipment which is a part of the municipal sewage
works. Any person violating this provision shall be subject to immediate arrest
under charge of disorderly conduct where the damage amounts to less than fifty
dollars ($50) and if the damage amounts to more than fifty dollars ($50) then
such charge shall be malicious destruction of property. (6-12-61, § 601)
As to destruction of City property generally, see Sections 13-7 to 13-9 of this
Code.
Sec. 21-46. Right of City to Enter for Inspections, Measurements, Testing, etc.
   The Council and other duly authorized employees of the City and agents of
the SWRC bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to
enter upon all properties for the purpose of inspection, observation,
measurement, sampling and testing in accordance with the provisions of this
Article at any time during reasonable or usual business hours. (6-12-61, § 701)
Sec. 21-47. Violation of Article – Notice; Correction Generally.
   Any person found to be violating any provision of this Article, except Sec.
21-45, shall be served by the City with written notice stating the nature of
such violation and providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory
correction thereof. The offender shall, within the period of time stated in
such notice, permanently cease all violations. (6-12-61, § 801)
Sec. 21-48. Same – Continuation after Time Limit Set by Notice.
   Any person who shall continue any violation beyond the time limit provided
for in Sec. 21-47 shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. (6-12-61, § 802)
Sec. 21-49. Same – Indemnification of City for Expense Caused by Violation.
   Any person violating any of the provisions of this Chapter shall become
liable to the City for any expense, loss or damage occasioned to the City by
reason of such violation. (6-12-61, § 803)
DIVISION 2: RATES, CHARGES AND BILLS *
   *Charter references – Utility rates, § 14.3; collection of charges, § 14.4.
Sec. 21-50. Free Service.
   No free service shall be furnished by the system to any person or to any
public agency or instrumentality. (2-10-58, § 9)
Sec. 21-51. Charges for Service to Premises Generally; Installation of Meters.
   a.   The charges for sewer service for premises connected to the system
shall be measured by the quantity of water shown on the water or sewage meters
and shall be as follows:
 
Water meters under 2" - Domestic Standard Domestic, Commercial or Industrial Use:
   Readiness-to-Serve (min. quarterly bill based on metered water use up to $
4,000 gals./quarter)                                                           41.20
   Rate/1,000 gals. water used per quarter of 5,000 gals. or more/quarter   5.04
Water meters 2" and over - Commercial or Industrial Use only:
   Readiness-to-Serve (min. quarterly bill based on metered water use up to 264.00
4,000 gals./quarter)
   Rate/1,000 gals. water used per quarter of 5,000 gals. or more/quarter   6.30
 
   b.   All premises connected to the system shall have a water meter or a
sewage meter as determined by the City Manager. Such meter shall be furnished
and installed in a suitable location by the property owner. (2-10-58, § 8; 12-
6-71, § 1; 6-4-73, § 1; 7-18-77, § 1; 9-17-84; Ord. of 6-6-88; Ord. No. O-94-
02, 6-20-94; Ord. No. O-95-04, 6-5-95; Ord. No. O-11-05, 7-5-11; Ord. No. O-17-
04, 6-19-17; Ord. No. O-20-02, 5-18-20; Ord. No. O-23-07, 11-6-23)
Sec. 21-52. Commercial customers; Schools and Churches.
   Commercial customers are those establishments whose primary function is
other than providing a place of residence. Where a combination of commercial
uses include apartments, the customer shall be classified as commercial.
   Quarterly charges for sewer service shall be based on the actual amount of
water used during the quarter.
   Schools and churches shall be billed as residential customers. (12-6-71, §
1)
Sec. 21-53. Miscellaneous Services; Special Rates for Large User of Water not
Discharged into System.
   For miscellaneous services for which, in the judgement of the Council, a
special rate should be established, such rates shall be fixed and established
from time to time by the Council. Where a user uses a large amount of water,
which is not discharged into the sanitary sewer system, a special rate for
sewer service for such user may be established. (2-10-58, 8; 12-6-71, § 1)
Sec. 21-54. Special sewer rate for commercial laundromats and drycleaner
establishments.
   The charges for sanitary sewer service for commercial laundromats and
drycleaner establishments shall be at a ten (10%) percent discounted rate from
the established rates in sec.
21-51.
(Ord. No. O-19-04, 2-4-19)
Sec. 21-55. Reserved.
Sec. 21-56. Additional Charges for Discharges of Unusual Burden on System;
Preliminary Treatment; Denial of Right to Discharge.
   If the character of sewage from any manufacturing or industrial plant or any
other building or premises shall be such as to impose an unreasonable
additional burden upon the sewers or sewage treatment plant of the system, then
an additional charge may be made over and above the regular rates, or it may be
required that such sewage be treated by the person responsible therefor before
being emptied into the sewer, or the right to empty such sewage may be denied
if necessary for the protection of the sewer and sewage disposal facilities of
the system or the public health and safety. (2-10-58, § 10)
Sec. 21-57. Fees for Connection to System Generally.
   Charges for connections to the system shall be at actual cost plus an
inspection fee for each sewer connection made. Where a sewer line runs along
one side of a street or highway, the City Manager, subject to the approval of
the Council, shall be authorized to equalize such actual cost between
connectors on either side of the street or highway as the equities may require.
The amount of the inspection fee shall be determined from time to time by
resolution of the Council. (2-10-58, § 8; 12-6-71, § 1; 11-19-79)
Sec. 21-58. Fees for Connection to Trunkline Sanitary Sewer.
   In addition to the regular special assessment to be established by the
Council for the construction of sanitary sewer lines leading from the trunkline
sanitary sewer that runs from the sewer plant to the intersection of Oak Street
and Connie Avenue, there is hereby established a connection fee for every
connection made to any sewer line that runs into the trunkline sanitary sewer.
   The connection fee shall be an amount equal to twenty dollars ($20) per acre
of area of land serviced by each connection; provided, that in no event shall
the connection fee be less than ten dollars ($10). (9-11-61, § 1, 2)
Sec. 21-59. Issuance and Payment of Bills.
   Billing for sewer charges shall be made quarterly and shall be due and
payable thirty days after date of such bill. For all bills not paid when due, a
penalty of ten percent (10%) of the amount of such bill shall be added. (2-10-
58, § 8; 12-6-71, § 1)
Sec. 21-60. Remedies for Collection of Delinquent Accounts; Tenants Solely
Liable for Payment.
   The charges for sewer services, which are under the provisions of M.C.L.A. §
141.121, made a lien on all premises served thereby, unless notice is given
that a tenant is responsible, are hereby recognized to constitute such lien.
Whenever any such charge against any piece of property shall be delinquent for
six (6) months, the City official in charge of the collection thereof shall
certify annually, on April first of each year, to the tax assessing officer of
the City the fact of such delinquency whereupon such charge shall be entered by
him upon the next tax roll as a charge against such premises and shall be
collected and the lien thereof enforced in the same manner as general City
taxes against such premises are collected and the lien thereof enforced;
provided, however, where notice is given that a tenant is responsible for such
charge and service as provided by M.C.L.A. § 5.2751, no further service shall
be rendered such premises until a cash deposit of not less than twenty-five
dollars ($25) shall have been made as security for payment of such charges and
service.
   In addition to other remedies provided, the City shall have the right to
shut off and discontinue the supply of water to any premises for the nonpayment
of sewer rates when due. If such charges are not paid within thirty (30) days
after the due date thereof, then water services to such premises shall be
discontinued. Water services so discontinued shall not be restored until all
sums then due and owing shall be paid plus a turn-on charge as may from time to
time be determined by resolution of the Council. (2-10-58, § 8; 12-6-71, § 1)
Article III: Private Sewage Disposal Systems.
For Charter provisions as to regulation of construction, etc., of buildings and
their appurtenances, see Char., § 2.2 (28).
Sec. 21-61. Definitions.
   For purposes of this Article, the following words and phrases shall have the
meanings respectively ascribed to them by this Section:
   Automatic siphon. A bell and siphon arrangement that controls intermittent
flow of effluent from the dosing tank into the subsurface disposal system
according to the compression of air under the bell.
   Building inspector. The building inspector of the City or his duly
authorized representative.
   Dosing tank. A watertight tank or receptacle used or intended for use for
the purpose of receiving and retaining the effluent or overflow of a septic
tank until discharged by an automatic siphon or pump.
   Septic tank. A watertight tank or receptacle used for the purpose of
receiving wastes from flush toilets, sinks, lavatories, bathtubs, showers,
laundry drains and any other similar waste lines and intended to provide for
the separation of substantial portions of the suspended solids in such wastes
and the partial destruction by bacterial action on the solids so separated.
   Sewage. The liquid wastes from all habitable buildings and shall include
human excreta and wastes from sink, lavatory, bathtub, shower and laundry and
any other water carried wastes of organic nature, either singly or in any
combination thereof.
   Sewer. Any pipe, tile, tube or conduit for carrying sewage.
   Subsurface disposal system. An arrangement for distributing septic tank
effluent or overflow below the ground surface. (2-11-63, § 1.1 to 1.8)
Sec. 21-62. Construction or Maintenance of Privies, Privy Vaults, Septic Tanks,
Cesspools, etc., Generally.
   Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be unlawful to construct or
maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool or other facilities
intended or used for the disposal of sewage. (6-12-61, § 203)
For state law as to privies, septic tanks, etc., generally, see M.C.L.A. §
333.12771
Sec. 21-63. Water Flush Systems where Connection to Public Sewer is Not
Required.
   Every residence, place of business or other building or place where persons
congregate, reside or are employed, and which is not required to be connected
to any public sanitary sewer shall be provided with a private water flush
toilet by the owner or agent of the premises. Such water flush toilet system
shall be built, rebuilt, constructed and maintained in such a manner as to meet
the requirements of construction and maintenance hereinafter prescribed. (7-13-
42, § 3)
Sec. 21-64. Use of Building Not Provided with Flush Toilet Connected to a
Sewage System.
   It shall be unlawful to maintain, occupy or use any residence, place of
business or other building or place where persons reside, congregate or are
employed in the City, which is not provided with means for the disposal of
human excreta by a flush toilet connected with a sewerage system approved by
the Michigan Department of Health. (7-13-42, § 1)
Sec. 21-65. Construction Permits – Required; Issuance.
   No person shall begin construction of any sewage disposal facility as
defined in these minimum standards until such person or his duly authorized
representative has made written application to the building inspector or his
duly authorized representative and has received a duly signed construction
permit from the building inspector. Such permit shall be issued only when a
suitable sketch showing all pertinent dimensions of the installation has been
submitted for consideration by the building inspector. Such permit shall be
signed by the applicant and by the building inspector or his duly authorized
representative. (2-11-63, § 3.1)
Sec. 21-66. Same – Fees.
   A fee of five dollars ($5) shall be charged for each such permit issued for
the installation of a sewerage disposal system as defined herein. This fee
shall be made payable to the City Treasurer. (2-11-63, § 3.3)
Sec. 21-67. Inspections.
   The building inspector or his duly authorized agent shall be allowed to
inspect the work at any stage of construction, and, in any event, the applicant
for the permit shall notify the building inspector when the work is ready for
final inspection and before any underground portions are covered. (2-11-63, §
3.2)
Sec. 21-68. Septic tanks – Location.
   Septic tanks shall be located at least fifty feet (50') from any potable
water supply, well, spring or unprotected water suction line; except, that in
the case of schools, resorts, trailer parks, restaurants, taverns or other
dwellings or habitable buildings that serve the public such distance shall be
seventy-five feet (75'), except where the Michigan Department of Health
regulations require a greater distance or upon the written approval of the
building inspector or his duly authorized representative an exception is
granted. No septic tank shall be located closer than five feet (5') to any
footing or foundation wall. No septic tank shall be placed within ten feet
(10') of any lot lines or within twenty-five feet (25') of any lake, creek,
river, pond or other body of water. No septic tank shall be located where it is
inaccessible for cleaning or inspection, nor shall any structure be placed over
any septic tank rendering it inaccessible for cleaning or inspection. Cast iron
sewer shall be installed within a fifty-foot (50') radius of a private well and
within a seventy-five foot radius (75') of a public well. (2-11-63, § 4.1)
Sec. 21-69. Same – Materials and Construction Generally.
   Septic tanks shall be watertight construction and of a material not subject
to decay or corrosion when installed. Concrete blocks or bricks at least eight
inches (8") in thickness may be used in septic tank construction. Cinder blocks
shall not be approved for septic tank construction. Septic tanks shall be
provided with one (1) or more suitable openings with watertight covers to
permit cleaning and inspection. The outlet from such tank shall be constructed
so as to permit flow of liquid from the tank and to prevent the escape of
floating or settled solids. The inlet shall be designed to permit gasses to
collect above the liquid level and to pass through the inlet and out the vent
pipe serving the sewer leading into the septic tank. (2-11-63, § 4.2)
Sec. 21-70. Same – Capacity.
   Every septic tank installed after February 11, 1963 shall have a liquid
capacity of at least the average volume of sewage flowing into it during any
twenty-four- (24) hour period. In no case shall the liquid capacity of any
septic tank be less than seven hundred fifty (750) gallons. If a compartmented
tank is installed, the first compartment shall have two-thirds (2/3's) of the
total capacity.
   The following capacity for septic tanks shall be required, except where, in
the opinion of the building inspector or his duly authorized representative,
increased capacities may be required:
   One- or two- bedroom dwelling: seven hundred fifty (750) gallons; with
garbage grinder: one thousand, one hundred (1,100) gallons.
   Three-bedroom dwelling: nine hundred (900) gallons; with garbage grinder:
one thousand, three hundred, fifty (1,350) gallons.
   Four-bedroom dwelling: one thousand, one hundred (1,100) gallons; with
garbage grinder: one thousand, five hundred (1,500) gallons.
(2-11-63, § 4.3)
Sec. 21-71. Same – Dosing Tanks.
   The building inspector or his duly authorized representative may require
that dosing tanks provided with automatic siphons or pumps or a type approved
by the State Department of Health be used on installations where the liquid
capacity of the septic tank is two thousand (2,000) gallons or more. (2-11-63,
§ 4.4)
Sec. 21-72. Subsurface disposal – Generally.
   Septic tank effluent shall not be disposed of into a lake, stream,
watercourse, open ditch, county drain, storm sewer or allowed to seep on the
ground surface; but shall be disposed of in a subsurface disposal system of
design and capacity as hereinafter provided. (2-11-63, § 5.1)
Sec. 21-73. Same – Location.
   Subsurface disposal systems shall be located at least fifty feet (50') from
any potable water supply, well casing, spring structure or unprotected water
suction line, except where the State Department of Health requires a greater
distance. Such drainfields shall be located at least ten feet (10') from a lot
line, twenty-five feet (25') from any lake, pond, creek or other surface water
flooding and at least ten feet (10') from any habitable building or dwelling.
(2-11-63, § 5.2)
Sec. 21-74. Same – Headers; Distribution Boxes.
   Watertight headers shall be set true and level so as to afford an even
distribution of all septic tank effluent throughout the subsurface disposal
field. A distribution box or other approved equivalent device may be required
for installation where site conditions would not otherwise ensure proper
distribution of septic tank effluent within the allowable limits of grade and
depth of distribution lines. (2-11-63, § 5.3)
Sec. 21-75. Same – Size of Drain Tile.
   Drain tile used in a subsurface disposal system shall have a diameter of not
less than four inches (4"). (2-11-63 § 5.4)
Sec. 21-76. Same – Depth, Slope and Length of Lines; Construction of Lines.
   The top of the subsurface distribution lines shall be not less than twelve
inches (12") or more than thirty inches (30") below the finished surface grade.
   The slope of the distribution lines shall be not more than four inches per
one hundred feet (4"/100').
   The length of any one lateral line shall not exceed one hundred feet (100').
   Distribution lines shall be constructed to properly disperse all of the
septic tank effluent throughout the subsurface disposal area. Tile joints shall
be covered with building paper strips four to six inches (4-6") wide. (2-11-63,
§ 5.5)
Sec. 21-77. Same – Filter Material; Trench Construction.
   Subsurface disposal system lines for distributing septic tank effluent for
direct soil absorption shall be laid over at least four inches (4") of washed
stone from one-half to one inch (½-1") in size or an equivalent aggregate
approved by the building inspector or his duly authorized representative.
   Trenches shall be not less than eighteen inches (18") wide or more than
twenty-four inches (24") wide at the bottom. Washed stone or such other
aggregate as may be necessary to prevent the filtering of backfill material
around the lateral distribution lines shall be spread over the distribution
line to a depth of at least two inches (2"). (2-11-63, § 5.6)
Sec. 21-78. Same – Field Area; Soil Percolation Tests.
   Subsurface disposal field areas shall comply with the following minimum
trench bottom areas depending upon the average daily volume of septic tank
effluent and the type of soil in the drain area based on the following
percolation rates:
   0-5 minutes      225 square feet (ft.2) absorption area
   5-15 minutes      300-600 square feet (ft.2) absorption area
   15-30 minutes      600-750 square feet (ft.2) absorption area
   30-45 minutes      750-900 square feet (ft.2) absorption area
   45-60 minutes      900-1150 square feet (ft.2) absorption area
   Percolation rates above sixty (60) minutes indicate that the soil is
unsuitable for subsurface disposal systems.
   No subsurface disposal system hereafter installed shall contain less than
two hundred twenty-five square feet (225 ft.2) of trench bottom absorption
area. No subsurface system hereafter installed shall contain less than one
hundred fifty lineal feet (150') of field tile. The subsurface disposal field
shall contain at least one (1) lineal foot of drain tile or other approved
conduit for every two square feet (2 ft.2) of trench bottom.
   Soil percolation tests shall be required in all clay soils before minimum
drainage areas can be specified on the permit. Test holes shall be dug and
filled with water by the applicant for the permit, but notice shall be given to
the building inspector or his duly authorized representative to check the drop
in water level and record results of such test.
   When bed area absorption systems are used, the above absorption areas shall
be increased by fifty percent (50%). (2-11-63, § 5.7)
Sec. 21-79. Systems Where Subsurface Disposal is Not Suitable.
   When conditions are not suitable for installation of a subsurface disposal
field for the disposal of sewage, the building inspector or his duly authorized
representative may approve other methods safeguarding the public health. (2-11-
63, § 5.8)
Sec. 21-80. Nonconforming Systems – Declared Nuisances; Orders to Abate.
   Any private sewage disposal system existing or being maintained, which does
not conform to the requirements of this Article is hereby declared a nuisance,
dangerous and a menace to the public health. The building inspector of the City
shall order the abatement of such nuisance according to the laws of the State.
(2-11-63, § 6.1)
For Charter provisions as to nuisances and the abatement, see Char., §2.2(13).
Sec. 21-81. Same – Abatement by City and Assessment of Costs against Owner or
Occupant.
   In case the owner or occupant of any premises shall neglect or refuse to
abate such nuisance or to construct and maintain such sewage disposal system as
required by this Article, within sixty (60) days or such time as determined by
the building inspector of notice to comply therewith, the City shall cause the
work to be done at the expense of such owner or occupant. The actual cost of
such work shall constitute a lien upon the premises affected and may be
included in the taxes assessed against such premises upon the general tax roll
of the City and collected in the same manner as general City taxes. (2-11-63, §
6.2)
Sec. 21-82. Enforcement of Article.
   It shall be the duty of the building inspector to enforce strictly the
provisions of this Article. In the performance of this duty, the building
inspector or his duly authorized agent is hereby authorized to enter at any
reasonable hour any premises as may be necessary in the enforcement of this
Article. (2-11-63, § 7.1)
CHAPTER 22.
ZONING.
Editor's Note: The zoning code is available for viewing by clicking on this
link: http://www.cityoffremont.net/web/planzone.htm
Chapter 23
MEDICAL MARIHUANA
Article I. In General
§
23-1.   Definitions.
§
23-2.   Prohibition on medical marihuana dispensaries.
§
23-3.   Regulations regarding primary caregiver’s residential dwelling.
§
23-4.   Regulations regarding qualifying patients.
§
23-5.   Required compliance with federal law.
§
23-6.   General regulations.
§
23-7.   Responsibility for the premises.
                   
   Cross reference – Licensing of medical marihuana,
11-85 – 
11-87.
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 23-1. Definitions.
The following words, terms and phrases shall have the following meanings for
purposes of this article:
   (a)   “Act” means the Michigan Medical Marihuana Act, Public Act 2008,
Initiated Law 1, being M.C.L. 333.26421 et seq., as well as any and all
amendments thereto, and also any legislation enacted into law to implement that
statute.
   (b)   “Marihuana” is also known as Marijuana and Cannabis.
   (c)   “Medical Marihuana Dispensary” means any business, facility,
association, cooperative, location or operation, whether fixed or mobile, where
medical marihuana is sold, grown, processed, delivered, transmitted, dispensed,
or distributed by or to one or more of the following:
      (1)   A primary caregiver (as defined by Michigan Initiated Law I of
2008, as amended, being MCL 333.26421 et seq., as amended).
      (2)   A qualifying patient (as defined by Michigan Initiated Law I of
2008, as amended, being MCL 333.26421 et seq., as amended).
   A medical marihuana dispensary shall also include any place, location,
facility, or operation, whether fixed or mobile, where medical marihuana is
consumed on the property of a business, association, cooperative, or commercial
operation or facility or on a public or government property.
   A medical marihuana dispensary does not include the lawful dispensation of
medical marihuana by a primary caregiver personally dispensing to not more than
five (5) qualified patients (as defined by Michigan Initiated Law 1 of 2008, as
amended, being MCL 333.26421 et seq., as amended) so long as the primary
caregiver personally delivers the lawful amount of medical marihuana to the
qualifying patient where the qualifying patient resides and it is done in full
compliance with not only this article but also any other applicable City of
Fremont Ordinance or Code provision.
   (c)   “Medical Use of Marihuana” is the acquisition, possession,
cultivation, manufacture, use, delivery, transfer or transportation of
marihuana or paraphernalia relating to the administration of marihuana to treat
or alleviate a qualifying patient's debilitating medical condition or symptoms
associated with the debilitating medical condition, as defined by the Act.
   (d)   “Primary Caregiver” shall be as defined by the Act.
   (e)   “Qualifying Patient” shall be as defined by the Act.
   (f)   “Residential dwelling” shall be defined as a lawful owner-occupied,
detached single-family residential dwelling. (Ord. O-11-07, 8-15-11)
Sec. 23-2. Prohibition on Medical Marihuana Dispensaries.
   No medical marihuana dispensary shall be commenced, established, conducted,
maintained, operated or utilized anywhere within the City of Fremont or on or
from any property within the City of Fremont. (Ord. O-11-07, 8-15-11)
Sec. 23-3. Regulations Regarding Primary Caregiver’s Residential Dwelling.
   The following regulations generally pertain to the residential dwelling of a
primary caregiver:
   (a)   The primary caregiver may grow and process marihuana in compliance
with the Act within an owner-occupied, detached single-family residential
dwelling where the primary caregiver lives and is the primary caregiver’s
residence pursuant to Michigan Law. No such residential dwelling of the primary
caregiver shall be located within an apartment building, multi-family
residential building or similar housing building or development, but rather,
shall occur only within a lawful detached single-family residential dwelling.
   (b)   No person other than the primary caregiver (and no person under 18
years of age) who resides in an owner-occupied, detached single-family
residential dwelling shall be engaged or involved in the growing, processing,
dispensing, delivery, or handling of the marihuana.
   (c)   Use of the residential dwelling (which is the residence of the primary
caregiver) for medical marihuana related purposes shall be clearly incidental
and subordinate to its use for single-family residential purposes. Not more
than 25% of the gross finished floor area of the dwelling or 200 square feet of
floor area of the dwelling, whichever is less, shall be used for the growing,
processing and handling of the marihuana. No part of an accessory building,
detached garage, pole barn or similar building or structure shall be used for
the growing, processing or distribution of marihuana.
   (d)   No qualifying patient shall visit, come to or be present at the
residential dwelling of the primary caregiver to purchase, smoke, consume,
obtain or receive possession of any marihuana; rather, the primary caregiver
must personally deliver any medical marihuana to a qualifying patient at the
residence of that qualifying patient.
   (e)   No person shall deliver marihuana to a qualifying patient other than
the primary caregiver for that qualifying patient. The primary caregiver must
personally deliver the marihuana to his/her qualifying patient.
   (f)   There shall be no visible change to the outside appearance of the
primary caregiver’s residential dwelling or other visible evidence of the
conduct of the medical marihuana operation occurring inside the residential
dwelling.
   (g)   No marihuana, marihuana plants, marihuana paraphernalia or plant
growing apparatus shall be visible from the exterior of the dwelling.
   (h)   No growing, processing, smoking or use of marihuana shall occur
outdoors. All medical marihuana growing, processing and handling shall occur
entirely within the dwelling.
   (i)   No sale or distribution of merchandise or products shall be conducted
on, within or from the residential dwelling (including the lot or parcel
involved) of the primary caregiver apart from the medical marihuana itself.
Therefore, if a permit to be a medical marihuana caregiver is granted, no home
occupation will be allowed in the residential dwelling of the caregiver.
   (j)   No equipment or process shall be used in growing, processing or
handling medical marihuana, which creates noise, vibration, glare, light,
fumes, odors, or electrical interference detectable to the normal senses
outside the residential dwelling. In case of electrical interference, no
equipment or process shall be used which creates visual or audible interference
with any radio, television or similar receiver off the premises or causes
fluctuation of line voltage off the premises. The residential dwelling of the
primary caregiver shall meet all building, housing, fire and local and state
codes and ordinance requirements.
   (k)   The growing, processing, distribution, sale and handling of medical
marihuana shall comply at all times and all circumstances with the Act and any
applicable regulations or requirements by the Michigan Department of Community
Health or any other Michigan agency.
   (l)   The residential dwelling for the primary caregiver shall be located
more than 1,000 feet from any school, library or day care center as defined by
Michigan law to ensure community compliance with federal “Drug-Free School
Zone” requirements and to minimize negative impacts. The residential dwelling
for the primary caregiver shall be located more than 500 feet from any City-
owned playground/park.
   (m)   Not more than one (1) primary caregiver shall be permitted to grow,
process or handle medical marihuana at or from a given dwelling unit.
   (n)   All medical marihuana shall be contained within the primary
caregiver’s residential dwelling (except when being delivered by the primary
caregiver to a qualifying patient off site) and in an enclosed, locked facility
inaccessible on all sides and equipped with locks and other security devices
that permit access only by the registered primary caregiver. Any person under
eighteen (18) years old shall not have any access to any medical marihuana.
   (o)   No on-site consumption or smoking of marihuana is allowed within the
residential dwelling (or on the lot or parcel) of a primary caregiver except
for any medical marihuana consumption by the primary caregiver himself/herself
if he/she is a qualifying patient and in full compliance with the Act.
   (p)   No medical marihuana shall be grown, processed or handled at, from or
through the residential dwelling of the primary caregiver beyond that which is
needed or allowed by law (whichever is less) for the qualifying patients of
that particular primary caregiver.
   (q)   No sign in the form of a device, structure, fixture or placard using
graphics, symbols, and/or written copy designed specifically for the purpose of
advertising or identifying an establishment, product, service or activity and
in this case identifying the residential dwelling as being a place where
medical marihuana is grown, sold, processed, kept, or distributed shall be
visible outside of the residential dwelling or within any of the windows of the
residential dwelling. No sign or other advertising materials identifying a
particular dwelling or property as being associated with the use or cultivation
of medical marihuana or marihuana in general shall be displayed, posted or
distributed. (Ord. O-11-07, 8-15-11)
Sec. 23-4. Regulations Regarding Qualifying Patients.
   (a)   A primary caregiver is required to deliver marihuana to his/her
qualifying patients at the residence where the particular qualifying patient
resides. A qualifying patient shall not go to the residence of their primary
caregiver to purchase, obtain, smoke or consume marihuana.
   (b)   Use of marihuana by a qualifying patient shall fully comply with this
Article and the Act. (Ord. O-11-07, 8-15-11)
Sec. 23-5. Required Compliance with Federal Law.
   (a)   Nothing in this Code is intended to grant, nor shall any provisions of
this Code be construed as granting immunity from prosecution for the growing,
sale, consumption, use, smoking, distribution or possession of marihuana which
is not in strict compliance with the Act, this Code and all other applicable
laws and regulations.
   (b)   Since federal laws are not affected by the Act or this Code, nothing
in this Code is intended to grant, nor shall it be construed as granting
immunity from criminal prosecution under federal law. The Act and this Code do
not protect users, primary caregivers, qualifying patients or the owners of
properties on which medical use of marihuana is occurring from federal
prosecution or from having their property seized by federal authorities under
the Federal Controlled Substances Act, as amended. (Ord. O-11-07, 8-15-11)
Sec. 23-6. General Regulations.
   (a)   No medical marihuana shall be grown, utilized, smoked, consumed,
processed, distributed, or handled within 1,000 feet of any school, library or
day care center or within 500 feet of any City-owned playground/park.
Notwithstanding such prohibitions, a qualifying patient may possess and smoke
or consume lawful medical marihuana inside of the qualifying patient’s
residence.
   (b)   No medical marihuana shall be grown, utilized, smoked, consumed,
distributed, or handled within a dwelling or on a residential lot or parcel
within 1,000 feet of the residential dwelling of another primary caregiver.
Notwithstanding such prohibitions, a qualifying patient may possess and smoke
or consume lawful medical marihuana inside of the qualifying patient’s
residence.
   (c)   The smoking or consumption of marihuana shall not occur in any public
place.
   (d)   Every primary caregiver, qualifying patient and any other person shall
comply at all times and all circumstances with the Act and the regulations of
the Michigan Department of Community Health, as may be amended from time to
time.
   (e)   It shall be unlawful to give, sell, dispense, or otherwise distribute
medical marihuana (or any marihuana) to anyone other than a primary caregiver
or qualifying patient.
   (f)   Every primary caregiver shall maintain an accurate and complete
written record of all medical marihuana purchased, sold, distributed, or
dispensed by or through the primary caregiver which shall include, at a
minimum, all of the following:
      (1)   The identity of the primary caregiver and qualifying patient
involved in each transaction.
      (2)   The total quantity of, and amount paid for, the medical marihuana
for each transaction.
      (3)   The date, time and location of each transaction.
   (g)   All transactions and the above-required information shall be recorded
and kept in a numerical register in the order of which the transaction occurs.
All such records must be kept in the English language in a legible manner and
must be preserved and made available for inspection by the City for a period of
three (3) years after the date of the transaction.
   (h)   It is unlawful to purchase or otherwise obtain medical marihuana (or
any marihuana) from any source other than a primary caregiver who is authorized
under the Act to sell or dispense medical marihuana to that particular person.
   (i)   The City Council by resolution shall require the issuance of a City
permit by the Fremont Police Department for each medical marihuana primary
caregiver. Permit information shall be kept confidential to the extent the
Freedom of Information Act allows. There shall be an initial permit fee and an
annual permit renewal fee. The primary caregiver will be required to sign an
Affidavit of Compliance in relation to his/her adherence to not only this
Article but also any other applicable City of Fremont Ordinance or Code
provisions related to medical marihuana. (Ord. O-11-07, 8-15-11)
Sec. 23-7. Responsibility for the Premises.
   A primary caregiver shall be responsible (and shall be deemed to be in
violation of this
Chapter 23) for any violation of
Chapter 23 or the Act which occurs in the residential dwelling or lot or parcel
owned by the primary caregiver. (Ord. O-11-07, 8-15-11)
Chapter 24
FLOODPLAIN MANAGEMENT
§ 24-1.   Agency designated.
§ 24-2.   Code appendix enforced.
§ 24-3.   Designation of regulated flood prone hazard areas.
§ 24-4.   Repeals.
Sec. 24-1. Agency designated.
   Pursuant to the provisions of the state construction code, in accordance
with Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as amended, the City
Manager of the city is hereby designated as the enforcing officer to discharge
the responsibility of the city, under Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as
amended, State of Michigan. The city assumes responsibility for the
administration and enforcement of said Act throughout the corporate limits of
the community adopting this chapter.
(Ord. No. O-15-01, 1-26-15)
Sec. 24-2. Code appendix enforced.
   Pursuant to the provisions of the state construction code, in accordance
with Section 8b(6) of Act 230, of the Public Acts of 1972, as amended, Appendix
G of the Michigan Building Code shall be enforced by the enforcing agency
within the jurisdiction of the community adopting this chapter.
(Ord. No. O-15-01, 1-26-15)
Section 24-3. Designation of regulated flood prone hazard areas.
   The Federal Emergency Management Agency (FEMA) Flood Insurance Study (FIS)
Entitled "Newaygo County, Michigan (All Jurisdictions)" and dated 2/18/2015 and
the Flood Insurance Rate Map(s) (FIRMS) panel number(s) of 26123C; 0402D,
0403D, 0404D, and 0406D dated 2/18/2015 are adopted by reference for the
purposes of administration of the Michigan Construction Code, and declared to
be a part of Section 1612.3 of the Michigan Building Code, and to provide the
content of the "Flood Hazards" section of Table R301.2(1) of the Michigan
Residential Code.
(Ord. No. O-15-01, 1-26-15)
Section 24-4. Repeals.
   All ordinances inconsistent with the provisions of this chapter are hereby
repealed.
(Ord. No. O-15-01, 1-26-15)
Chapter 25
RECREATIONAL MARIHUANA
Article I. In General
§
25-1.   Prohibition of marihuana establishments.
§
25-2.   Prohibition on sale and consumption of marihuana in public places.
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
Sec. 25-1. Prohibition of marihuana establishments.
   (a)   Pursuant to the provisions of Section 6.1 of the Michigan Regulation
and Taxation of Marihuana Act (the "Act"), marihuana establishments, as defined
by the Act, are completely prohibited within the boundaries of the City of
Fremont.
   (b)   Any applicant for a state or local license to establish a marihuana
establishment, as defined by the Act, within the boundaries of the city shall
be deemed to be not in compliance with this chapter or with the Code of
Ordinances amended by the ordinance codified herein.
   (c)   This section does not supersede rights and obligations with respect to
the transportation of marihuana through the city to the extent provided by the
Act, and does not supersede rights and obligations under Michigan law and
Chapter 23 of this Code of Ordinances with respect to the establishment and
licensing of medical marihuana facilities under the Michigan Medical Marihuana
Act, the Medical Marihuana Licensing Act, 2016 PA 281, or any other law of the
State of Michigan allowing for or regulating marihuana for medical use.
(Ord. No. O-18-08, 12-3-18)
Sec. 25-2. Prohibition on sale and consumption of marihuana in public places.
   (a)    In conformance with Sec. 4.1(e) and 6.2(b) of the Act, except as
otherwise provided in this section, the sale or consumption of marihuana in any
form and the sale or display of marihuana accessories, as defined by the Act,
is prohibited in any public places within the city's boundaries.
   (b)   Any person who violates any of the provisions of this section shall be
responsible for civil and criminal penalties as set forth in Section 15 of the
State of Michigan Regulation & Taxation of Marihuana Act, 2018, as it may be
amended, but currently reads as follows:
   “Section 15: 
      A person who commits any of the following acts, and is not otherwise
authorized by this act to conduct such activities, may be punished only as
provided in this section and is not subject to any other form of punishment or
disqualification, unless the person consents to another disposition authorized
by law:
      (a)   Except for a person who engaged in conduct described in section 4
(1)(a), 4(1)(b), 4(1)(c), 4(1)(d), 4(1)(g), 4(1)(h), a person who possesses not
more than the amount of marihuana allowed by section 5, cultivates not more
than the amount of marihuana allowed by section 5, delivers without receiving
any remuneration to a person who is at least 21 years of age not more than the
amount of marihuana allowed by section 5, or possesses with intent to deliver
not more than the amount of marihuana allowed by section 5, is responsible for
a civil infraction and may be punished by a fine of not more than $100 and
forfeiture of the marihuana.
      (b)   Except for a person who is engaged in conduct described in section
4, a person who possesses not more than twice the amount of marihuana allowed
by section 5, cultivates not more than twice the amount of marihuana allowed by
section 5, delivers without receiving any remuneration to a person who is at
least 21 years of age not more than twice the amount of marihuana allowed by
section 5, or possesses with intent to deliver not more than twice the amount
of marihuana allowed by section 5:
         (1)   For a first violation, is responsible for a civil infraction and
may be punished by a fine of not more than $500 and forfeiture of the
marihuana;
         (2)   For a second violation, is responsible for a civil infraction
and may be punished by a fine of not more than $,1000 and forfeiture of the
marihuana;
         (3)   For a third or subsequent violation, is guilty of a misdemeanor
and may be punished by a fine of not more than $2,000 and forfeiture of the
marihuana.
      (c)   Except for a person who engaged in conduct described by section 4
(1)(a), 4(1)(d), or 4(1)(g), a person under 21 years of age who possesses not
more than 2.5 ounces of marihuana or who cultivates not more than 12 marihuana
plants;
         (1)   For a first violation, is responsible for a civil infraction and
may be punished as follows:
            a.   If the person is less than 18 years of age, by a fine of not
more than $100 or community service, forfeiture of the marihuana, and
completion of 4 hours of drug education or counseling; or
            b.   If the person is at least 18 years of age, by a fine of not
more than $100 and forfeiture of the marihuana.
         (2)   For a second violation, is responsible for a civil infraction
and may be punished as follows:
            a.   If the person is less than 18 years of age, by a fine of not
more than $500 or community service, forfeiture of the marihuana, and
completion of 8 hours of drug education or counseling; or
            b.   If the person is at least 18 years of age, by a fine of not
more than $500 and forfeiture of the marihuana.
      (d)   Except for a person who engaged in conduct described in section 4,
a person who possesses more than twice the amount of marihuana allowed by
section 5, cultivates more than twice the amount of marihuana allowed by
section 5, or delivers without receiving any remuneration to a person who is at
least 21 years of age more than twice the amount of marihuana allowed by
section 5, shall be responsible for a misdemeanor, but shall not be subject to
imprisonment unless the violation was habitual, willful, and for a commercial
purpose or the violation involved violence.
      (e)   This section does not supersede rights and obligations with respect
to the transfer and consumption of marihuana on private property to the extent
authorized by the person who owns, occupies or operates such property, as
provided in and authorized by the Act, and does not supersede rights and
obligations with respect to the use of marihuana for medical purposes as
provided by any law of the State of Michigan or Ordinance of the City of
Fremont allowing for or regulating marihuana for medical use.”
(Ord. No. O-18-08, 12-3-18)
